# Poudre School District — Policy Compendium

# Section A — Foundations & Basic Commitments

## AB — District Advisory Board

PURPOSE
A District Advisory Board (DAB) shall represent student and parent/guardian interests, communicating with the Board of Education and the superintendent to improve district programs and operations.

BYLAWS
The DAB must draft bylaws consistent with this policy for Board approval and review them annually.

FEEDBACK COLLECTION
The DAB solicits parent/guardian feedback on district matters and presents it to the superintendent or designee "at times and in the manner directed by the superintendent."

COMMUNICATION PROTOCOLS
Internal DAB member communications regarding district responses must be coordinated with the superintendent or designee. External communications to district/school communities must be "made by or at the direction of the superintendent or superintendent's designee."

BOARD PRESENTATION
The Board may permit the DAB to present feedback periodically at Board meetings, as determined by the Board in consultation with the superintendent.

BOARD LIAISON
The Board appoints one member as DAB liaison and an alternate, with roles including listening to feedback, communicating matters to the Board, and facilitating district response communications.

DAC RECOMMENDATIONS
The DAB may recommend DAC subcommittees, issues to be addressed, work to be conducted, and deliverables.

COMPLIANCE
The DAB remains "subject to Board of Education Policy GP 3.6."

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools appears in this policy.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY
No nondiscrimination or disability-specific provisions appear in this policy.

Adopted January 28, 2014.

## AC — Nondiscrimination/Equal Opportunity

POLICY STATEMENT
The district commits to providing safe learning and working environments treating all community members with dignity and respect, prohibiting discrimination based on protected classes including "race, color, creed, religion, national origin, ancestry, sex, sexual orientation, gender identity, gender expression, pregnancy, family composition, marital status, veteran status, age, disability, or need for special education services."

PROTECTED CLASSES
The categories listed above apply, plus genetic information for employees/applicants.

DEFINITION OF DISCRIMINATION
Discrimination occurs when individuals are "denied or limited in the ability to participate in or benefit from the District's services, activities, or opportunities on the basis of any protected class."

HARASSMENT AND DISCRIMINATION AGAINST STUDENTS
Addressed through District Policy JBB.

SEXUAL HARASSMENT (TITLE IX)
Encompasses unwelcome conduct including quid pro quo arrangements, and conduct that is severe/pervasive enough to deny equal access, and specific acts: "sexual assault, dating violence, domestic violence, or stalking."

SUPPORTIVE MEASURES
Include counseling, deadline extensions, course adjustments, schedule modifications, and contact restrictions.

RETALIATION
Means intimidating or discriminating against those reporting or participating in investigations; retaliation is prohibited.

PROHIBITED CONDUCT
Discrimination, harassment, bullying based on protected classes, and retaliation are prohibited "at any District school, at any District or school-sanctioned activity or event, on any District property, off District property when such conduct has a connection to the District."

REPORTING PROCEDURES
Students, parents, guardians, and employees may report to administrators, counselors, teachers, through online forms, or to compliance officers. "All District employees who witness harassment or discrimination must take prompt and effective action to stop the harassment or discrimination."

DISTRICT RESPONSE REQUIREMENTS
The district will: "promptly and impartially investigate allegations of harassment or discrimination"; stop confirmed incidents and take "steps to prevent it from happening again"; protect good-faith reporters from retaliation; provide investigation updates; implement supportive measures; and refer potential criminal violations to law enforcement.

CONFIDENTIALITY
"To the extent possible, all reports of harassment or discrimination will be kept confidential."

FALSE REPORTS
"Students or employees who knowingly file false complaints or give false statements in an investigation will be subject to discipline, up to and including suspension/expulsion."

COMPLIANCE OFFICERS
For students/public: Compliance, Prevention, & Response Coordinator, 2407 LaPorte Avenue, Fort Collins, CO 80521, Phone (970) 490-3333, Email nondiscrimination@psdschools.org.
For employees/applicants: Chief of Staff, 2407 LaPorte Avenue, Fort Collins, CO 80521, Phone (970) 490-3333, Email HRCompliance@psdschools.org.

NOTICE AND TRAINING
The district issues an annual written notice before each school year advising students, parents, employees, and the general public. Materials are provided in plain language and translated when possible. "Students and District employees will receive periodic training related to recognizing, reporting, and preventing discrimination and harassment."

EXTERNAL COMPLAINT OPTIONS
Complainants may alternatively file with the U.S. Department of Education Office for Civil Rights (Denver): (303) 844-5695; the federal EEOC (Denver): (303) 800-669-4000; or the Colorado Civil Rights Division: (303) 894-2997.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring systems, or predictive tools appears in this policy document.

## AC-R1 — Harassment and Discrimination Investigation Procedures for Students

OVERVIEW
The district must investigate allegations promptly and impartially, take effective action to stop harassment, remedy effects, impose discipline on offenders, protect reporters from retaliation, and maintain privacy as required by law. Criminal violations are referred to law enforcement.

REPORTING PROCESS
Any person experiencing or witnessing harassment or discrimination may report through administrators, compliance officers, or the district's online form, in writing, in person, by phone, or by email. Employees who receive information about incidents must report to supervisors, compliance officers, or via the online form.

PROTECTIONS FOR REPORTERS
The district cannot use a student's harassment report or investigation information to discipline the reporting student for: reasonable self-defense, consensual sexual activity, drug or alcohol use, late arrival/truancy, unauthorized facility access, public discussion of the alleged harassment, or expressing trauma symptoms. However, false complaints may result in discipline, and school safety measures may override these protections.

SUPPORTIVE MEASURES
The district must offer accommodations and supportive measures "designed to protect the safety of all students and that preserve and restore equal access" to education. Students need not file formal complaints or wait for investigations to receive these supports. Additional accommodations are available for students with disabilities.

INITIAL CONFERENCE
Within two school days, administrators meet with complainants to discuss supportive measures, obtain clear complaint details, and explain resolution options (informal/formal), the district's obligation to prevent recurrence, available accommodations for students with disabilities, and confidentiality limitations.

INFORMAL RESOLUTION
When both parties consent and administrators deem it suitable, matters may be resolved through mediation, counseling, or restorative practices. Informal resolution requires written consent from all student parties and cannot be used for sexual assault or violence cases. Either party may end informal processes anytime. Successful resolution requires a written report within five school days detailing the agreement and prevention steps.

FORMAL INVESTIGATION
Investigations proceed fairly, impartially, and promptly. The investigator provides written notice including "the specific section of the policy allegedly violated, and the conduct constituting the alleged violation." Both parties receive equal opportunity to present evidence, be heard, and have advisors present. Advisors may consult parties but cannot speak for them, with restrictions applied equally to both sides. Status updates are provided "at least every fifteen (15) workdays." The written investigation report must be completed within sixty calendar days, applying "the preponderance of the evidence standard, which is a determination of whether it is more likely than not that the conduct occurred."

APPEAL PROCESS
Parties may appeal within five school days on grounds of procedural irregularity affecting outcomes, new unavailable evidence, or investigator bias. The compliance officer's decision is final.

DISCIPLINE AND CONSEQUENCES
Violations may result in warnings, exclusion, progressive discipline, suspension, expulsion, transfer, or termination. Third parties may face contract cancellation or facility bans.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring systems, or predictive tools appears in this document.

RESOURCES
The policy lists crisis hotlines for domestic violence, sexual assault, and behavioral health services, plus contact information for state crisis services.

## AC-R2 — Harassment and Discrimination Investigation Procedures for Employees

POLICY OVERVIEW
Poudre School District commits to maintaining a workplace free from harassment or discrimination based on protected class status, as outlined in District Policy AC.

HARASSMENT AND DISCRIMINATION PROHIBITED
The district prohibits discrimination across all employment areas: "job advertising, pre-employment requirements, recruitment, compensation, fringe benefits, job classifications, promotion, and termination."

REPORTING REQUIREMENTS
Employees experiencing or witnessing harassment must notify their immediate supervisor, building administrator, or Human Resources Department immediately. The district commits to protecting confidentiality "to the greatest extent possible."

INVESTIGATION PROCEDURES
When complaints reach HR, investigations must be "fair, impartial, and prompt," with decisions rendered within sixty days, extendable only for documented good cause with written notice to both parties. The district applies a "preponderance of the evidence" standard—determining whether alleged conduct more likely than not occurred. Both parties receive information about investigation procedures and district legal obligations. Investigators issue written reports documenting policy violations and recommended actions, distributed simultaneously to all parties.

DISCIPLINARY MEASURES
Substantiated violations result in discipline ranging from verbal warnings to dismissal, potentially including mandatory harassment education programs.

RETALIATION PROHIBITION
The policy strictly prohibits retaliation, stating good faith reporting "will not reflect upon an employee's status or affect future employment or work assignments and/or promotions."

RECORD KEEPING AND CONFIDENTIALITY
Complaint records remain confidential personnel files, exempt from public disclosure under Colorado law, except as specified in statutory exceptions.

OUTSIDE REMEDIES
Employees may file complaints with external agencies listed in Policy AC.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring tools, or predictive technologies in any investigation or disciplinary procedures.

## AC-R3 — Sexual Harassment Investigation Procedures

CORE COMMITMENT
The district maintains commitment to "a safe, nondiscriminatory learning and working environment" free from sexual harassment and retaliation, complying with Title IX.

KEY DEFINITIONS
Complainant: individual alleged to be a harassment victim. Consent: defined by Colorado law as "cooperation in act or attitude pursuant to an exercise of free will" with knowledge of the act; conduct of a sexual nature by employees toward students is "presumed to be unwelcome and nonconsensual." Decision-Maker: trained individual assessing evidence using preponderance standard; cannot be Title IX Coordinator or investigator. Respondent: reported perpetrator of alleged sexual harassment.

TITLE IX COORDINATOR
District compliance employee located at 2407 LaPorte Avenue, Fort Collins, Colorado 80521, Phone (970) 490-3333, Email nondiscrimination@psdschools.org.

REPORTING PROCEDURES
Reports may be submitted via online form, in person, mail, telephone, or email. The Title IX Coordinator "must promptly contact the complainant to discuss the availability of supportive measures."

FORMAL COMPLAINT FILING
Complaints must be filed in writing and signed by the complainant or Title IX Coordinator.

DISMISSAL CRITERIA
The Title IX Coordinator may dismiss complaints if: conduct occurred outside the education program or activity; conduct did not occur in the United States; complainant requests withdrawal in writing; respondent is no longer enrolled or employed; or insufficient evidence gathering is possible.

INVESTIGATION PROCESS
The investigator begins "in a reasonably prompt manner." "The respondent is not responsible for the alleged conduct during the course of the investigation" (presumption of non-responsibility). No investigation of complainant's prior sexual history is permitted; parties receive equal opportunity to present witnesses. Parties receive gathered evidence and have "10 days to submit a written response" before the investigative report is finalized. The investigator waits "10 days before providing the report to the decision-maker."

DECISION STANDARDS
The decision-maker applies "the preponderance of the evidence standard" and provides a written determination with reasoning and recommended disciplinary measures simultaneously to both parties.

APPEAL PROCESS
Appeals must be filed within "10 days" on grounds of procedural irregularity affecting outcome, new unavailable evidence that could affect outcome, or conflict of interest or bias by officials. The appeal decision-maker cannot be the original decision-maker, investigator, or Title IX Coordinator.

INFORMAL RESOLUTION
Available at any time before a decision if both parties voluntarily consent in writing. This option excludes cases involving employee-to-student sexual harassment allegations.

DISABILITY / NONDISCRIMINATION CONTENT
Emergency removal of respondents must comply with "the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, Section 504 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973, and the Americans with Disabilities Act, as applicable." The district does not discriminate on the basis of sex "in its educational programs, activities, operations, and employment decisions."

NOTICE AND TRAINING
The district provides periodic employee training; procedures are prominently posted on the website and referenced in the Student Rights & Code of Conduct.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, or predictive tools are mentioned.

Adopted May 1, 2025.

## ACE — Nondiscrimination on the Basis of Disability

POLICY OVERVIEW
The district commits to nondiscrimination under Section 504 of the Rehabilitation Act and the Americans with Disabilities Act, ensuring "no qualified individual with a disability shall...be excluded from participation in" district programs.

STUDENT NONDISCRIMINATION
The district provides a free, appropriate public education without discriminating based on disability, including exclusion from curricular or extracurricular activities.

EMPLOYMENT NONDISCRIMINATION
The district prohibits discrimination in recruitment, hiring, advancement, and termination. The district must "make reasonable accommodations to the known physical or mental limitations" of qualified employees unless accommodation creates undue hardship or modifies essential job functions.

PUBLIC AND PARENT ACCOMMODATIONS
The district provides reasonable accommodations for public members and parents/guardians to participate in school programs, conferences, IEP meetings, and Section 504 meetings.

SECTION 504/ADA COORDINATORS
Students/public: Director of Student Services, 1630 South Stover Street, Fort Collins, CO 80525, (970) 490-3033.
Employees: Executive Director of Human Resources, 2407 LaPorte Avenue, Fort Collins, CO 80521, (970) 490-3620.
Coordinators ensure compliance, formulate procedures, investigate complaints, and monitor district operations.

NO RETALIATION
The district prohibits retaliation against individuals exercising Section 504/ADA rights or participating in complaint resolution.

GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE — STEP 1 FILING
Complainants submit Form AC-E to their school principal, department director, or supervisor within 90 calendar days of alleged discrimination. Oral submissions are permitted if the complainant cannot complete the form due to disability. If discrimination is alleged against the principal/director or a coordinator, the form goes directly to the appropriate coordinator.

GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE — STEP 2 INVESTIGATION
The coordinator's designee conducts an impartial investigation, meets with all parties, and issues a written determination within 30 calendar days, distributed to the complainant, accused party, superintendent's cabinet member, and coordinator.

GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE — STEP 3 APPEAL
Dissatisfied complainants may appeal the Step 2 determination to the coordinator within 10 calendar days, in writing or orally if the complainant has a disability or legitimate reason.

GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE — STEP 4 COORDINATOR REVIEW
The coordinator reviews the appeal, conducts further investigation if necessary, and issues a written decision within 30 calendar days to the complainant, accused party, and cabinet member.

GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE — STEP 5 FURTHER ACTION
Complainants unsatisfied with Step 4 may pursue any legal remedy authorized by law.

IMPARTIAL DUE PROCESS HEARING
Parents/guardians or students (18+) may request a hearing from the Director of Student Services to resolve complaints regarding a student's Section 504 identification, evaluation, or educational placement. The request must specify each issue and remedy sought, filed no later than five months after the alleged discrimination. Both parties may be represented by legal counsel (parties pay their own costs); legal counsel notification must occur at time of request; the district must notify the complainant within three business days if represented; an independent, Section 504/ADA-knowledgeable hearing officer is retained; the hearing is scheduled within 30 calendar days or as soon as reasonably practicable; the hearing is recorded, and parties may present witnesses, documents, and evidence.

DECISION STANDARDS
The hearing officer issues a written decision within 10 business days, addressing all submitted issues, confined to Section 504 identification/evaluation/placement matters, based solely on hearing evidence, including summary and reasoning. Decisions are provided to all parties and cannot assess or award attorney fees. Either party may seek court review within 30 calendar days of the decision.

EXTERNAL COMPLAINT OPTIONS
Complaints may be filed with the U.S. Department of Education, Office for Civil Rights: Cesar E. Chavez Memorial Building, 1244 Speer Boulevard, Suite 310, Denver, CO 80204; (303) 844-5695; TDD (877) 521-2172; OCR.Denver@ed.gov.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools appears in this policy document.

## ADC — Tobacco-Free and Marijuana-Free District

SCOPE OF PROHIBITION
The district prohibits "use of any tobacco product and use of marijuana by students, staff and members of the public" on all district property, as well as at "all District or school-sanctioned activities or events off District property."

POSSESSION RESTRICTIONS
Marijuana possession is banned for all persons on district grounds; tobacco possession is restricted for students only.

DISCIPLINARY CONSEQUENCES
Students violating tobacco policies face measures including "revocation of privileges, exclusion from extracurricular activities, detention and, for repeated violations, suspension or expulsion." Marijuana violations trigger consequences outlined in separate Policy JICH.

MEDICAL MARIJUANA EXCEPTION
"Primary caregivers are permitted to administer medical marijuana in a nonsmokeable form to students" under Policy JLCD.

ENFORCEMENT FOR OTHERS
Employees face "appropriate disciplinary action"; members of the public "may be requested to leave" district property.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No references to algorithms, AI, machine learning, or predictive scoring tools.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY / ACCOUNTABILITY
No nondiscrimination, disability-related, or accountability/appeals provisions appear in this document.

Originally adopted August 1994; most recently revised June 12, 2018.

## ADF — Student and Employee Wellness

POLICY OVERVIEW
The district implements "a coordinated approach to promote healthy schools through a culture of wellness" that encompasses physical, mental, emotional, and social health dimensions.

GOVERNANCE STRUCTURE
The district established the Wellness Advisory Council for Schools (WACS), comprising "students, parents, community partners, administrators, physical education teachers and other District employees." The council supports policy implementation under district wellness coordinator direction.

REVIEW AND COMPLIANCE
District administration conducts annual policy reviews with WACS collaboration to "develop or revise the plan for implementing the policy," ensuring compliance with the Healthy, Hunger-Free Kids Act of 2010. Compliance results "shall be available to the public."

COMPREHENSIVE WELLNESS EDUCATION
The district provides "standards-based health education, nutrition education in the cafeteria and integration of wellness teams" to develop lifelong wellness behaviors.

NUTRITION STANDARDS
"School meals, as well as other foods and beverages available on school grounds," must "align with District standards and current U.S. Dietary Guidelines" and meet state/local health department guidelines.

PHYSICAL EDUCATION AND ACTIVITY
Schools provide "standards-based physical education programs, and multiple opportunities to engage in movement," including co-curricular activities and recess.

EMPLOYEE WELLNESS
The district provides "integrated and comprehensive wellness opportunities for staff."

MENTAL HEALTH SERVICES
The district delivers "prevention, early intervention, crisis intervention and recovery, and mental health support" through school-based programs and community collaboration.

HEALTH SERVICES
The district ensures "adequate resources for students' overall health," including health plans, screenings, and community resource access.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No references to algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring systems, or predictive tools.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY
No specific nondiscrimination or disability accommodation provisions within this policy's text.

Originally adopted May 8, 2006; revised March 22, 2010; May 5, 2014; June 12, 2017.

## ADF-R — Student and Employee Wellness

COMPREHENSIVE LEARNING ENVIRONMENT
The district maintains programs integrating "wellness components and health standards into curricula" with evidence-based practices. Schools develop wellness teams operating under the Whole School, Whole Community, Whole Child model to create yearly School Health Improvement Plans.

NUTRITION EDUCATION AND FOOD ACCESS
Implementation follows National School Lunch/Breakfast Program USDA guidelines. Districts provide "accessible and easily understood information" about nutritional content and allergens. Beverages must meet USDA/Colorado State Board standards during regular and extended school days. 50% of food options should comprise "fruits, vegetables and non-sugared sweetened beverages." Minimum eating time: 10 minutes breakfast, 20 minutes lunch. Safe snack provisions address "students with food allergies and other dietary restrictions." Non-food based incentives are encouraged for student recognition. Students must have access to "functioning water fountains" and hand sanitizing facilities.

PHYSICAL ACTIVITY
Physical education complies with Colorado state standards. PE teachers must be "properly endorsed and highly qualified." Districts discourage "withholding of physical activity as a consequence for student misconduct."

EMPLOYEE WELLNESS
Districts designate wellness champions and provide opportunities for nutrition, physical activity, and mental health resources, including worksite screenings and Employee Assistance Services.

MENTAL HEALTH SUPPORT
Employees receive suicide prevention training. School counselors provide social/emotional learning opportunities. Mental health teams collaborate on early identification and crisis support. Strong relationships with community agencies are emphasized.

OVERALL HEALTH SERVICES
School nurses provide recommendations for healthy weight maintenance. Preventative screenings for vision and hearing are encouraged. Compliance is required with policies on allergies, medication, and health issues.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring systems, or predictive tools.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY
The policy addresses accommodation of "students with food allergies and other dietary restrictions" but contains no comprehensive nondiscrimination clause or detailed disability provisions.

ACCOUNTABILITY
Limited formal accountability mechanisms are specified beyond team creation and plan development requirements.

Adopted May 8, 2006; revised June 12, 2017.

## ADFA — Communicable Diseases

GENERAL PROVISIONS
Poudre School District must report suspected or confirmed communicable diseases to the Colorado Department of Public Health and Environment or local public health agencies "as soon as possible." District employees aware of such diseases must "immediately notify a responsible District official," who reports to public health authorities. Responsible officials include principals, school nurses, and the district health coordinator. The district "may temporarily prohibit the attendance of students and/or employees" to mitigate transmission risks affecting health and safety. Volunteers are treated as employees under this policy.

CONFIDENTIALITY
Information about student and employee communicable disease status must comply with FERPA, HIPAA, the Colorado Open Records Act, and applicable laws. Such information should "only be shared with those persons who have a need to know based upon their legitimate educational, supervisory and/or healthcare responsibilities." Confidentiality protections extend after individuals leave the district.

EMPLOYEE TRAINING AND INFORMATION
The health coordinator shall develop trainings helping employees recognize disease symptoms, exclude affected individuals, provide notices, and take required actions per CDPHE and public health agencies.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
None mentioned.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY
The policy cross-references "ACE, Nondiscrimination on the Basis of Disability" but contains no substantive disability provisions in the main text.

ACCOUNTABILITY
Minimal accountability provisions; the policy emphasizes reporting obligations to external health agencies.

## ADG — Animals in District Facilities and Vehicles

SERVICE ANIMALS — CORE RIGHT AND DEFINITION
Students, employees, and others with disabilities may be accompanied by "service animals" in district schools, facilities, and vehicles. The policy defines service animals as "dogs individually trained to do work or perform tasks required for the benefit of a person with a disability" that are directly related to that person's disability. Miniature horses may qualify under certain conditions. The policy explicitly excludes emotional support animals: "crime deterrent effects...nor the provision of emotional support, wellbeing, comfort or companionship constitute work or tasks."

PERMISSIBLE INQUIRIES
District officials may ask only two questions: "(a) Is the animal required because of a disability? (b) What work or task has the animal been trained to perform?" Officials cannot inquire about the nature or extent of disability.

NOTICE AND VACCINATIONS
Users must provide "at least ten (10) working days' advance written notice" to the Section 504/ADA Compliance Officer. All service animals must have current vaccinations.

CONTROL REQUIREMENTS
Service animals must be "under the control of their handlers" via harness, leash, or tether, with exceptions where the handler has a disability preventing such use or control would interfere with task performance. On vehicles, animals must remain "near the individual they are accompanying and out of the aisle."

EXCLUSION GROUNDS
Service animals may be excluded if: (a) presence would "fundamentally alter" district services; (b) the animal poses "significant risk to the health or safety of others" that cannot be eliminated; (c) the animal is not under handler control; or (d) the animal is not housebroken.

LIABILITY AND CARE
"The owner...and the person having control or custody...are liable for any damage to persons, premises, facilities, or vehicles." The district assumes no responsibility for animal care.

COMPLIANCE OFFICER ROLE
The Section 504/ADA Compliance Officer handles reasonable accommodation determinations, risk assessments, policy modifications, and care-related issues.

ANIMALS AT SCHOOL FOR EDUCATIONAL PURPOSES — PERMISSION AND PURPOSE
Animals may be brought to school only "after receiving permission from the building principal, only for a specific and appropriate educational purpose and only for the amount of time necessary to achieve the educational goal." Poisonous animals are prohibited.

TEACHER QUALIFICATIONS AND ANIMAL CONDITION
Teachers must be "familiar with the appropriate care, feeding and handling" and potential dangers. Animals must be "in good physical condition and, where appropriate, vaccinated against transmittable diseases." Allergies must be considered.

CONTROL AND SAFETY
Teachers are responsible for animal control and student/staff safety. "No animals shall be allowed to run freely anywhere in the school building."

CARE ON NON-SCHOOL DAYS
Teachers must arrange appropriate care when animals remain during closed days, maintaining sanitary conditions with food and water.

HEALTH PROTOCOLS
Students cannot eat or drink during animal activities. "Immediately after handling any animal, all students shall be required to thoroughly wash their hands with soap and water with adult supervision."

INCIDENT REPORTING
The principal must be notified of bites, scratches, or incidents affecting "physical or emotional health." Teachers must complete written reports and contact parents/guardians if students are involved.

TRANSPORTATION
Animals cannot be transported on buses except as expressly permitted by law or district policy.

DISABILITY / NONDISCRIMINATION CONTENT
This policy explicitly addresses disability accommodation through service animal provisions, implementing federal ADA requirements (28 C.F.R. 35.104, 35.136 & 35.139).

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No automated systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools are mentioned.

## AE — District and School Accountability

OVERVIEW
The policy establishes District Accountability Committees (DAC) and School Accountability Committees (SAC) pursuant to the Education Accountability Act of 2009.

DISTRICT ACCOUNTABILITY COMMITTEE MEMBERSHIP
Sixteen voting members representing: students with disabilities, gifted/talented students, charter school students, English language learners, ethnic minority students, early childhood program students, elementary/middle/high school students, business/industry representatives, administrators, teachers, and classified employees. Additional non-voting ex officio members include a charter school-knowledgeable administrator (co-chair) and a Parent Engagement Liaison.

DISTRICT ACCOUNTABILITY COMMITTEE MEETINGS
"At least once each month during the school year"; open to the public with posted notices.

DISTRICT ACCOUNTABILITY COMMITTEE KEY DUTIES
Develop budget spending recommendations by December 15; submit written recommendations on district performance/improvement/turnaround plans; review charter school applications; increase parent engagement, particularly for underrepresented populations; study additional areas as determined annually with the Board and superintendent.

SCHOOL ACCOUNTABILITY COMMITTEE MEMBERSHIP
Principal, teachers, at least three parents/guardians, a PTO/PTA representative, and a community business representative. "The Board's intent is that no maximum shall be imposed on the number of parents/guardians."

SCHOOL ACCOUNTABILITY COMMITTEE MEETINGS
"At least four times each school year"; open to the public.

SCHOOL ACCOUNTABILITY COMMITTEE KEY DUTIES
Recommend school spending priorities; advise on school performance/improvement/turnaround plans; quarterly discussion of plan implementation; provide input on principal development and evaluation; increase parent engagement.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, predictive tools, or scoring systems.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY
References to students with disabilities and various underrepresented populations appear throughout membership and engagement provisions.

# Section C — General School Administration

## CA — District Governance

GOVERNANCE STRUCTURE
Poudre School District R-1 operates under policy governance with Board of Education oversight and superintendent leadership. The district's governance framework includes District Ends (DE), Executive Limitation (EL), Governance Process (GP), and Board-Superintendent Relationship (BSR) policies.

COMPLIANCE FRAMEWORK
"District employees shall comply with applicable federal, state and local laws in connection with their work" and must ensure operations align with such legal requirements. Employees must also follow Board policies, employee association agreements, district policies, regulations, and supervisor directives.

ADMINISTRATIVE GUIDELINES AUTHORITY
Superintendents, assistant superintendents, executive directors, directors, coordinators, and principals may establish administrative guidelines implementing laws and policies to facilitate operations and manage personnel and volunteers.

SUPERVISOR DIRECTIVE AUTHORITY
Supervisors may issue directives consistent with laws, policies, and procedures. "Superintendent, assistant superintendents and executive directors may issue directives that override administrative guidelines."

DISCIPLINE FOR NON-COMPLIANCE
"District employees who fail or refuse to comply...shall be subject to discipline up to and including termination of employment."

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mentions of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring systems, or predictive tools appear in this policy.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY / ACCOUNTABILITY
No nondiscrimination, disability accommodation, or accountability provisions are included in this governance policy.

Adopted July 14, 2009; revised January 19, 2015.

## CF — School Building Administration

PRINCIPAL AUTHORITY
"Principals shall act as the chief administrative officers of their schools. They shall be responsible for and shall have authority over the actions of their students, employees, and visitors."

EDUCATIONAL OBJECTIVES
Principals must work toward achieving both long- and short-range educational goals for the district, overseeing students and staff within their buildings.

PROGRAM MANAGEMENT
Principals oversee the district's standards-based education program while adhering to applicable laws, district policies, administrative guidelines, and supervisor directives. They must "rigorously monitor and modify the program to best enable students to meet or exceed District and state standards."

RULEMAKING AUTHORITY
"Principals shall have the authority to make school rules consistent with District policies and regulations that are deemed necessary to ensure the opportunity for students to take full advantage of the educational experiences provided."

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No references to algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring systems, or predictive tools.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY / ACCOUNTABILITY
The document lacks explicit nondiscrimination language, disability accommodations, or accountability mechanisms.

Originally adopted April 1972; most recently revised July 2009.

## CFD — Site-based School Management

CORE POLICY STATEMENT
The Poudre School District endorses site-based management practices, granting principals decision-making authority subject to specified constraints and oversight mechanisms.

AUTHORITY AND CONSTRAINTS
Principals may make decisions provided actions comply with: governing law, Board policies, District policies/regulations, superintendent directives, District contracts, and budgetary limits. "Principals and other school-based personnel may make hiring recommendations, but shall have no authority to hire employees."

STAKEHOLDER INPUT
Principals determine whether stakeholder consultation is necessary, exercising discretion regarding input from staff, students, parents, or community members. This discretionary authority "is not intended to supplant the leadership duties and responsibilities of the principal."

ACCOUNTABILITY
Principals bear full accountability for implementation and results of site-based decisions, including compliance with all applicable constraints.

VARIANCE REQUESTS
Schools seeking exceptions must submit written requests through supervisory channels to the superintendent's cabinet for evaluation.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring mechanisms, or predictive tools.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY
No explicit nondiscrimination, disability access, or detailed accountability reporting provisions beyond the School Accountability Committee requirement referenced in the policy.

## CH — Procedures for Superintendent Policies

TITLE
CH - Procedures for Creating, Revising and Deleting Superintendent Policies and Regulations.

ADVANCE SUBMISSION TO CABINET
Draft policies must reach Cabinet members with adequate lead time for review and stakeholder feedback collection from affected District employees and community members.

CABINET CONSIDERATION
The Cabinet considers drafts at meetings, either approving them or requesting revisions. This cycle repeats until approval is achieved.

SUPERINTENDENT AUTHORIZATION
The superintendent initials and dates the final version; the assistant to the superintendent/board secretary maintains a copy.

WEBSITE POSTING
"Legal and policy counsel or his/her designee shall ensure that the District website properly reflects the adopted new, revised or deleted policy/regulation," with creation/revision dates matching the superintendent's initials.

BOARD NOTIFICATION
Adopted policies are provided to the Board as informational items only.

IMPLEMENTATION COMMUNICATION
The superintendent consults with Cabinet to assign administrators for communicating policies to affected stakeholders and implementers.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention of algorithms, AI, machine learning, or automated decision-making systems.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY / ACCOUNTABILITY
No explicit nondiscrimination, disability access, or accountability provisions appear in this procedural document.

Adopted October 16, 2006; revised December 10, 2012.

## CL — Research Involving District Students, Employees or Resources

DEFINITION OF RESEARCH
Research is defined as "a systematic investigation or inquiry (including but not limited to evaluations and/or the analysis of existing data)" but excludes direct classroom assessments.

AUTHORIZATION REQUIREMENTS
Research involving district participants requires one of four authorizations: a legal mandate, superintendent approval for third-party research, superintendent/designee approval for district research, or principal approval for single-school research. The policy mandates minimizing "interference with student and employee participation in regular District curricular and extracurricular programs/activities."

DISTRICT RESEARCH REQUIREMENTS
District research must be conducted by district officials, typically supervised by the director of research and evaluation or school principals, depending on scope.

THIRD-PARTY RESEARCH REQUIREMENTS
Third parties must submit written proposals identifying all associated entities, personnel, research methods, and anticipated publications.

CONSENT REQUIREMENTS
Parents/guardians (or students age 18+) must provide "informed written consent for the research involving the student," including disclosure of personally identifiable information from education records.

CONTRACT REQUIREMENT
"Authorization of all third-party research involving District students, employees or resources shall be conditioned on the execution of a written contract." Publication restrictions prohibit identifying the district or students without superintendent authorization and advance written consent.

TERMINATION AUTHORITY
The superintendent may suspend or terminate research "at any time" for contract violations.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI / DATA ANALYTICS
The policy text obtained contains no specific provisions expressly naming automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, predictive analytics, or algorithmic scoring tools in the research-approval or data-handling process; its data protections are instead framed generally around personally identifiable information from education records, informed written consent, and confidentiality/contract obligations under the general "analysis of existing data" language in the research definition.

Adopted September 28, 2015.

# Section D — Fiscal Management

## DB — Annual Budget

Adopted May 22, 1995; revised August 11, 1997.

PURPOSE
The annual budget serves as the financial plan for school system operations, establishing the framework for both expenditures and revenues for the year.

REGULATORY FRAMEWORK
Public school budgeting is governed by state statutes and State Board of Education requirements regarding district budget forms, maintained to ensure statewide uniformity.

PRESENTATION REQUIREMENTS
Budgets must be presented in a summary format understandable by any lay person reviewing the District's budget. The format shall itemize expenditures by fund and by student, describing expenditures with amounts for both the current and ensuing fiscal years. Budgets must disclose planned compliance with Colorado Constitution article X, section 20 (TABOR).

LEADERSHIP RESPONSIBILITY
The Board assigns the superintendent overall responsibility for budget preparation, presentation, and administration, with authority to delegate tasks to the budget manager.

SUFFICIENCY STANDARD
The adopted budget should be adequate to implement all Board-approved programs and policies.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-44-101 through 22-44-117; C.R.S. 29-1-103(3) (lease-purchase payment obligations).

CROSS REFERENCES
DB subcodes (budget-related policies); State Board of Education Financial Policies and Procedures Handbook.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, predictive tools, or software/technology vendor terms was found in this policy.

## DBAA — General Fund Balances

Adopted March 26, 2013; revised June 10, 2014.

POLICY OBJECTIVE
The district aims to maintain appropriate fund balances within the General Fund to maximize resources while complying with governing law, mitigating financial risk, and ensuring financial stability.

FUND BALANCE CATEGORIES (GASB STATEMENT NO. 54)
Nonspendable: amounts unable to be spent due to form or legal requirements (e.g., inventories, endowment principal).
Restricted: amounts spent only for specific purposes stipulated by the constitution or external resource providers.
Committed: amounts designated by formal Board action prior to fiscal year end (June 30); actual amounts may be determined later.
Assigned: amounts intended to be used by the District for specific purposes without meeting restricted/committed criteria; the superintendent or designee may assign funds.
Unassigned: the residual fund category comprising all spendable amounts not in other categories; may be used for any legal purpose.

FUND BALANCE USAGE PRIORITY
Restricted funds are spent first when applicable. Among unrestricted categories, committed funds are used before assigned, and assigned before unassigned. Within unassigned balances, reserves precede contingency reserves.

RESERVE REQUIREMENTS
The district shall strive to maintain a reserve amount between 3% and 5% of each fiscal year's expenditures. If reserves fall below 3%, shortages must be replenished within one year (for shortfalls of 0-1%) or two years (for shortfalls of 1-3%) through expenditure cuts or revenue increases. Excess reserves exceeding 5% may fund nonrecurring expenditures that require no future maintenance costs.

IMPLEMENTATION AND REVIEW
The Financial Services Department develops implementation guidelines and conducts annual policy reviews with recommendations to the Board.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-44-101 to -304.

CROSS REFERENCES
DB (Annual Budget); DBG (Budget Adoption).

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, predictive tools, or software/technology vendor terms was found in this policy.

## DDA — Federal Procurement and Fiscal Requirements

Adopted September 11, 2017; revised December 8, 2020; revised May 13, 2025 (effective July 1, 2025).

SCOPE
This policy governs purchases of services, supplies, equipment, and property using federal funds, and District employees compensated with federal funds. It applies to transactions subject to the Uniform Grant Guidance (UGG), EDGAR, and USDA regulations for school food service programs.

KEY PROCUREMENT THRESHOLDS
Micro-purchases: under $10,000.
Small purchases: $10,000 to $100,000.
Large purchases: $100,000 or more.

CONFLICT OF INTEREST STANDARDS
Board members and employees may not participate in selecting, awarding, or administering federally funded contracts when they have a real or apparent conflict of interest. A conflict arises when the individual, an immediate family member, a partner, or their employer has a financial or other interest in, or a tangible personal benefit from, the contracting entity.

PROHIBITED CONDUCT
Covered individuals may not solicit or accept gratuities, favors, or anything of monetary value from contractors, except unsolicited items of nominal value consistent with state law standards.

RECORD RETENTION
The District must maintain procurement records including the rationale for the method of procurement, the basis for contractor selection or rejection, and the basis for the contract price.

TECHNOLOGY / AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
This policy contains no mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, or predictive technologies.

## DEBA — Incentive Payments to Taxpayers

Adopted August 1994; reviewed August 11, 1997.

POLICY OVERVIEW
The Board of Education possesses statutory authority to negotiate incentive payments with taxpayers establishing new business facilities or expanding existing ones within school district boundaries.

CASE-BY-CASE CONSIDERATION
The Board shall evaluate tax incentive agreements or credits individually, limited to new or expanded business facilities as defined by state law.

FUNDING PROTECTION
Any negotiated incentive arrangement shall not have a negative impact on existing funding for the district.

AGREEMENT DURATION
Incentive agreements cannot exceed a four-year term.

ADMINISTRATIVE GUIDANCE
Accompanying regulations (DEBA-R) provide direction for district administration and taxpayers seeking incentive negotiations.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-32-110(1)(ff) and (gg); C.R.S. 30-11-123(5); C.R.S. 31-15-903(4); C.R.S. 39-22-508.2(2)(a), (3).

TECHNOLOGY / AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, or software vendor terms appears in this policy.

## DEBA-R — Incentive Payments to Taxpayers (Regulation)

Adopted August 1994; reviewed December 1997.

FISCAL IMPACT ANALYSIS REQUIREMENT
The superintendent or designee and administration must conduct a fiscal impact analysis prior to negotiating with any taxpayer establishing a new facility or expanding an existing one, to determine how incentive payments or credits will affect the district.

NOTIFICATION REQUIREMENT
Poudre School District will notify Larimer County and the City of Fort Collins of its intent to enter into negotiations with taxpayers establishing or expanding facilities.

DETERMINATION OF QUALIFICATION
The superintendent or designee must determine that the taxpayer has established a new business facility or expanded an existing facility meeting state law definitions. The superintendent may rely on city and county agreements but retains authority to require independent documentation to verify statutory compliance.

NEGOTIATION AUTHORITY
The superintendent or designee may negotiate incentive payments, subject to Board approval.

PAYMENT LIMITATION CAP
No annual incentive payment shall exceed 50 percent of taxes levied on: (a) taxable personal property at the new facility used in operations for the current tax year, or (b) taxable personal property directly attributable to expansion within the expanded facility for the current tax year.

STATE LAW COMPLIANCE
Agreements require approval as mandated by state law.

NOTIFICATION OF NEGOTIATIONS
The superintendent or designee must inform Larimer County and the City of Fort Collins regarding all negotiations.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, predictive tools, or software/technology vendor terms was found in this policy.

## DFA-DFAA — Revenues from Investment/Use of Surplus Funds

Adopted April 1972; revised April 1977, May 1982, April 1988, August 1994, May 22, 1995, August 11, 1997, October 14, 2002, June 28, 2004, February 28, 2012.

SCOPE
This policy applies to all Poudre School District financial assets and funds over which the District exercises control, as documented in the Comprehensive Annual Financial Report.

INVESTMENT OBJECTIVES
District funds not immediately needed shall be invested by Board-authorized individuals to accomplish four primary goals: (1) compliance with governing law and Board direction; (2) protection of financial assets; (3) maintaining liquidity for timely obligation payment; and (4) earning a competitive market rate of return from legally permitted investments while respecting risk constraints and cash flow needs.

INVESTMENT PRINCIPLES
Diversification: investments must be sufficiently diverse to protect against the risk of loss from over-concentration in specific maturities, issues, classes, or institutions.
Liquidity: investments must remain sufficiently liquid to allow continuity of the District's fiscal operations without emergency borrowing. The controller shall maintain updated cash-flow projections.
Pooling: all unrestricted moneys may be pooled into a single investment account with separate accounting. Income distribution follows governing law as determined by the executive director of finance or Board direction.

AUTHORITY AND RESPONSIBILITIES
Executive Director of Finance: holds overall responsibility for District investment decisions and transactions, including wire and electronic fund transfers. This individual also serves as Board Treasurer and shall consult independent investment advisors as needed.
Authorized Personnel: beyond the executive director of finance, the following employees may make investment decisions and conduct transactions: controller; primary accountant (designated in writing by executive director); backup accountant (designated in writing by executive director). Primary and backup accountants must be reported to the Board at the beginning of the fiscal year and whenever changed.
Broker/Dealer Standards: authorized broker/dealers must maintain a minimum net capital of $10,000,000 and a ten-year history of services to governmental entities. The executive director and investment advisors maintain lists of eligible brokers with current financial statements.

EMPLOYEE CONDUCT AND FIDUCIARY DUTIES
Employees must operate under Colorado law's fiduciary standard, exercising the judgment and care under the circumstances then prevailing that persons of prudence, discretion and intelligence exercise in the management of the property of another.
Prohibited Activities: employees shall avoid personal business activity conflicting with proper investment program execution or impairing impartial decision-making.
Disclosure Requirements: employees must disclose to the executive director, superintendent, and Board any material financial interests in financial institutions conducting District business or under consideration, plus personal financial positions potentially affected by portfolio performance.
Bonding and Insurance: investment decision-makers must be bonded, with District insurance against their misfeasance.
Training: all authorized employees shall receive education and training necessary to ensure their proficiency as fiduciaries.

INTERNAL CONTROLS
The District maintains controls including: (1) written documentation of all transactions; (2) at least two authorized employees, as designated in this policy, signing off in advance on investments; and (3) periodic internal auditor review. The executive director shall ensure annual policy review with revisions submitted to the Board.

REPORTING AND ACCOUNTABILITY
Accounting Standards: investments follow generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP) and Governmental Accounting Standards Board standards, included in annual external audits.
Monthly Reports: the controller prepares performance statements showing earnings and rate of return for each investment in the current month and for the term of each investment to date.
Public Posting: annual audits and monthly reports are posted online and maintained in fiscal records.
Board Notification: the Board receives investment, earnings, and rate-of-return updates on no less than a quarterly basis.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 11-10.5-101 et seq.; 11-47-101 et seq.; 11-60-101 et seq.; 15-1-304; 22-32-107; 22-40-105; 24-75-601 et seq.; 24-75-701 et seq.

CROSS REFERENCES
DG (Depository of Funds); DH (Bonded Employees and Officers); GBEA (Staff Ethics/Conflict of Interest).

No automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, or predictive tools are mentioned in this policy.

## DFDA — Free Admissions

Adopted December 9, 1996; revised January 28, 2002.

LIFETIME ACTIVITY PASS PROGRAM
The Poudre School District establishes a lifetime activity pass program with the following eligibility categories.

MANDATORY ELIGIBILITY
Retired district employees meeting 20 years of continuous district employment; Board of Education members who have completed two terms in office; residents aged 65 and older (upon request).

DISCRETIONARY ELIGIBILITY
The Board retains authority to grant a lifetime pass to any person who has made a significant contribution to Poudre School District, at its discretion.

The policy contains no mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring mechanisms, predictive tools, or technology vendor terms. No dollar thresholds, specific procedures, deadlines, or cross-references to statutory law are included in this document.

## DGA-DGB — Authorized Signatures on District Checks

Adopted April 1972; revised April 1977, December 1981, March 1988, May 22, 1995, April 8, 1996, October 14, 2002, June 28, 2004, August 23, 2016.

CHECKS OF $5,000 OR MORE
All checks for $5,000 or more shall require the written or facsimile signatures of the President, Secretary and Treasurer of the Board of Education.

CHECKS UNDER $5,000
Institutions may use either option: (1) signatures from all three board officers (President, Secretary, Treasurer), or (2) the Treasurer's signature plus countersignature from an authorized District employee.

AUTHORIZATION PROCESS FOR COUNTERSIGNERS
The Board annually determines job titles eligible to countersign checks under $5,000. The controller then designates specific employees holding those titles in writing.

FACSIMILE SIGNATURE REQUIREMENTS
As required by law, an authorized individual's facsimile signature may only be used after that individual's manual signature has been filed with the Colorado Secretary of State and certified by the individual under oath.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 11-55-101, et seq.; C.R.S. 22-32-107; C.R.S. 22-32-121.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, predictive tools, or software/technology vendor terms was found in this policy.

## DH — Employee Surety Bonds/Insurance

Codified 1995. Adopted by Board May 22, 1995; revised by Board August 11, 1997; revised by Superintendent May 14, 2007; revised by Superintendent September 26, 2016.

CORE REQUIREMENT
District employees with probable temporary custody of District funds exceeding fifty dollars must be protected by either a blanket form of surety bond or by individual surety bonds adequate for the amount involved. As an alternative, the District may purchase crime insurance with equivalent coverage.

COST RESPONSIBILITY
The District bears all expenses related to bonds and/or insurance programs.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-32-104(4); C.R.S. 22-32-109(1)(h); C.R.S. 22-32-121(3).

## DIC — Financial Reports and Statements

Adopted April 1972; revised May 1982; revised April 1988; reviewed August 11, 1997.

MONTHLY RECONCILIATIONS
Monthly reconciliations shall be made showing the total monthly revenue, expenditures, and fund balances of all funds.

BUDGET REPORTS
Budget reports shall be prepared each month showing monthly expenditures, total expenditures to date, and balance of each budgeted appropriation.
