## DIE — Audits/Financial Monitoring

Adopted April 1982; revised April 1988; revised to conform with practice May 22, 1995; reviewed August 11, 1997.

ANNUAL AUDIT REQUIREMENT
The district must conduct annual audits of all funds and accounts following fiscal year close, as required by state law.

AUDITOR APPOINTMENT AND QUALIFICATIONS
The Board appoints an independent auditor who is licensed to practice in Colorado and knowledgeable in government accounting. This auditor must also audit the district's activities accounts for Board reporting.

REQUIRED AUDIT REPORT CONTENTS
The audit report must include: (1) financial statements prepared in conformity with generally accepted governmental accounting principles, noted as district representations; (2) disclosures per the Financial Policies and Procedures Handbook, with supplemental schedules in State Board of Education format, aligned with audited statements; (3) coverage of all funds and activities of the school district; (4) a budget-to-actual comparison for each fund and activity; (5) the auditor's opinion on financial statements (including general fixed assets), with non-unqualified opinions requiring explanation; (6) disclosure of all instances of noncompliance with state law, including the Public School Finance Act of 1994, irrespective of materiality; and (7) a supplemental investment listing as of financial statement date.

AUDITOR RECOMMENDATIONS AND SERVICES
The auditor provides recommendations regarding accounting records, procedures, and related activities, plus other Board-requested services.

SUBMISSION DEADLINES
Reports must be completed within five months of fiscal year close (unless the state auditor grants an extension). Districts submit copies to the state auditor and state commissioner of education within 30 days of receipt.

AUDIT FREQUENCY
The Board reserves discretion to request audits at more frequent intervals.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-32-109(1)(k); C.R.S. 24-75-601.3; C.R.S. 29-1-601, et seq.

This policy contains no references to automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring tools, or software vendor terms.

## DIEA — Audit Committee

Adopted November 16, 2005; revised January 27, 2009; revised November 9, 2010; revised May 26, 2015.

PURPOSE AND RESPONSIBILITIES
The policy establishes a District Audit Committee to support the Board of Education's financial oversight. Key responsibilities include: monitoring policies, practices and procedures concerning internal and external audits; recommending policy changes to the Board; coordinating audit oversight and evaluating auditor performance; advising on selection and retention of auditors; reviewing audit findings, external opinions, and administrator letters; monitoring District responses to audit recommendations; facilitating reports on regulatory changes and accounting developments; ensuring compliance with applicable laws concerning accounting and financial matters; and maintaining effective fiscal internal controls.

MEMBERSHIP COMPOSITION
The Committee consists of seven voting members appointed by the Board: two Board members and five community members with significant financial and accounting experience. Non-voting ex officio members include the District's legal counsel, policy counsel, executive director of finance, and controller. The Committee may invite additional attendees ad hoc as needed.

GOVERNANCE AND LIABILITY
Members must comply with the Colorado Standards of Conduct Statute, C.R.S. §§ 24-18-101 et seq. The Committee must develop and annually review a Board-approved charter. Members receive immunity protections and defense cost coverage under the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act, C.R.S. §§ 24-10-101 et seq., for good-faith actions.

MEETING REQUIREMENTS
The Committee must meet a minimum of four times each year per the Colorado Open Meetings Law and submit annual fiscal year activity reports to the Board.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, or software vendor terms appears in this policy.

## DIEA-R — Internal Audit Services

Adopted August 13, 2012; revised July 25, 2016.

INTERNAL AUDITOR
The District may employ an internal auditor reporting to the executive director of finance with oversight from the District Audit Committee. The auditor reports directly to the finance director and, as requested, to the controller, superintendent, and Audit Committee. On matters presenting impropriety or conflict concerns, the internal auditor reports to the superintendent or Board President.

PURPOSE
The internal auditor assists in resource safeguarding by promoting an economical, efficient and effective business environment based on sound and practical internal controls. Services aim to evaluate organizational processes systematically and provide independent and objective insight, analysis and recommendations for constructive change and risk management. The philosophy emphasizes adding value to District operations and controls.

PROFESSIONAL STANDARDS
The internal auditor operates under The Institute of Internal Auditors' Code of Ethics and International Standards for the Professional Practice of Internal Auditing and adheres to applicable Practice Advisories.

ACCESS TO INFORMATION
The auditor receives full, free, timely and unrestricted access to any and all District records, physical properties and personnel relevant to functions under review. All employees must cooperate. Documents receive confidential handling. Administrators and Finance staff must inform appropriate officials in a timely manner of any significant breaches affecting compliance systems related to accounting and financial activities.

INDEPENDENCE
The auditor remains free of improper influence from District employees regarding audit selection, procedures, frequency, timing, or content. The auditor has no operational responsibility over reviewed activities and shall not develop systems, install procedures, or prepare records normally subject to audit.

AUDIT SCOPE
Services focus on activities affecting compliance with accounting and financial standards, regulations, procedures and policies, including: reviewing financial information reliability, operating systems, and measurement/reporting mechanisms; examining compliance systems regarding governing laws and District policies; reviewing asset safeguarding means and verifying asset existence; recommending internal control improvements; reviewing external auditor performance and coordination; assisting in investigations of suspected law or policy violations; informing leadership of emerging internal audit trends; and reviewing employee compliance with significant financial policy requirements. Matters exclusively involving non-financial operations fall outside current scope.

AUDIT PLANNING
The finance director and controller collaborate with the internal auditor to develop an annual plan submitted to the Audit Committee. Planning uses a risk-based methodology prioritizing the financial audit universe. Significant deviations require communication to the finance director and Audit Committee.

REPORTING
Periodic internal audit reports go to the finance director, with copies to the Audit Committee and external auditors. Reports include locations visited, audit ratings, significant findings, employee responses, and corrective actions with completion timelines. The finance director and controller collaborate on follow-up, with the Audit Committee providing input. Issues remain "open" until all parties agree on resolution.

PERIODIC ASSESSMENT
The finance director, controller, internal auditor, and Audit Committee periodically assess whether services adequately fulfill regulatory purposes, recommending necessary revisions to the superintendent.

This policy contains no references to automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring tools, or technology vendor terms.

## DJ — Purchasing

Adopted by Superintendent May 14, 2007; revised by Superintendent March 21, 2016; adopted by Board February 12, 2019; revised by Board December 8, 2020.

PURPOSE
The policy aims to provide for fair and equitable treatment of all persons or entities involved in purchasing, maximize the value of District funds, standardize the purchasing procedures, and foster full and open competition.

DEFINITION OF PURCHASE
Purchase encompasses buying goods and/or services with cash, a check or a purchasing card, as well as signing or otherwise agreeing to a contract obligating the District. Purchases shall not be divided for the purpose of circumventing the limits on purchasing authority. Incremental purchases are considered in the aggregate for the school year.

COMPLIANCE REQUIREMENTS
All purchases must comply with governing law and District policies, regulations and administrative guidelines. Non-compliant purchases are voidable by the District, and violations may result in disciplinary action up to and including termination of employment.

STRATEGIC SOURCING DEPARTMENT
A centralized Strategic Sourcing Department operates within Finance to work cooperatively with other District departments, sites and employees on procurement.

PURCHASE ORDER THRESHOLDS
$5,000 or more: a purchase order is required with either the District's standard written purchase order terms and conditions or a separate written contract.
Under $5,000: Finance maintains a list of goods/services requiring purchase orders; standard terms/contracts are optional.

VENDOR SELECTION CRITERIA
Employees must strive to obtain the best possible terms and conditions, price, quality, warranty/guarantee, support and overall value.

COOPERATIVE PURCHASING
The District may enter cooperative agreements with governmental entities when deemed to be in the best interest of the District and procedures are compatible with District policies.

GRANT PURCHASES
Grant-funded purchases may require special management, accounting or procedures with Finance Department coordination for compliance.

PUBLIC RECORDS ACCESS
Requests regarding purchase records follow the Colorado Open Records Act (CORA).

The policy contains no explicit references to automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring mechanisms, or predictive technology tools.

## DJA — Purchasing Authority, Methods, and Thresholds

Last revised May 13, 2025 (effective July 1, 2025).

PURCHASING AUTHORITY
The Board retains ultimate authority over all District purchases, with delegated authority based on purchase value: $250,000 or more requires prior Board approval; under $250,000 may be approved by the superintendent or chief finance officer if funds are budgeted and the purchase aligns with law and policy; under $10,000 may be approved via purchasing card (p-card) by Finance Department authorized employees. The chief finance officer may delegate authority to Finance Department employees through written documentation annually. District administrators may veto any employee purchase they supervise.

PURCHASING METHODS
Documented Price Quotes: requires soliciting written quotes from at least three (3) qualified vendors, with the Finance Department maintaining records. The Finance Department may approve purchases with fewer than three quotes if reasonable attempts were made.
Competitive Bidding: administered by the Finance Department, requiring detailed specifications, written terms/conditions, procedures, solicitation of at least three (3) qualified bidders, and a public/electronic bid opening.
Competitive Proposals: appropriate for complex purchases, requiring objectives/descriptions, evaluation procedures, solicitation from at least three qualified organizations, potential interviews by two District officials (one from Finance), and a written contract.

PURCHASING THRESHOLDS
Under $10,000: no competitive method required.
$10,000-$100,000: minimum three documented price quotes required.
$100,000+: competitive bidding or proposal process required.
Purchases cannot be divided to circumvent these methods.

EXCEPTIONS
Educational Equipment: superintendent or assistant superintendent may authorize based on a written need determination without competition.
Cooperative Purchasing: chief finance officer may authorize joint purchasing arrangements with other agencies.
Sole Source Items: chief finance officer has discretion to approve unique goods/services from single vendors with sufficient documentation.
Standardization/Compatibility: Finance Department develops guidelines for system interoperability justifications.
Conferences/Speakers: District administrator may authorize based on a written need determination.
District's Best Interests: superintendent or chief finance officer designee may waive methods if competition would result in a substantially higher cost or adversely affect the District.

EMERGENCIES
Defined as imminent threats to health, welfare, safety, property, or creating excessive financial risk/liability exposure. Designated administrators may make immediate purchases without competitive requirements, submitting written explanation to the Finance Department afterward. The chief finance officer reviews all emergency purchases and reports those exceeding $250,000 to the Board.

GRIEVANCES
Vendors may protest within ten (10) business days of the challenged action. Investigation leads to an executive director decision, appealable to the chief finance officer. The superintendent's decision is final for purchases under $250,000; the Board may hear appeals for $250,000+ purchases.

This policy contains no mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, scoring, predictive tools, or procurement software requirements.

## DJB — Contracting

Adopted May 13, 2025; effective July 1, 2025.

OVERVIEW
The policy governs all District contracts for goods and services procurement regardless of cost. A contract is mandated for services that may create liability for the District unless exempted by administrative guidelines approved by legal counsel. Purchases of $10,000 or more require either a purchase order with standard written terms or an executed contract per this policy.

DEFINITIONS
Contract: an agreement between the District and one or more parties that creates mutual obligations that are enforceable or otherwise recognizable at law.
Cooperative Purchasing Agreement: a process allowing the District to purchase goods/services at pre-negotiated rates using existing contracts awarded by other public agencies.
District-Issued Contract: an agreement generated by the District for specific services/goods, requiring generation or minimum review/approval by Finance or legal counsel.
Material Change: a modification to a standard District template or standard written terms and conditions that alters the legal obligations of a party.
Service: work by non-District employees providing specialized knowledge/skills/expertise, typically intangible.
Standard District Template: contracts reviewed/approved by legal counsel for construction, service agreements, software purchases, community partnerships, and other services.
Standard Written Terms and Conditions: standard contract approved by legal counsel for goods purchases (excluding software).
Vendor Contract: vendor-issued agreements requiring Finance or legal counsel review before execution.

CONTRACT EXECUTION AND APPROVAL
The District prioritizes standard written terms, standard templates, or District-issued contracts. Exceptions require Finance or legal counsel approval. Standard District templates bypass legal counsel review unless material changes are requested. Cooperative purchasing agreements may be executed if in the District's best interest and compliant with District policies.

REQUIREMENTS FOR WRITTEN CONTRACTS
Criminal Background Check Provision: all written contracts must require a criminal background check for any person providing direct services to students under the contract, including but not limited to instruction, physical, mental, and social health supports, transportation or food services as required by law. The contracting entity bears background check costs.
Public Works Contingency: construction/design contracts must include provisions making District obligations contingent on appropriated/budgeted funds per C.R.S. § 24-91-103.6.
Insurance Requirements: all written contracts must include insurance requirements reviewed and approved by risk management.

PROHIBITED TERMS (VOID UNLESS LEGAL COUNSEL PRE-APPROVES)
Any requirement that the District indemnify or hold harmless another person or entity. Any requirement that the District participate in binding arbitration or other extrajudicial process for dispute resolution. Any requirement that the District agree to limit liability of another person or entity for bodily injury, death, or damage to school district property. Any waiver, alteration, or limitation of the application of the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act. Any waiver, alteration, or limitation of the application of the Student Data Transparency and Security Act or the Colorado Privacy Act. Any conflict with Colorado law or associated rules under state statute.

CONTRACT APPROVAL AUTHORITY
Contracts require signatures from the appropriate employee with purchasing authority or the Board's presiding officer. The Board may delegate negotiation/execution to specified staff upon purchase amount approval.

APPROVAL THRESHOLDS (TABLE)
No cost: Principal/Manager/Director and Executive Director/Cabinet Member sign.
Under $10,000: Principal/Manager/Director and Executive Director/Cabinet Member sign.
$10,000-$100,000: Principal/Manager/Director, Executive Director/Cabinet Member, and Legal Counsel sign.
$100,000-$250,000: Principal/Manager/Director, Executive Director/Cabinet Member, Legal Counsel, and Finance Designee sign.
$250,000+: Principal/Manager/Director, Executive Director/Cabinet Member, Legal Counsel, and Finance Designee sign; Board Presiding Officer signature required unless Board delegates signing authority.
District receiving payment: Principal/Manager/Director and Executive Director/Cabinet Member sign; Finance Designee required when federal grant funding is involved or District receives payment (excluding donations).
Legal Counsel approval is required for non-standard templates or high-risk contracts, and for standard templates with material changes.

CROSS REFERENCES
DJ (Purchasing and Contracting); DJA (Purchasing Authority, Methods, and Thresholds).

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-1-135 (terms and conditions in public school contracts); C.R.S. 22-32-122(4) (background check provision required in service contracts).

The policy contains no explicit mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, predictive tools, or specific software/technology vendor requirements, beyond general references to "software purchases" as a category covered by standard District contract templates and the cross-reference to the Student Data Transparency and Security Act and Colorado Privacy Act (data protection statutes, not AI-specific provisions).

## DJC — Petty Cash

Adopted May 14, 2007; revised March 21, 2016.

AUTHORIZATION AND PURPOSE
The controller holds authority to establish petty cash accounts for District departments and sites as needed. The stated purpose is to provide a source of ready cash for immediate settlement of small transactions. However, the policy emphasizes that the preferred method of making District purchases is by means of a restricted check or use of a purchasing card.

CUSTODIAN RESPONSIBILITIES
For authorized petty cash funds, the controller designates a custodian. This individual must ensure that all expenditures from the fund are properly approved, accounted for and documented.

FINANCIAL LIMITATIONS
Two dollar thresholds govern petty cash operations: maximum fund size per department/site is $5,000; maximum individual purchase amount is $100. The policy explicitly prohibits circumventing limits through purchase subdivision: purchases shall not be divided for the purpose of circumventing this limitation.

CROSS REFERENCES
Related policies include DJ (Purchasing), DJA (Purchasing Authority), DJB (Purchasing Procedures), DJG/DJGA (Vendor Relations, Sales Calls and Demonstrations), and DH (Bonded Employees and Directors).

The policy contains no references to automated systems, algorithms, AI tools, or software vendor arrangements.

## DJG-DJGA — Vendor Relations, Sales Calls and Demonstrations

Originally adopted May 1972; most recent revision December 8, 2020.

VENDOR QUALIFICATIONS
The Finance Department may collaborate with other District departments to establish required vendor qualifications for certain District purchases and prequalify vendors as deemed appropriate.

CONFLICT OF INTEREST REQUIREMENTS
District staff must uphold fiduciary responsibilities in all contract and purchasing matters. The policy prohibits vendors from offering, and employees from accepting, any gift, service, honorarium, stipend or fee that could improperly influence purchasing decisions. Personnel cannot maintain financial interests in contracts they personally negotiate.

SALES CALL AUTHORIZATION
Sales representatives require authorization from the superintendent or finance executive director before entering District schools. Leadership may bar any vendor, organization or person from facilities when deemed necessary to protect educational operations.

VIOLATION CONSEQUENCES
Employees face potential discipline up to and including termination of employment. Vendors engaging in policy violations may receive indefinite disqualification from District business.

The policy contains no references to automated decision systems, algorithms, AI applications, machine learning tools, or predictive software in vendor evaluation or procurement processes.

## DKC — Expense Authorization/Reimbursement

Adopted September 1973; revised January 1975, February 1976, June 1990, May 22, 1995, August 11, 1997, June 28, 2004, September 27, 2004, April 14, 2014. (Also covers Mileage and Travel.)

CORE POLICY STATEMENT
Employees shall be reimbursed for expenses associated with mileage and in-state and out-of-state travel when such expenditures meet specific criteria including: necessity for conducting district business, proper authorization, reasonableness, and appropriate documentation.

ADMINISTRATIVE FRAMEWORK
The Finance Department bears responsibility for establishing administrative guidelines and procedures governing reimbursement. These guidelines must align with IRS regulations.

REQUIREMENTS FOR REIMBURSEMENT
Expenses must satisfy four conditions: (1) associated with mileage or in-state/out-of-state travel; (2) incurred conducting necessary, legitimate district business; (3) properly authorized; and (4) reasonable and appropriately documented per Finance Department procedures.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-32-110(1)(i); C.R.S. 24-18-104(3)(d) & (e).

The provided content contains no mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, AI tools, machine learning, scoring mechanisms, or software vendor terms.

## DN — School Properties Disposition

Adopted April 1972; last revised December 8, 2020.

KEY RESPONSIBILITIES
The superintendent or designee serves as the Board's authorized agent for property disposition, determining whether assets are obsolete, surplus, and/or of no further value. The policy emphasizes attempting re-use of surplus property within the district wherever practical.

DISPOSITION METHODS
Surplus property shall be handled through one of four approaches: sealed bid sales or auctions deemed advantageous to the district; trade-ins for similar equipment purchases; charitable or governmental donations; or disposal or recycling per established procedures.

REAL ESTATE AND TITLE TRANSFER REQUIREMENTS
The Board of Education will approve the disposition of any and all real estate (e.g., land and/or buildings). Sales or conveyances requiring recorded title transfers (such as motor vehicles) need superintendent or designee advance approval.

PROHIBITED CONDUCT
District personnel cannot purchase surplus or district property except through official public sales available to the general public.

TECHNOLOGY EQUIPMENT PROTOCOLS
Technology items remain district-owned until the equipment and/or software is deemed by district administration to be unused, obsolete, unwanted, or ineffective. The IT department then relocates equipment within the district or disposes per established guidelines.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-32-110(1)(e); C.R.S. 24-18-202.

# Section E — Support Services

## EBAB — Hazardous Substances

PURPOSE AND SCOPE
The District commits to maintaining an environment for students, staff, and the general public that is as free as reasonably possible of known hazardous substances. "Hazardous substances" are defined by reference to the federal Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation, and Liability Act of 1980 (CERCLA), as amended, and its implementing regulations.

ENVIRONMENTAL AND SAFETY COORDINATOR
The superintendent appoints an environmental and safety coordinator responsible for: (1) ensuring District compliance with federal, state, and local hazardous substance laws; (2) ensuring compliance with the Poudre School District Crisis Response and Management Manual as it relates to hazardous substances; (3) providing education and training to District employees and students regarding compliance and crisis response procedures; and (4) serving as liaison with federal, state, and local regulators on hazardous substance matters.

INVENTORY AND MATERIAL SAFETY DATA SHEETS
Each District site must conduct an annual identification and inventory of chemicals and hazardous substances used in construction, building/grounds maintenance, custodial services, arts, crafts, industrial arts, music, science, and other work activities involving chemicals. The coordinator assists with and bears responsibility for disposal of unidentified chemicals and suspected hazardous substances. The coordinator also oversees completion and maintenance of Material Safety Data Sheets (MSDS) at each site, maintaining a complete set at a central location "readily available for review and use by District employees; by police, fire and emergency service authorities; and by the general public as permitted or required by law."

ACCEPTANCE, STORAGE, DISPOSAL, AND TRANSFER
The District shall not accept donations of chemicals or hazardous substances. When hazardous substances are no longer needed, they may be declared waste; the coordinator arranges storage, disposal, and/or transfer in accordance with governing federal, state, and local laws and maintains written documentation of all disposals. Federal and state law provides exemptions from certain regulatory requirements for conditionally exempt small quantity generators, and the District seeks to preserve this status where reasonably possible in its disposal decisions. The coordinator designates storage areas for substances that are or might become hazardous, and for hazardous waste awaiting disposal. All containers must be labeled with (1) date received, (2) shelf life, and (3) expiration date, if any; where space permits, the oldest substances should be used first. The coordinator also ensures that transfer and transportation of hazardous materials comply with governing federal, state, and local laws.

TRAINING AND EMERGENCY RESPONSE
The coordinator ensures that staff and students with reasonably foreseeable use of or contact with hazardous substances receive training on appropriate use, handling, storage, disposal, and transfer of such substances, and on the District's emergency response and evacuation procedures. Emergency response follows the Poudre School District Crisis Response and Management Manual.

ADOPTION AND REVISION HISTORY
Adopted by the Board: April 1989. Revised by the Board to conform with practice: May 22, 1995. Revised by the Board: May 13, 1996. Revised by the Superintendent: June 23, 2009.

LEGAL REFERENCES
42 U.S.C. 9601 et seq.; C.R.S. 25-15-101 et seq.; C.R.S. 29-22-101 et seq.; C.R.S. 42-20-101 et seq.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
This policy contains no mention of information technology systems, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance, HIPAA, transportation eligibility, food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool.

## EBBA — Prevention of Disease/Infection Transmission

SOURCE ANOMALY NOTE
The PDF retrieved from the District's designated URL for policy code EBBA carries the header "EBBA - PREVENTION OF DISEASE/INFECTION TRANSMISSION," but the body text of the document, verified across two independent fetches (including verbatim quotation of the opening sentences and the adoption/revision date block), is entirely about accident reporting procedures rather than disease or infection transmission prevention. Because the primary URL did not fail or 404 (it returned a valid, consistently-reproduced document), no fallback fetch was attempted per instructions. The content below is transcribed faithfully as found at the source, with this discrepancy flagged rather than silently corrected or fabricated. Note that a separate, substantively different regulation document exists at EBBA-R and does address actual disease/infection transmission procedures (see below).

PURPOSE
"Adequate and prompt accident reporting is essential if similar accidents are to be prevented." The Board requires that accident reports be filed for incidents occurring on school grounds or involving District vehicles, students, volunteers, visitors, or staff during school-sponsored or authorized business trips. Reports are required "regardless of whether injuries or property damage are immediately apparent." Prompt reporting is described as "vital in assuring the district staff, students, and others of insurance coverage."

PROCEDURES
The risk manager must establish filing procedures ensuring that reports capture: (1) details useful for preventing future accidents; (2) information needed for insurance claims; and (3) details potentially relevant to litigation.

ADOPTION AND REVISION HISTORY
Adopted: February 1975. Revised: February 1982. Revised: January 1986. Revised: May 1988. Revised to conform with practice: May 22, 1995. Revised: May 13, 1996.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
No mention found of information technology systems, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance, HIPAA, transportation eligibility, food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool.

## EBBA-R — Prevention of Disease/Infection Transmission

DOCUMENT OVERVIEW
This regulation (accompanying policy EBBA) addresses infection control procedures for staff handling blood and bodily substances, specifically "Handling Body Fluids and Substances." Issued May 22, 1995; revised February 27, 1998 and January 26, 2000.

CORE PRINCIPLE
"All blood and other body fluids should be considered as potentially infectious," without distinguishing between individuals with known infections and those who are asymptomatic or pathogen-free.

POTENTIALLY INFECTIOUS BODY FLUIDS
Blood is identified as "the single most important source of infection." Additional substances of concern include semen, vaginal fluids, feces, wound drainage, urine, vomit, respiratory secretions, saliva, and any visibly blood-contaminated fluid.

UNIVERSAL PRECAUTIONS
Staff must assume all body fluids are infectious and use appropriate personal protective equipment (PPE) in all situations where blood or bodily fluid contact may occur. One exception is permitted: employees may temporarily forgo PPE "under rare and extraordinary circumstances" using good judgment, with the understanding that this increases safety risk.

PERSONAL PROTECTIVE EQUIPMENT STANDARDS
Gloves must be maintained in emergency response kits at accessible locations and worn when treating nosebleeds or bleeding cuts, during diaper changes and handling of soiled clothing, when contacting contaminated laundry, and during disinfection/cleanup of contaminated surfaces or broken objects. Cuts, sores, or non-intact skin (e.g., chapped hands, torn cuticles) must be covered with gloves or finger cots. Pocket face masks should be used and kept available for mouth-to-mouth resuscitation.

HAND WASHING PROTOCOL
Hand washing is described as "the single most important technique for preventing the spread of infectious disease," with no available substitute. Proper technique requires soap and water with vigorous washing under running water for approximately 15-30 seconds using circular motions and friction, covering front and back hand surfaces, between fingers, knuckles, around fingernails, under nail beds, and entire wrists. Required hand-washing occasions include: before and after eating, drinking, or smoking; before and after bathroom use; before care begins and between care/first-aid delivery; before and after assisting with feeding or food preparation; before handling clean equipment or utensils; after handling soiled garments, diapers, or assisting with toileting/diapering; after bodily secretion contact; after disposable glove removal; and "when in doubt."

DISINFECTION REQUIREMENTS
Hepatitis B virus (HBV) and HIV are identified as "two of the most common bloodborne pathogens hazards." HBV is described as "highly stable" and capable of remaining viable on environmental surfaces for up to seven days, unlike HIV. Bloodborne pathogens can transmit via contaminated objects such as broken glass. Work surface decontamination procedures require: washing contaminated surfaces and non-disposable items with standard disinfectants using aerosol germicide cleaners; placing contaminated clothing in plastic-lined, covered containers; washing contaminated clothing and linen in hot water with detergent; placing contaminated tissues, paper towels, and disposable items in plastic bags before safe disposal; never picking up broken glass by hand, but sweeping it into a pan using a broom while wearing gloves during disposal; and using individual judgment for barriers in unpredictable situations, with barriers recommended whenever bodily fluid or substance contact is anticipated.

HIV/AIDS INFORMATION
The regulation states: it is extremely difficult to be infected with HIV/AIDS, and intact-skin exposure to blood is a highly unlikely transmission route; transmission requires blood, semen, or vaginal secretions entering the bloodstream of a noninfected person; other substances (saliva, tears, urine, feces) have extremely minimal or no detectable virus levels; no documented cases exist of HIV transmission via mouth-to-mouth resuscitation; and HIV is easily destroyed by common disinfectants.

ADDENDUM I — TRANSMISSION CONCERNS BY BODY SUBSTANCE SOURCE
Blood (cuts/abrasions, nosebleeds, menses, contaminated needles): organisms of concern are Hepatitis B virus, Hepatitis C virus, HIV/AIDS, and Cytomegalovirus; transmission occurs via bloodstream inoculation through hand cuts/abrasions or direct bloodstream inoculation.
Feces (incontinence): organisms of concern are Hepatitis A virus, Salmonella bacteria, and Shigella bacteria; transmission occurs via oral inoculation from contaminated hands.
Respiratory secretions (saliva, nasal discharge): organisms of concern are the common cold virus, influenza virus, and Epstein-Barr virus; transmission occurs via oral inoculation from contaminated hands.
Vomitus: organism of concern is gastrointestinal viruses (e.g., Norwalk virus); transmission occurs via oral inoculation from contaminated hands.
Urine (incontinence): organism of concern is Cytomegalovirus; transmission occurs via bloodstream inoculation through hand cuts and abrasions.
Semen/vaginal fluids: organisms of concern are Hepatitis B virus, Hepatitis C virus, HIV/AIDS, and Gonococcus bacteria; transmission occurs via sexual contact (intercourse).

SPECIAL NOTES
The regulation emphasizes that no reported HIV/AIDS transmission cases involve feces, respiratory secretions, vomitus, or urine sources, and reiterates the primacy of hand washing. Epstein-Barr virus is noted as causing a mononucleosis-like illness.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
No mention found of information technology systems, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance, HIPAA, transportation eligibility, food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool.

## EBCB — Fire and Emergency Evacuation Response Drills

GENERAL COMPLIANCE OBLIGATIONS
The District shall cooperate with local fire department officials regarding building inspections and evacuation procedures, and must comply with local, state, and federal fire and safety regulations to ensure the safety of students, employees, and members of the public. All unsafe conditions must be reported to the Customer Support Center.

ORIENTATION AND TRAINING
Orientation programs for employees and students must include instruction about each school's emergency plan and equipment use, with particular attention to: fire alarm activation procedures; location of fire extinguishers; location of fire alarm boxes or stations; fire extinguisher usage appropriate to building types; "the usual exits, lines of travel, and/or other emergency procedures that students in every classroom shall be expected to follow in case of fire, earthquake, civil defense, or other emergency"; alternate sites and procedures if primary exits are blocked; first aid equipment location and use; and fire-safe room locations where applicable. Emergency exit information must be posted in each room, "clearly printed in large letters on a sign posted next to the doors in each room."

FIRE DRILL PROCEDURES AND AUTHORITY
Fire drill procedures are developed jointly by the District and the local fire department. The fire department has authority to conduct unannounced drills at any time and shall notify the superintendent "if practicable" in advance. Sufficient fire drills must be held at each site to ensure students and employees thoroughly understand proper procedures and evacuation routes; all students and employees must evacuate the building during every fire drill.

FIRE DRILL SCHEDULE
First semester: one announced drill is required during the first four weeks, pre-planned by the principal, plus at least one unannounced drill between October 1 and November 30. Second semester scheduling depends on the results of the first unannounced drill: if results are satisfactory, only one additional drill is required in the first month of the second semester; if results are unsatisfactory, "a minimum of one additional fire drill per month shall be held until satisfactory results are obtained." Summer school: a minimum of one required fire drill must be held during the summer school session at each school holding summer school.

REPORTING REQUIREMENTS
A report of each fire drill must be made to the superintendent or designee after the first four weeks of school and after each subsequent fire drill during the school year. Reports must include the date, time of day, evacuation duration, general evaluation, unusual conditions, and special mention of "the equipment, alarm systems, exits, or other circumstances that in any way limit the complete exit of the school."

ADOPTION AND REVISION HISTORY
Adopted by the Board: August 11, 1997. Revised by the Superintendent: December 1, 2008.

CROSS REFERENCES
KDE, Crisis Management and Prevention.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
No mention found of information technology systems, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance, HIPAA, transportation eligibility, food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool.

## EBCE — School Closings and Cancellations

DOCUMENT STATUS
Adopted by the Board: May 22, 1995 (current practice codified). Revised by the Board: April 28, 1997. Revised by the Superintendent: December 17, 2007.

AUTHORITY AND CORE PRINCIPLE
The superintendent has the authority to close schools or dismiss them early "in the event of hazardous weather or other emergencies" that threaten student or staff safety, health, or welfare.

DECISION-MAKING FRAMEWORK
Closure determinations may be non-uniform across the district owing to its "large and diverse geographic area," where "weather conditions may vary greatly within the District" — for example, a storm concentrated in the foothills may result in closure of only the mountain schools. Parents retain independent authority to determine that conditions are too hazardous for their child's attendance, delayed arrival, or early dismissal; class time missed as a result of such parental determinations "shall be dealt with and accounted for as an excused absence."

SEVERE WEATHER RESPONSE PROCEDURES
For a moderate snowstorm, snow removal personnel begin plowing "in sufficient time to ensure safe parking and pedestrian movement for normal morning operations," while transportation personnel concurrently assess storm severity and area road conditions, analyzing data from the National Weather Service and area emergency services. Weather and road information must be delivered to the superintendent before 5:00 a.m., with a final decision made not later than 5:30 a.m.; communication to personnel and media begins immediately thereafter. Full-day closures occur "under extreme circumstances if conditions are such that it would be unusually hazardous for students to walk and/or be bused to school." When conditions are "severe but not serious enough to close schools," the superintendent may announce a two-hour late start: schools open two hours later than normal, bus riders are picked up two hours later than normal, and District employees report one hour later than normal unless otherwise directed.

PUBLIC NOTIFICATION
Closure and delay information is broadcast via television channels 2, 4, 7, 9, 10, and 31, and radio stations KCOL, EAGLE, BEAR, KCSU, KIIX, KLOV, KOA, KOOL 105, KTRR (TRI-102), KUAD, KUNC, and KWBI; information is also made available by e-mail. District personnel are instructed to consider broadcast information accurate and not to call television or radio stations or the District switchboard, because "Support Services Center telephone lines must be kept open for emergency communications."

MID-DAY EMERGENCY CLOSURES
Storms commencing during the school day are assessed as they occur. When a midday closure becomes necessary, information is passed to all locations via the emergency telephone calling chain, and administrators must ensure sufficient staff remain on site until all students have been released to a safe mode of transportation home.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-32-109(1)(n); C.R.S. 22-33-104.

CROSS REFERENCES
JLIB, Student Dismissal Precautions.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
No mention found of information technology systems, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance, HIPAA, or food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool. Transportation is discussed only in the operational sense of bus pickup delays and safe release of students to transportation home, not in terms of transportation program eligibility determinations.

## EC — Property Management

PURPOSE
District property (grounds, buildings, facilities) represents a substantial public investment and must be "efficiently utilized, economically managed, and properly maintained in accordance with governing federal, state and local laws and applicable District policies and regulations."

GENERAL RESPONSIBILITIES
The superintendent or designee(s) must establish administrative guidelines and procedures and maintain general oversight of: facilities planning, design, and construction; facilities and grounds; property management; custodial services; utilities management and environmental services; transportation; food services; and safety, security, and emergency planning.

GOVERNING PRINCIPLES FOR MANAGEMENT, MAINTENANCE, AND PROTECTION OF DISTRICT PROPERTY
District property management must comply with all governing laws, District policies, and regulations. Any material change in the intended use of District grounds, buildings, or other facilities must be approved by the superintendent or the superintendent's designee. All remodeling, retrofitting, renovations, repairs, modifications, additions, and improvements must be coordinated through the Operations Department and comply with applicable building codes and specifications; Operations staff must collaborate with site managers regarding the nature/scope, funding, timeline, operational impact, and prioritization of such projects.

LEGAL REFERENCES
6 CCR 1010-6, Rules 1-101 et seq. through 10-101 et seq.

CROSS REFERENCES
CFD, Site-Based Management; DJB, Purchasing Procedures.

ADOPTION DATE
Approved by the Superintendent: October 13, 2008.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
The policy lists "transportation" and "food services" among the operational areas subject to superintendent oversight and administrative guidelines, but does not itself set out transportation or food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility criteria. No mention found of information technology systems, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance, HIPAA, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool.

## ECAB — Securing District Facilities

ACCESS CONTROL SYSTEM
The superintendent or designee must establish "an adequate key and access control system for entry to District facilities and areas within District facilities when they are not open to the public."

ISSUANCE OF ACCESS CREDENTIALS
Keys, access cards, and security codes "shall be issued only to those employees, individuals or entities that require access pursuant to their employment or contract with the District."

ACCESS CONTROL RESTRICTIONS
No individual with issued credentials may release or loan a key, access card, and/or security code from their possession to anyone for any reason. Duplicate keys shall not be made.

LOSS REPORTING
Loss of a key, access card, and/or security code must be reported immediately to the building principal or site/department access manager, and to the District's Customer Support Center.

PHYSICAL SECURITY MEASURES
Alarm systems and other devices that protect buildings against illegal entry and vandalism shall be installed where appropriate. Employment of security personnel requires superintendent approval "in situations where special risks are involved."

AFTER-HOURS SECURITY
Employees leaving a building after hours must ensure the building is secure prior to their exit.

ADOPTION AND REVISION HISTORY
Adopted April 1972. Revised June 1982, August 1982, June 1988, September 9, 1996, January 9, 2006, and April 26, 2010.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 18-4-503; C.R.S. 18-4-504.

CROSS REFERENCES
KF, Use of District Facilities.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
The policy addresses physical access control (keys, access cards, security codes, alarm systems) but contains no explicit mention of information technology systems as a distinct subject, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance (beyond generic reference to "alarm systems and other devices"), HIPAA, transportation eligibility, food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool.

## ECAC — Vandalism

FUNDING AND COMMUNITY RESPONSIBILITY
School buildings and grounds are maintained through community tax dollars, making vandalism damage a shared fiscal burden. The Board urges all citizens, students, and law enforcement to report vandalism incidents and to identify responsible parties.

REPORTING OBLIGATIONS
District employees must report all known vandalism incidents to their school's principal or site manager, including the names of suspected perpetrators when available.

AUTHORIZATION TO PURSUE LEGAL ACTION
The superintendent, assistant superintendents, principal, or their designee may sign criminal complaints against persons suspected of vandalizing school property.

STUDENT CONSEQUENCES
Students who willfully or maliciously destroy school property through vandalism or arson, or who create safety hazards, may be referred to law enforcement. "Students who are caught vandalizing school property may be suspended and/or expelled."

DAMAGE RECOVERY
The Board intends to pursue monetary damages from vandals and their parents or guardians as permitted by law.

ADOPTION AND REVISION HISTORY
Adopted May 22, 1995. Revised September 9, 1996.

FLAGGED TOPIC REVIEW
No mention found of information technology systems, records retention timelines, electronic monitoring or surveillance, HIPAA, transportation eligibility, food-service/free-or-reduced-price meal eligibility, copyright, or any automated decision system, algorithm, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tool.

## ECAF — Electronic Monitoring and Surveillance

AUTHORIZATION AND SCOPE
The Board of Education authorizes the District to use video and audio-visual cameras at District facilities, in and around District buildings, and on District transportation vehicles, as well as monitoring of communications across District tools, services, and infrastructure (including the District telephone system). The superintendent or designee must approve all monitoring/surveillance systems before acquisition, and the Chief Technology Officer must approve any network connections associated with such systems. The policy was adopted April 22, 2008 (effective July 1, 2008) and has been revised May 26, 2009; April 28, 2015; and May 27, 2025 (this most recent revision effective July 1, 2025).

USE OF CAMERAS
Video and audio-visual cameras may be used to monitor and record students, staff, and other persons at District facilities on a year-round basis, "at any and all times, whether or not school is in session." Deployment covers District buildings, grounds in and around buildings, and District transportation vehicles.

NOTICE REQUIREMENTS
Where audio-visual recording (i.e., recording that captures both video and audio) is used, the District must give "sufficient notice ... to reasonably inform them of the monitoring and recording." Notice may be satisfied through posted signage in monitored areas.

PRIVACY LIMITS
Cameras are expressly prohibited "in restrooms, locker facilities or other areas where students, staff, and/or other persons have a reasonable expectation of privacy." This is a hard carve-out from the general camera-use authorization.

TELEPHONE MONITORING AND RECORDING
Communications over the District's telephone system "may be monitored and/or recorded at any time in compliance with applicable state law." Any resulting recordings are District property. Access to telephone recordings requires the requester to demonstrate "a legitimate need to do so, as determined by the superintendent, director of student safety & emergency management, or their designee(s)."

USE, STORAGE, AND SECURITY OF RECORDINGS
Video, audio, and audio-visual recordings may be used as evidence that a student, staff member, or other person has engaged in behavior relevant to disciplinary, investigatory, or other District proceedings. Recordings are and remain the property of the District.

STUDENT EDUCATION RECORDS
The District will comply with all applicable law regarding student education records as it pertains to video, audio, and audio-visual recordings, including obligations arising under the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act (20 U.S.C. 1232g), which is cited as a legal reference for this policy.

RETENTION
Video and audio recordings must be "maintained in their original form for at least seven (7) calendar days after the initial recording." This baseline retention period is extended where "an incident has occurred in which a recording may be relevant to an investigation," in which case the relevant recording must be preserved beyond the seven-day floor — specifically, materials tied to an investigation must be preserved "until the investigation and any resulting legal proceedings and/or disciplinary action is finally concluded."

ACCESS AND VIEWING PROCEDURES
Video and audio-visual recordings "are and shall remain the property of the District." Authorized District officials with a legitimate need may view recordings without additional approval. Non-District officials (which may include parents, law enforcement, or other outside parties) seeking access must submit a written request within seven (7) calendar days of the incident, specifying the reason for the request. Approved viewings occur only at specified District locations, with a designated District supervisor/administrator present to oversee the viewing.

DOCUMENTATION AND LOGS
The District maintains written logs tracking all access to and viewing of recordings, including the date of access, the reason given for the request, and identifying information about who accessed or viewed the recording.

AUTOMATED / AI ANALYSIS — NONE FOUND
FLAG: Repeated, targeted review of this policy's full text found NO language anywhere in ECAF referencing artificial intelligence, machine learning, algorithms, automated or algorithmic analysis, predictive analytics, facial recognition, weapons detection, gunshot detection, video analytics, or any other automated/smart-technology processing applied to camera footage, telephone recordings, or network/device monitoring data. The policy addresses only camera placement/notice, telephone monitoring, storage, retention, and manual (human-reviewed) access/viewing procedures.

LEGAL REFERENCES AND CROSS-REFERENCES
