The District may allocate resources among activities based on institutional judgment and educational mission priorities.

SCHOOL-SPONSORED ACTIVITIES AND ORGANIZATIONS ESTABLISHMENT AND OVERSIGHT
School-sponsored activities may be established by the principal with superintendent approval. District employees may apply in writing to establish sponsored activities, with principal decisions subject to superintendent review. A District employee must supervise or advise each approved activity.

MEMBERSHIP REQUIREMENTS AND PROTECTIONS
Membership is voluntary and limited to currently enrolled students unless law requires otherwise. Activities may impose academic qualifications for membership where necessarily related to the purposes of the activity or organization. Prohibited discrimination includes denials based on race, color, national origin, religion, ancestry, sex, sexual orientation, or disability. Sex-based restrictions apply only where necessary to preserve the health, safety or welfare of students, or where sex is a bona fide and integral qualification.

RESOURCE ALLOCATION
The principal determines financial support levels and facility access, subject to superintendent approval and policies DJ, DJA, and DJB (purchasing authority).

SECONDARY SCHOOL STUDENT-INITIATED AND LED ORGANIZATIONS — APPROVAL PROCESS
Secondary students may establish organizations upon prior written approval of the school's principal and the superintendent's designee through District-approved applications complying with laws, discipline rules, and policy terms. Annual re-application is required.

EQUAL ACCESS AND NON-DISCRIMINATION
The District shall not deny equal access to school facilities for meetings of approved student-initiated and led organizations, or otherwise discriminate against such organizations based on religious, political, philosophical or other content.

MEETING PARAMETERS
Organizations meet during non-instructional time (before instruction begins or after it ends; lunch periods overlapping instruction count as instructional). Meetings must not materially and substantially interfere with the orderly conduct of educational activities and cannot be regularly attended by nonschool persons. A school employee must monitor meetings, attending religious meetings only in a nonparticipatory capacity.

PUBLICATIONS AND COMMUNICATIONS
Approved organizations appear in yearbooks and publications on the same basis as other noncurriculum-related student groups. They may post on designated bulletin boards using District-approved forms and announce meetings via public address system.

FINANCIAL AND SPONSORSHIP CLARIFICATIONS
Organizations bear all out-of-pocket costs. The District maintains no accounts, funds, or involvement in fundraising. Organizations shall not be deemed to be sponsored or endorsed by the District and cannot represent District sponsorship or control. Organizations may identify student membership but may not represent that they are sponsored, supervised or controlled by the District.

PROHIBITED ACTIVITIES AND COMPLIANCE
Organizations must not engage in activities contrary to law, District policies/regulations or school rules; that disrupt or clearly threaten to disrupt the orderly operation of the District or school; or that would adversely affect the health, safety or welfare of any student or District employee. Noncompliance grounds revocation rights.

RELIGIOUS ACTIVITY PROTECTIONS
Officials may not influence the form or content of any prayer or religious activity, require any person to participate in prayer or religious activity, or compel any school employee to attend any meeting if the meeting is contrary to the beliefs of the employee.

LEGAL REFERENCES
Equal Access Act, 20 U.S.C. 4071-4074; C.R.S. 22-1-117; C.R.S. 22-1-118.

CROSS REFERENCES
KF (Use of District Facilities); DJ, DJA, DJB (Purchasing policies).

This policy contains no provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, assessment-based placement, or automated decision systems, algorithms, AI, machine learning, or predictive tools.

## IGF — Curriculum Review

REVIEW PARTICIPANTS AND TIMELINE
The curriculum shall be reviewed at regular intervals by administrators, teachers, parents, accountability committee members, other advisory committee members, and community stakeholders. The administration establishes the specific review schedule.

REGULATORY REQUIREMENTS
Administration must develop regulations addressing: which courses undergo review, the sequence for reviewing them, specific curriculum review activities, and review scope areas.

SUBSTANTIVE REVIEW COMPONENTS
Reviews must examine achievement results for all student populations, educational equity, curriculum breadth and depth, and congruence of instructional strategies and assessment with district performance standards adopted by the Board.

POLICY HISTORY
Adopted: May 22, 1995; Revised: June 10, 1996; Revised: June 8, 1998.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-573-401 et seq.

CROSS REFERENCES
AEA: Standards Based Education; IA: Instructional Goals and Learning Objectives; IL: Evaluation of Instructional Programs and subcodes; KB: Parent Involvement in Education.

This policy contains no provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, automated decision systems, algorithms, or artificial intelligence tools.

## IGF-R — Curriculum Review

YEAR ONE: MATERIALS ADOPTION — MASTER STUDY, INITIAL STAGE
The curriculum specialist must inform all stakeholders of the initiation of the process and that communication will continue through the study; create a communication plan involving appropriate individuals and groups throughout the process; determine study participants and define their respective roles; select the method for compensating those involved (stipend, release-time, graduate credit, other); and prepare a preliminary timeline.

FOUNDATION STAGE
Conduct foundational work including comprehensive data analysis from preceding years and examination of stakeholder-identified issues. Contact affected parties including curriculum coordinating personnel, principals, community, teachers, and the curriculum study committee. Review research, trends, and best practices. Develop or review philosophy, beliefs, and standards for the curriculum area, aligned with district philosophy and beliefs. Perform internal analysis of current curriculum documenting strengths (qualities enabling standards achievement) and weaknesses (characteristics restricting standards achievement, including gaps and redundancies). Conduct external analysis examining social, political, demographic, economic, and technological impacts on students. Identify critical issues regarding funding, space, support, and maintenance. Assess foundation stage effectiveness.

MATERIALS SELECTION/DEVELOPMENT STAGE
Identify student expectations — state what the student will be able to do as a result of participating in the program. Identify essential components including content and teaching strategies. Determine sequence of material selection activities: survey available materials, consider alternatives, narrow possibilities, conduct on-site trials at every level affected, assess trials, select materials for purchase or development, develop assessment tools, seek approval, and plan staff development. Assess development stage.

YEAR TWO — INITIAL IMPLEMENTATION STAGE
The curriculum coordinator with department chairs and teachers implement review processes: provide staff development for implementation; select implementation approach (pilot in several classrooms for modifications, or move to full district-wide implementation if uncomplicated); refine student expectations; refine assessment tools and gather baseline data on student achievement; assess initial implementation and modify accordingly; identify concern areas; initiate program monitoring procedures; address school-to-career, technology, and diversity infusion.

YEAR THREE
Continue gathering student achievement data; continue developing appropriate assessment strategies; monitor standards through assessment, and modify and support as necessary; continue staff development; continue identifying improvement areas; examine curriculum for strengths and weaknesses; begin data analysis; identify additional needed data; monitor school-to-career, technology, and diversity infusion procedures.

YEAR FOUR
Continue Year Three processes; use assessment data and other data to do program evaluation; share data and data analysis with stakeholders.

YEARS FIVE THROUGH SEVEN
Years Five and Six continue prior activities; Year Six includes communicating with stakeholders about materials selection and researching trends and best practices. Year Seven includes intense review of assessment data, research trends, and current curriculum, and reviewing all standards and benchmarks.

This policy contains no provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, or predictive tools.

## IHA — Instructional Program

INSTRUCTION — STANDARDS FOR ALL DISTRICT SCHOOLS
Instructional strategies shall reflect best practices and stimulate student engagement, and the District requires integration of appropriate technology to enhance curricular outcomes. Assessment requirements include both formative and summative components used to ensure quality learning and to inform teachers and teams regarding curricular and instructional decisionmaking. Curriculum, instructional practice and assessment shall recognize and accommodate individual differences, interests and abilities, while maintaining commitment to continuous improvement and closing achievement gaps. For comprehensive high schools, each master schedule shall provide students with the opportunity to take at least eight (8) different courses for credit each year.

PRINCIPAL RESPONSIBILITIES
Principals must ensure staff utilize evidence-based instructional strategies, assessment and data-driven decisionmaking, and build staff capacity through professional growth in instruction and assessment areas.

TEACHER RESPONSIBILITIES
Teachers shall modify instruction based on student performance on assessments and use formative and summative state and District assessments to diagnose student needs in order to modify instructional strategies and improve student achievement.

ASSESSMENT AND EVALUATION
The District establishes targets to reduce achievement gaps in student performance related to ethnicity, gender, disability and limited English proficiency while holding high expectations for all students. The evaluation process uses classroom, schoolwide and Districtwide formative and common summative assessments to inform instructional decisions and program modifications.

No provisions regarding automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, or predictive tools appear in this policy.

## IHAAA — School-Sponsored Student Publications

PURPOSE AND SCOPE
School-sponsored student publications serve to provide guided instructional experiences in reporting, writing, editing, and understanding English, and responsible journalism. Newspapers additionally disseminate school-related information.

PROHIBITED EXPRESSION
Students are prohibited from publishing: obscene expression; libelous, slanderous, or defamatory expression under state law; false expression regarding any person; expression creating clear and present danger of the commission of unlawful acts or material disruption to school operations; expression violating others' privacy rights; expression violating lawful school regulations maintaining educational environments.

INSTRUCTOR RESPONSIBILITIES
The publications instructor directs the learning experience, teaches responsible expression and professional standards, and may assign work or delegate content decisions to student editors subject to review and approval. Instructors must develop editorial policy guidelines addressing profanity, advertising, confidentiality, privacy, deaths, and letters to the editor, reviewed yearly.

REQUIRED DISCLAIMER
All publications must contain a disclaimer stating student expression is not an expression of the District or of District policy and that the District is immune from liability.

DISTRIBUTION COORDINATION
The principal coordinates time, place, and manner of distribution to minimize instructional conflicts.

REVIEW AND APPEAL PROCEDURES
Staff notifying administrators of prohibited expression triggers an informal hearing where students and instructors present views without legal representation. The principal issues a written decision specifying violated rules. Appeals proceed to the superintendent, then potentially to the Board.

LEGAL REFERENCE
C.R.S. 22-1-120.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, assessment-based placement, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IHAM — Health Education

COMPREHENSIVE HEALTH EDUCATION PROGRAM
The district commits to providing health education covering physical activity, nutrition, personal health and fitness, human growth and development, hereditary and developmental conditions, community and environmental health, consumer health, substance use, communicable diseases, mental and emotional health, family life/sex education, high-risk behaviors, and injury prevention. The curriculum and materials to be used in the District's comprehensive health education program shall be made available for public inspection during school hours. Public comment is required before implementing substantial new or revised curriculum.

Parents must receive written notice before each health education unit, including: content overview, curriculum inspection information, and notification that they may request written exemption from some or all of the comprehensive health education program on the grounds that it is contrary to the religious beliefs and teachings of the child. Students receive alternative assignments for excused portions.

FAMILY LIFE/SEX EDUCATION
Parents/guardians are primarily responsible for assisting their children to develop responsible behaviors and attitudes concerning family life and human sexuality. Schools supplement parental efforts through factual instruction and discussion. The District shall maintain content standards for any planned curriculum that includes instruction concerning human sexuality based on scientific research, as required by Colorado law. Written notice must precede such instruction, detailing topics and providing exemption rights with alternative assignments.

HIV/AIDS EDUCATION
Education covers transmission, risk behaviors, and prevention strategies at developmentally appropriate levels. Parents receive written notice and exemption options.

ELEMENTARY SCHOOL PHYSICAL ACTIVITY REQUIREMENTS
Full-day students must have opportunities for a minimum of 600 minutes of physical activity per month, and half-day students 300 minutes of physical activity per month. Accommodations apply for medical or physical limitations.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IHBA — Abbreviated School Day

DEFINITIONS
Abbreviated School Day encompasses instruction or educational services lasting fewer hours than peers in the same grade and school, whether planned or unplanned. Abbreviated School Day Schedule constitutes a designed and approved plan by the IEP or 504 team for regularly providing fewer instructional hours than majority peers in the same grade and school. Student with a disability includes those determined eligible under IDEA, Section 504, or for whom the District has received evaluation requests under either statute.

PLACEMENT CIRCUMSTANCES
Students with disabilities may be placed on abbreviated schedules when: the IEP or 504 team determines the schedule is necessary to provide free appropriate public education (FAPE) in the least restrictive environment (LRE) based on individualized needs; or the student has met graduation requirements and receives post-secondary transition services. Placement cannot occur based on administrative convenience or a lack of resources, including staffing availability, waiting lists, facilities access, or related services availability.

INITIAL PLACEMENT REQUIREMENTS — PROCEDURAL SAFEGUARDS AND TEAM DETERMINATION
Prior to meetings discussing abbreviated schedules, parents must receive applicable procedural safeguards notices. The IEP or 504 team must determine appropriateness based on unique disability-related needs and document how FAPE will be achieved and whether the schedule impacts least restrictive environment placement.

REQUIRED DOCUMENTED COMPONENTS
The IEP or 504 plan must address: how the schedule supports return to full-day attendance, including stages for gradual reintroduction, unless the team documents that gradual reintroduction is inappropriate due to circumstances like degenerative medical conditions; how the schedule ensures progress toward IEP goals and general education curriculum advancement; specified instructional hours, related services, and percentage of school year on abbreviated schedule; measurement methodology for progress toward IEP goals and benchmarks; expected return date to full-day schedule based on unique needs.

ADDITIONAL REQUIRED DOCUMENTATION
The plan must include: daily school schedule specifications; team justification for the abbreviated schedule; timeline for IEP or 504 team review; appropriate contact point for policy violation concerns; documentation that parents received procedural safeguard information; parent's informed written consent if the abbreviated schedule is disconnected from the FAPE offer.

PRIOR WRITTEN NOTICE REQUIREMENTS
For IEP students, initial placement cannot use the IEP amendment process. Prior written notice must include: supports, services, and alternatives that have been provided or considered before placing the student on abbreviated schedule; outcomes and justification for the abbreviated schedule.

PARENT DISPUTE REMEDIES
When parents disagree that an abbreviated schedule is necessary for FAPE, they may pursue existing remedies: for IEP students, requesting mediation, filing state complaints, or pursuing due process; for 504 students, filing Office for Civil Rights complaints.

ABBREVIATED SCHEDULE NOT CONNECTED TO FAPE
If an abbreviated schedule is not connected to the FAPE offer and is not a permissible disciplinary removal, the school must obtain informed and written consent from the student's parent/guardian prior to implementing the schedule. Parents may revoke consent in writing at any time. Requests must use language and format that is accessible to the parent/guardian.

REVIEW SCHEDULE
The IEP or 504 team must review the abbreviated schedule within 30 calendar days of placement, unless the District and parent agree otherwise at the initial meeting. Subsequent review frequency must be documented in the plan; schedules exceeding 30 calendar days require parent agreement. Regardless of parent agreement, annual review is mandatory. During reviews, teams must discuss progress toward IEP goals and stages described by the team for gradual reintroduction. If expected progress is not occurring, the team must consider adjusting the supports and services provided to ensure progress.

ENROLLMENT, SCHEDULE, ATTENDANCE, AND PARTICIPATION
High school students with disabilities voluntarily enrolling in reduced class loads or part-time status consistent with nondisabled peers, or those whose parents voluntarily enrolled them part-time (including dually enrolled students), are not considered on abbreviated schedules. Students placed on abbreviated schedules may not be considered truant or chronically absent based solely on the Abbreviated School Day Schedule. Students on abbreviated schedules should not be determined ineligible to participate in field trips, school functions, and extracurricular activities based solely on the Abbreviated School Day Schedule.

SCHOOL DISCIPLINE AND ABBREVIATED DAYS
When schools shorten a student's day due to behavioral concerns, this must be counted as a disciplinary removal, regardless of whether the student is formally suspended. This includes: requesting parent pickup before the school day ends due to behavior; teachers excluding students from class due to behavior; administrators unilaterally determining abbreviated attendance due to behavior. These requirements apply even when parents agreed to early pickup due to behavioral concerns, but do not apply when parents independently requested early pickup. Partial disciplinary removals must be accurately recorded and tracked to ensure the student with a disability receives the disciplinary protections under IDEA or Section 504. Nothing prohibits schools from disciplining students for conduct violations, provided discipline complies with District policy and IDEA or Section 504 protections.

LEGAL REFERENCES
20 U.S.C. 1401 et seq. (Individuals with Disabilities Education Act); 29 U.S.C. 701 et seq. (Section 504 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973); C.R.S. 22-20-123 (Abbreviated School Days); 1 CCR 301-8 (Rules for the Administration of the Exceptional Children's Educational Act).

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, or predictive tools appear in this policy.

## IHBG — Home-Based Education

NOTIFICATION AND ENROLLMENT REQUIREMENTS
Parents/guardians must submit written notification of the establishment of the program to the assistant director of student outreach 14 days prior to starting. Annual renotification is required if the program continues. Written certification must include the name, age, place of residence and number of hours of attendance of each child enrolled. These requirements apply only to children ages 6-15.

PRIOR TRUANCY RESTRICTION
Students with habitual truancy in the six months before proposed home-based enrollment face an additional barrier. Such students cannot enroll unless parents first submit a written description of the curriculum to be used in the program along with standard notification.

RECORD MAINTENANCE
Parents must maintain permanent records including attendance data, test and evaluation results and immunization records. Records must be produced to the assistant director upon 14 days' written notice if the superintendent has probable cause of non-compliance.

ASSESSMENT REQUIREMENTS AT SPECIFIED GRADES
Each child participating in the program shall be evaluated when he or she reaches grades three, five, seven, nine and eleven through either nationally standardized achievement testing or evaluation by a qualified person as defined by law. Results must be submitted to the district or to an independent/parochial school (with school name reported to the district).

STANDARDIZED TEST SCORE THRESHOLDS
Children scoring above the 13th percentile shall continue to be exempt from compulsory school attendance. Scores at or below the 13th percentile allow parents to request retesting using alternate approved tests.

QUALIFIED EVALUATOR STANDARD
Evaluations by qualified persons showing sufficient academic progress according to his or her ability allow continued exemption from compulsory attendance.

REMEDIATION REQUIREMENT
If retest scores remain at or below the 13th percentile or qualified evaluation shows insufficient progress, the District shall require the parent/guardian to enroll the child in a public, independent or parochial school until the next testing period.

PARTIAL ENROLLMENT OPTIONS
Home-based students may: enroll in PSD Options School; enroll in District school classes on space-available basis if generating at least 0.5 FTE per-pupil funding; or remain exclusively in home-based education.

INSTRUCTIONAL MATERIALS ACCESS
Access to District textbooks and materials is limited based on enrollment: Options School enrollees access the lending library only; District class enrollees access materials for enrolled classes only; exclusively home-based students receive no District material access.

EXTRACURRICULAR PARTICIPATION
A child in a nonpublic home-based educational program may participate in District extracurricular and interscholastic activities as provided by law and District policy.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-33-104.5; C.R.S. 22-33-107.

Note: standardized test percentile scores (13th percentile threshold) are used as a scored cutoff determining continued exemption from compulsory attendance versus mandated enrollment in a public, independent, or parochial school; no automated/algorithmic/AI system is mentioned — the process relies on standardized test scoring and human evaluator judgment.

## IHCFA — Elementary-Based Child Care

POLICY OVERVIEW
Poudre School District may discretionarily offer child care services at elementary schools using either district personnel or properly licensed outside providers.

CONTRACTING PROCEDURES — REQUEST FOR PROPOSALS
The District's Student Services and Facilities Departments, consulting with the relevant school principal, shall prepare and advertise a request for proposals (RFP) for the provision of child care services at the designated elementary school.

EVALUATION AND SELECTION
The director of student services, director of facilities, and elementary school principal jointly evaluate proposals with assistance from Purchasing and Materials Management. Following this collaborative assessment, the principal shall select the provider to whom a contract will be awarded for the provision of child care services.

CONTRACT REQUIREMENTS
Selected providers must sign a written contract with the District before providing any child care services, which must incorporate a schedule of the provider's fees for providing the child care services.

RFP FREQUENCY
Unless the District discontinues offering child care services or transitions to district personnel, it shall prepare and advertise an RFP for such services no less frequently than once every five (5) years.

LEGAL REFERENCE
C.R.S. 26-6-101 et seq.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class rankings, diplomas, assessment scoring for placement, algorithms, or automated decision systems appear in this policy.

## IJ — Instructional Resources and Materials

BOARD RESPONSIBILITY AND DELEGATION
The Board of Education maintains legal responsibility for approving instructional and library materials but delegates selection authority to district professional personnel per established policies. The Board officially approves textbooks and required curriculum materials upon recommendation of the superintendent or designee.

MATERIAL DEFINITIONS
Textbooks are defined as the major information resource(s) and bound materials provided in multiple copies for use by a total class or a major portion of such a class. Required curriculum materials encompass print and non-print resources such as computer programs, maps, kits, audiovisual materials and teaching tools, which are required to supplement the planned curriculum.

SELECTION STANDARDS
All textbooks and instructional materials must be integral to the district's instructional programs and supportive of its vision and educational standards for all students.

SELECTION PROCEDURES
The assistant superintendent of school services holds primary responsibility for establishing review and selection processes. Selection procedures will include appropriate input from curriculum specialists, teachers, administrators, parents, and community members in the review and recommendation process.

VARIANCE PROCESS
Districts wishing to deviate from approved textbooks or curriculum materials must apply for a variance through the assistant superintendent of school services.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 22-1-104(2); C.R.S. 22-32-109(1)(t); C.R.S. 22-32-110(1)(o)-(r); C.R.S. 22-54-105(1).

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IJ-AR — Instructional Resources and Materials

PURPOSE
District professionals and citizens review and recommend learning resources serving as major information sources for standards-based instruction, with formal adoption by the Board of Education.

PROCEDURE — COMMITTEE FORMATION
The director of curriculum and instruction directs the curriculum specialist to establish a curriculum selection committee with defined formal review processes.

COMMITTEE COMPOSITION
The committee functions as a subcommittee of the Instructional Improvement Committee (IIC) and includes: classroom teachers, school administrators, library media specialists, special education teachers, parents, citizens, and purchasing department representatives.

REVIEW PROCESS ELEMENTS
The review process encompasses: evaluating currently-used materials to determine retention versus replacement; surveying new published products, with the chairperson collecting samples and information; developing or revising evaluation standards and forms specific to curriculum areas; professional staff narrowing selections to materials meeting district standards and adhering to district policies of non-bias and nondiscrimination; testing selected materials through classroom situations using methods such as the Connie Muther blind review procedure; the committee documenting results on appropriate district forms; the committee chair, textbook budget officer, and purchasing officer negotiating vendor costs; the committee communicating findings to principals and the director; the committee presenting findings to the IIC (composed of department chairs/content representatives); the Selection Committee and IIC making final recommendations to the curriculum director; the curriculum director and selection committee representatives presenting recommendations to the Board of Education for approval.

POST-ADOPTION PROCEDURES
The director sends adoption notification to the procurement manager indicating approved texts and purchasable materials; principals receive lists designating district-purchased versus school-purchased items.

PROCUREMENT AND DELIVERY
Procurement and warehouse managers coordinate with curriculum coordinators for purchase and delivery; the procurement manager negotiates vendor agreements.

RECEIPT AND DISTRIBUTION
Upon receipt, orders are verified, inventoried, bar-coded, and distributed to appropriate sites.

Approval Date: May 30, 1997.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IJ-R — Instructional Resources and Materials

DISTRICT TEXTBOOK BUDGET USES
The district textbook budget finances: all newly adopted textbooks approved by the Board of Education; additional copies of adopted textbooks needed to serve student growth; consumable instructional materials deemed necessary through adoption processes for required courses used regularly by all students (such as workbooks replacing traditional textbooks); teacher guides and instructor editions of Board-adopted textbooks; replacement copies for damaged or lost textbooks and materials.

SCHOOL AND DEPARTMENTAL BUDGET USES
School and departmental budgets may cover: extra quantities of Board-adopted textbooks beyond growth needs; supplemental texts, approved materials, and pamphlets not part of formal adoption (paperback classroom books, unit-specific pamphlets, supplemental items like test masters); supplemental materials supporting adopted curriculum but representing individual teacher choices; consumable items becoming student property (portfolios, lab manuals); supplementary materials as defined in BOE Policy IJK, except when integral to new curriculum adoption — district textbook funds support start-up phases, with school budgets maintaining programs thereafter; textbooks upgraded to new editions by school choice rather than district mandate.

STUDENT CHARGES
Supplies and materials may be charged to students per Board of Education Policy JQ.

CROSS REFERENCES
IJK (Supplementary Materials); JQ (Student Fees).

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IJK — Supplementary Materials

DEFINITION
Supplementary materials encompass any hard-copy, digital or other instructional materials (including assessments) beyond core curriculum materials. These materials span conventional and electronic formats: books, periodicals, newspapers, pictures, diagrams, maps, charts, slides, films, records, audio and/or visual media, computer programs, instructional websites and online subscriptions. The policy explicitly excludes information technology as defined in District Policy EHA.

PRINCIPAL RESPONSIBILITIES
Principals hold accountability for all supplementary materials deployed at their schools and must ensure that they appropriately support the approved curriculum for each grade level, program and class in which they are used.

SELECTION AND APPROVAL PROCESS
While principals may delegate initial selection duties to other administrators or teachers, the selection and acquisition of supplementary materials at each school shall be subject to approval by the principal, assistant superintendent of student achievement and superintendent.

TEACHER USE AND EXPENSES
Educators are encouraged to employ diverse learning aids provided expenses remain within building budgets or are charged to students as authorized by District Policy JQ.

Adoption and Revision Dates: Adopted May 12, 1997; Revised March 24, 2015.

Legal Reference: C.R.S. 22-32-109(1)(t).

Note: the definition of supplementary materials explicitly includes "assessments" among covered instructional materials subject to principal/superintendent approval, but no automated decision system, algorithm, AI, machine learning, or predictive tool is mentioned.

## IJL — Library Materials Selection and Adoptions

PURPOSE AND FOUNDATIONAL PRINCIPLES
The Poudre School District R-1 Library Media Technology Centers provide resources in multiple formats to support curriculum and meet student and staff educational needs. The district adopts the American Library Association's Library Bill of Rights and the American Association of School Librarians' School Library Bill of Rights for School Library Media Programs as guiding philosophies.

SELECTION CRITERIA
Media selection shall address six key objectives: implementing and enriching the curriculum; helping students develop information access and usage skills; helping students develop personal codes of conduct; stimulating imagination, creativity, and vision through individual inquiry; encouraging critical thinking; providing pleasure during leisure time.

SELECTION AUTHORITY AND PROCESS
Building principals delegate material selection responsibility to licensed media specialists. While teachers, administrators, students, and site teams may recommend materials, the responsibility for the selection decision will rest with the media specialist applying professional collection development standards.

CONTENT CONSIDERATIONS
Materials addressing controversial subjects may be included when language, sexual content, or violence are integral to plot development or accurate reporting, provided such treatment avoids purposefully or sensationally exploited presentation.

VIDEO RATING GUIDELINES
PG-13 videos require no curricular justification for viewers 13+; R-rated content requires curricular objectives and parental permission slips for students under 17. R-rated materials are prohibited for elementary and middle school students. NC-17 and X-rated videos are not permitted.

GIFT MATERIALS
Donated materials must meet selection criteria; donors assume responsibility for valuation.

LEGAL REFERENCE
C.R.S. 22-32-110(1)(r).

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IJOA — Field Trips and Other Activities Away from School

OVERVIEW AND DEFINITIONS
The Poudre School District recognizes educational value in student participation in field trips and related activities. The policy defines covered activities as: enrichment and experiential educational activities (with or without course credit), extracurricular practices and competitions, and school-sponsored social, experiential, or fundraising activities.

RULES APPLICABLE TO ALL FIELD TRIPS AND ACTIVITIES — PERMISSION AND ELIGIBILITY
A District permission form must be signed by the parent or guardian of a student before the student may participate. Only current District students qualify, though recently graduated students may participate in activities they earned during enrollment.

STUDENTS WITH DISABILITIES
Determinations regarding the appropriateness of a field trip/activity, supervision requirements, necessary accommodations and/or modifications, and other matters concerning students with disabilities shall be made by the students' IEP or Section 504 team.

CHAPERONES AND SUPERVISION
Adult chaperones must be District employees or authorized volunteers, qualified and registered under District Policy KJ.

DISTRICT AUTHORITY
The District reserves the right to deny any request for a field trip/activity, to cancel any previously approved field trip/activity up to the time of departure, and to terminate or redirect any field trip/activity in progress for any reason deemed necessary or appropriate.

TRANSPORTATION
District vehicles, private vehicles, or commercial transportation may be used. Private vehicle drivers must hold valid licenses, acceptable insurance, and District approval.

CONDUCT STANDARDS
Students, employees, and volunteers remain subject to District policies and regulations, including but not limited to policies and regulations included in the Student Code of Conduct, on every field trip/activity.

RULES FOR NON-OVERNIGHT ACTIVITIES
The school principal approves each activity on District forms after consulting the risk manager regarding appropriateness and transportation modes. The principal designates a District employee sponsor with primary responsibility and determines required chaperone numbers and qualifications.

RULES FOR OVERNIGHT ACTIVITIES — APPROVAL AUTHORITY
An assistant superintendent (elementary or secondary, as applicable) approves overnight activities on District forms, including the content of a safety and emergency response plan for the field trip/activity, after risk manager consultation.

DESIGNATED ROLES
The assistant superintendent approves both a sponsor (primary responsibility) and a safety coordinator (a District employee who completes required training). At least one adult chaperone of the same sex shall be assigned for any male and female students participating.

INTERNATIONAL TRAVEL
Sponsors must register groups in the Smart Traveler Enrollment Program through the US State Department. All students must purchase the insurance offered by the educational tour company or travel agency, or other District-approved insurance.

MISCONDUCT PROVISION
Permission forms must include language allowing early termination of participation and sending students home at parental expense for serious or repeated misconduct.

LEGAL REFERENCES
C.R.S. 13-22-107.

CROSS REFERENCES
EEAG (Student Transportation in Private Vehicles), JQ (Student Fees, Fines and Charges), KJ (Volunteers).

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, curriculum placement, assessment-based decisions, automated scoring systems, algorithms, or artificial intelligence tools appear in this policy.

## IJOA-R — Field Trips

PROCEDURES FOR NON-OVERNIGHT FIELD TRIPS/ACTIVITIES — REQUEST AND APPROVAL PROCESS
Staff proposing field trips without overnight stays must submit a District request form to the principal with sufficient advance notice. The principal evaluates the form, potentially consulting the risk manager, then either approves as proposed, approves with required changes, or denies the activity in writing.

APPROVAL SPECIFICATIONS
When approved, the principal designates: the District employee who will serve as the field trip/activity sponsor; the number and qualifications of adult chaperones required for student supervision; and the mode(s) of transportation to be used.

PERMISSION FORMS
Before the activity occurs, the sponsor must obtain District permission forms signed by parents or guardians of all participating students. The sponsor reviews forms for completeness, carries originals, leaves copies with the principal, and maintains originals at school for at least three years.

INJURY PROCEDURES
If any student sustains injury during the activity or transportation, the sponsor forwards the original signed permission form and completed District student accident report to the risk manager.

CHSAA ACTIVITIES EXCEPTION
Activities away from school scheduled through the Colorado High School Activities Association (CHSAA) that do not involve an overnight stay shall be deemed to be approved by the District's school principals.

PROCEDURES FOR OVERNIGHT FIELD TRIPS/ACTIVITIES — INITIAL SUBMISSION
Staff must submit a District request form with a proposed safety and emergency response plan and a detailed proposed itinerary that includes all destinations, mode(s) of transportation to be used, lodging information, and planned or anticipated activities.

PRINCIPAL REVIEW
The principal evaluates materials and either forwards them to the risk manager or denies the proposal in writing.

RISK MANAGER EVALUATION
The risk manager reviews all materials, consults with the principal regarding itinerary and any health, safety and/or liability concerns, and coordinates changes before forwarding to the assistant superintendent.

RISK MANAGER RECOMMENDATIONS
The risk manager forwards documentation to the appropriate assistant superintendent with recommendations regarding whether the field trip/activity should be approved, and if so, requirements for addressing any remaining itinerary, health, safety and/or liability concerns.

ASSISTANT SUPERINTENDENT APPROVAL
The assistant superintendent approves as proposed, with changes, or denies in writing. Approvals specify: the District employee who shall serve as the sponsor; the District employee who shall serve as the safety coordinator; the content of the safety and emergency response plan; the number and qualifications of adult chaperones required for student supervision; and the mode(s) of transportation to be used.

NOTIFICATION AND DOCUMENTATION
The assistant superintendent notifies the risk manager and principal. The risk manager notifies the school nurse and provides relevant documents for health and safety advising.

SAFETY COORDINATOR TRAINING
The designated safety coordinator shall complete all required trainings before the activity occurs.

PERMISSION AND HEALTH FORMS
Approximately 45 days before departure, the risk manager sends a field trip packet containing forms requiring parent/guardian signatures: overnight release and indemnity forms (with power of attorney for out-of-state trips) and emergency contact/health information forms. The sponsor reviews, carries originals, leaves copies with the principal, and maintains originals for at least three years.

INJURY PROCEDURES (OVERNIGHT)
If injury occurs during the activity or transportation, the sponsor forwards the original signed permission form and completed District student accident report to the risk manager.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, curriculum placement, participation eligibility based on assessment scores, instructional material selection, or automated decision systems/algorithms appear in this policy.

## IKC — Grade Point Averages/Class Rankings

APPLICABILITY
This policy applies to students graduating in 2028-2029 or later, and those enrolling in ninth grade during 2025-2026 or thereafter.

GRADE POINT AVERAGE CALCULATION
4.0 Scale Conversion: letter grades convert as follows: A = 4 points; B = 3 points; C = 2 points; D = 1 point; and F, WF (Withdraw Failing) and IE (Insufficient Evidence) = 0 points.

WEIGHTED GPA FOR ADVANCED COURSES
Advanced Placement, International Baccalaureate, and Concurrent/Dual Enrollment college courses receive enhanced point values: A=5, B=4, C=3, D=2, F=0 (compared to unweighted equivalents of 4, 3, 2, 1, 0).

COURSE WITHDRAWAL PROVISIONS
Students dropping courses after established deadlines receive automatic WF grades counted in GPA calculations, except with principal approval. Withdrawals before deadlines receive W grades excluded from GPA calculations.

DECILE-BASED CLASS RANKING
Class rank divides students into ten equal groups using weighted GPA. The top 10% occupy the first decile, the next 10% the second decile, and so forth, reflecting relative academic performance.

RECALCULATION REQUIREMENTS
Both weighted and unweighted GPAs and class rank are cumulative, recalculated after each grading term beginning in ninth grade.

Note: this policy establishes a formulaic, rules-based (non-AI) calculation method for GPA weighting and decile-based class ranking that directly determines students' academic standing; no automated decision system, algorithm (in the AI/ML sense), artificial intelligence, machine learning, or predictive tool is referenced — the "calculation" is a fixed arithmetic formula, not a learned/predictive model.

## IKF-2017 — Graduation and Diploma Requirements

POLICY SCOPE
This policy applies to students who enter the 9th grade for the first time in the 2017-2018 school year and thereafter.

GRADUATION REQUIREMENTS
Students must meet or exceed the District's academic standards and measures, including College and Career Readiness Measures in English and Mathematics, plus PSD Core Credit Requirements.

COLLEGE AND CAREER READINESS MEASURES
Students must meet or exceed cut scores on one English measure and one Mathematics measure selected from these approved options: ACT assessment, SAT assessment, ACT WorkKeys assessment, Advanced Placement assessment, International Baccalaureate assessment, ASVAB (Armed Services Vocational Aptitude Battery), Concurrent Enrollment Course, District Capstone, Accuplacer assessment, Industry Certificate. The District provides access to the English and Mathematics SAT assessment during the students' 11th grade year at no cost. Other measures' costs fall to students unless fees are waived in accordance with District Policy JQ. Students must develop an Individual Career Academic Plan, which includes a review of graduation requirements, career exploration, and specific student course selection.

PSD CORE CREDIT REQUIREMENTS
Total of 240 credits across disciplines: Mathematics & Computer Science 30 credits; Science 30 credits; Language Arts 40 credits; Social Studies 25 credits; Humanities 5 credits; World Language or World Culture 10 credits; Fine and Applied Arts 10 credits; Wellness 15 credits; Financial Literacy 5 credits; Economics 5 credits; Electives 65 credits. International Baccalaureate program students fulfill requirements through a prescribed IB course of study with standards meeting or exceeding outlined requirements.

GRADUATION COURSES TAUGHT IN MIDDLE SCHOOL
Students receive credit for approved middle school courses upon earning a passing grade. Credit-bearing courses must use District-approved curriculum with District-adopted summative assessment. Partial credit is not awarded for completing one semester of a two-semester sequence in middle school. Parents may decline high school graduation credit for approved middle school courses at any time from the first day of the student's 9th grade year through the last day of the student's 9th grade year. Once declined, the grade record removal is permanent and non-reversible.

ENDORSEMENT CATEGORIES — POUDRE SCHOOL DISTRICT ENDORSEMENT OF ACADEMIC MERIT
Award requirements include: maintain a 3.6 cumulative grade point average or higher; receive credit for the PSD Algebra 2 course or higher; earn at least 30 credits in an Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB) or Post-Secondary (PS) course.

POUDRE SCHOOL DISTRICT ENDORSEMENT OF POSTSECONDARY SUCCESS
Requirement: complete a certificated program from a community college and/or an associate's degree.

POUDRE SCHOOL DISTRICT ENDORSEMENT OF BILITERACY
Requirements include demonstrating proficiency or higher in one or more world languages and in English.

CERTIFICATE CATEGORIES — CERTIFICATE OF CIVIC EDUCATION OR MERITORIOUS SERVICE
Requirements: 200 or more Civic Education Volunteer hours or Service Learning (SL) volunteer hours; participated in at least four extracurricular activities throughout high school; completed a Capstone Project.

HIGH SCHOOL CERTIFICATE OF ATTENDANCE
Awarded to students who have not satisfied the requirements for high school graduation but have remained enrolled and continued their education in the District until age 21.

Adopted: January 24, 2017. Revised: June 13, 2017; March 26, 2019.

Note: this policy uses a specific cumulative grade point average threshold (3.6 GPA) and standardized-assessment cut scores as gating criteria for graduation endorsements; no automated decision system, algorithm, AI, machine learning, or predictive tool is mentioned.

## IKF-2025 — Graduation and Diploma Requirements

GRADUATION REQUIREMENTS
To obtain a high school diploma from Poudre School District, students entering 9th grade for the first time in 2025-2026 or later must satisfy academic standards encompassing: (1) College and Career Readiness Measures in Reading, Writing, and Communicating; Mathematics; and (2) PSD Core Credit Requirements.

COLLEGE AND CAREER READINESS MEASURES
Students must demonstrate competency by meeting or exceeding cut scores on one approved Reading, Writing, and Communicating measure and one Mathematics measure, or complete an alternative College and Career Readiness pathway. The district provides, at no cost to students, access to the English and Mathematics SAT assessment during the students' 11th grade year. Other assessment costs are borne by students unless waived per District Policy JQ and the Board-Adopted Student Fee Schedule.

Approved measures include: Accuplacer, ACT, ACT WorkKeys, Advanced Placement, ASVAB, SAT, Concurrent Enrollment Courses, District Capstone, Industry Certificates, and International Baccalaureate assessments. Cut scores follow Colorado State Board of Education standards with locally approved criteria detailed in administrative guidelines. Students may select any combination of measures to satisfy requirements.

All students must develop an Individual Career Academic Plan, which includes a review of graduation requirements, career exploration, and specific student course selection.

PSD CORE CREDIT REQUIREMENTS
Students must complete 240 total credits distributed as follows: Mathematics & Computer Science 30 credits (including algebra and geometry; Algebra II recommended for four-year college); Science 30 credits (physical, life, earth system sciences; Chemistry/Physics recommended); Language Arts 40 credits (oral expression, listening, reading, writing, research, reasoning); Social Studies 30 credits (geography, civics, history, economics; must include World History, U.S. History, Civics); Fine and Applied Arts 10 credits (original products, artifacts, performing, critical/creative problem-solving); Wellness 10 credits (physical and personal wellness); Financial Literacy 5 credits (personal financial literacy skills); Additional Coursework 85 credits.

PSD RECOMMENDED ADDITIONAL CREDITS
The district recommends but does not require completion of credits in: World Language (10-30), Health Curriculum (5), Geography (10), Humanities (5), and Economics (5). These shall not impede a student from earning their high school diploma if they are not completed.

GRADUATION COURSES TAUGHT IN MIDDLE SCHOOL
Students receive high school graduation credit for approved middle school courses upon earning a passing grade. District-approved curriculum or equivalent accredited coursework is required; partial credit shall not be awarded for completing one semester of a two-semester sequence in middle school. Parents may opt out of graduation credit designation through the student's 9th grade year, with grade record removal becoming permanent and non-reversible once declined.

ELIGIBILITY FOR LEARNERS WITH DIVERSE BACKGROUNDS — STUDENTS WITH DISABILITIES
The district ensures access to all graduation pathways and standard diploma opportunity regardless of alternative state assessment participation. A student's Individualized Education Plan (IEP) describes course sequencing, specially designed instruction, accommodations, and modifications enabling competency demonstration. Students on 504 Plans and IEPs access allowable accommodations on competency demonstrations.

MULTILINGUAL LEARNERS
Students identified for English Language Development (ELD) programs who arrived in the U.S. in 8th grade or later and were classified as Non-English proficient may follow an alternate pathway. ELD courses may contribute to fulfillment of English Language Arts, World Language, or other graduation requirements. Immigrant students lacking prior transcripts receive an equitable credit process recognizing prior learning.

WAIVERS OF GRADUATION REQUIREMENTS
Schools may request waivers for senior-year requirements per assistant superintendent guidelines. For students with disabilities, IEP teams may seek waivers if determined in the student's best educational interest or necessary to provide Free Appropriate Public Education (FAPE). Waivers require approval by the assistant superintendent or designee and the student's IEP team, with documentation in permanent special education files.

ENDORSEMENT CATEGORIES
District endorsements align with Colorado Department of Education categories and requirements.

Adopted: April 9, 2024.

CROSS REFERENCES
IKC (Grade Point Averages/Class Ranking); IKFB (Graduation Exercises).

Note: this policy makes graduation and diploma eligibility contingent on meeting or exceeding numeric "cut scores" on standardized assessments (SAT, ACT, Accuplacer, ACT WorkKeys, ASVAB, AP, IB, etc.) — a scoring-based eligibility determination — but contains no explicit references to automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, or predictive tools.

## IKFB — Graduation Exercises

GRADUATION EXERCISES
Completion of high school diploma requirements merits public recognition. Each graduating senior's achievement receives acknowledgment through a publicly-celebrated graduation exercise. High schools develop their own graduation exercises collaboratively with faculty and the senior class. While graduating students may be asked to contribute fees toward graduation expenses, no student shall be barred from participating in the exercises because of inability to pay the fees.

The graduation program maintains a secular character. Poudre School District preserves neutrality regarding student religious expressions during graduation. Specifically, the program shall not include any school-sponsored or student lead prayers or other religious activities.

BACCALAUREATE EXERCISES
Student groups and families may independently organize baccalaureate services of a religious nature. However, the school district shall not be identified, explicitly or implicitly, as sponsoring or endorsing such services. Attendance remains entirely voluntary, with students and personnel participating as private individuals rather than in official capacities. District funds and compensated staff time cannot support baccalaureate services. Organizations planning such services may lease school facilities under district-established terms, conditions, and fee schedules.

Adopted: May 22, 1995. Revised: March 24, 1997.

CROSS REFERENCE
KF, Community Use of School Facilities.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, assessment-based placement, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IMA — Teaching Methods

INSTRUCTIONAL APPROACH AND PROFESSIONAL DEVELOPMENT
The district's Board mandates that schools employ the best available strategies and methods for bringing about learning. Instructional personnel must remain informed about emerging pedagogical approaches nationwide and implement those showing promise for enhancing the district's learning initiatives.

EDUCATIONAL CLIMATE
An environment conducive to rational thought, free inquiry, and respect for the dignity of the individual shall be established. Students receive instruction in how to think rather than what to think, with guaranteed opportunities to identify, express, and defend their opinions without penalty or fear of reprisal or ridicule.

PERSONALIZED LEARNING FOCUS
Strategies must emphasize personalizing education through: assessment of individual learning styles, abilities, and disabilities; evaluation of distinct learning needs; and creation, execution, and review of customized learning programs for each student.

PARENTAL INVOLVEMENT AND ALTERNATIVES
The Board acknowledges that certain teaching methods may prove objectionable to parents. Parents are encouraged to raise concerns with classroom teachers early in the school year or whenever appropriate. When parent/guardians determine a student should avoid assigned methods or activities, learning alternatives may be provided. Parents retain full rights to file formal complaints challenging instructional methods, activities, or presentations.

Adopted: June 10, 1996. Legal Reference: C.R.S. 22-32-109.2.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IMBB — Student Participation in Curricular Instruction, Programs and Activities

CORE REQUIREMENT
Students are expected to participate in the District's curricular instruction, programs and activities except where authorized by law or deemed necessary for implementation of a student's education program.

COMPREHENSIVE HEALTH EDUCATION PROGRAM/HUMAN SEXUALITY
Parents/guardians may request written exemptions from comprehensive health education or human sexuality curriculum instruction when they believe such content conflicts with their religious beliefs and teachings.

PHYSICAL EDUCATION
Parents seeking to excuse children from physical education must submit written requests specifying: which curriculum portions the child cannot access; duration of inability; and reasons for inability. Principals may require documentation from licensed healthcare providers. Disagreements may be appealed to the appropriate assistant superintendent, with final appeal to the superintendent.

OTHER CURRICULAR INSTRUCTION, PROGRAMS AND ACTIVITIES
Parents may request written exemptions for other curriculum components. The principal must first consult with instructional staff and parents to explore accommodations before approving exemptions. A child shall not be excused from curricular instruction, programs or activities solely because they may expose the child to viewpoints, ideas or information deemed objectionable by parents or students. The same three-tier appeal structure applies.

CREDIT REQUIREMENTS
Exempted or excused students must still earn the credits required by District policy in order to graduate from high school.

Adoption Date: May 22, 1995. Last Revised: September 28, 2009.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, assessment-based placement, or automated/algorithmic/AI decision tools appear in this policy.

## IMDB — Flag Displays

PRIMARY PROVISIONS
The United States and Colorado flags shall be displayed on a flagstaff at the Johannsen Support Services Center and all District schools at all times during the day while school is in session, except during inclement weather, in accordance with governing state and federal law.

CLASSROOM DISPLAY
The superintendent or designee must ensure the U.S. flag is prominently and permanently displayed in each academic classroom when classes are in session, in accordance with governing state and federal law.

RESPECTFUL HANDLING
Traditional customs for flag display must be observed, with flags treated respectfully at all times.

FIRST AMENDMENT PROTECTION
District policy explicitly protects the right of employees and students to reasonably display the flag of the United States on their person, on their personal property, and/or on property under their temporary control, consistent with constitutional protections.

Adoption/Revision Dates: Adopted September 9, 1996; Revised June 26, 2006.

This policy addresses only flag display protocols and contains no provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, curriculum placement, participation eligibility, assessment scoring, instructional materials, or automated decision systems.

## IMDC — Religious Observances and Displays

GENERAL PRINCIPLES
The district maintains religious neutrality and prohibits: organized worship services by district staff; religious indoctrination or prayers in school ceremonies; and advancement of any specific religion or religion over non-religion. Religious exhibits may be displayed only as an integral part of some curricular area such as art, music, history, or literature for informational purposes and with no intent to indoctrinate. Religious music is permissible when presented for its historical, cultural, or academic value as it relates to a unit of study, but not as part of a devotional exercise, service, or celebration. Staff are prohibited from using school facilities for group prayer or worship during school hours.

SCHEDULING
Schools must consider major religious observances when scheduling picture day, open house, prom, graduation, tests, assignments, and field trips. Important events may be scheduled on major religious observances only if such scheduling is reasonably necessary to carry out the proper functioning of a school program or course of study.

ACCOMMODATION
When conflicts arise between a student's religious observances and the school's schedule of classes or activities, the religious observance takes precedence. Absences for religious observance shall not count against a student in determining exclusion, failure, or reduction of grades. Teachers must provide a meaningful opportunity and reasonable time to make up missed classwork, tests, quizzes, and final exam reviews.

CROSS REFERENCES
JH/JHB (Student Attendance/Truancy); IMDC-R (Teaching About Religion); KF (Use of District Facilities).

Note: this policy directly governs how absences affect student grades (grade reduction/failure/exclusion determinations) but contains no automated decision system, algorithm, AI, machine learning, or predictive tool references.

## IMDC-R — Teaching about Religion

INTRODUCTION
Poudre School District activities must not advance or inhibit religious belief or non-belief, nor discriminate between belief systems. Schools shall neither endorse nor interfere with religions. The district endorses the study of religion in an objective, respectful, and cross-cultural manner as integral to education.

NEUTRALITY
No religious belief or non-belief shall be promoted or disparaged by district or employees. The district encourages appreciation and respect for differing religious views. Students and staff may be excused from activities contrary to their religious beliefs when there are clear issues overriding concern that would prevent it, with alternative activities provided where appropriate.

TEACHING ABOUT RELIGION AND SCHOOL PROGRAMS
An education excluding religious references would be incomplete. Teaching must be about and not of religion in an open, objective, and respectful manner. The district supports inclusion of religious literature, music, drama, and arts when intrinsic to the learning experience and presented objectively. Religious themes may be included to enhance understanding that religion and diversity of beliefs are basic components of our cultural heritage, without fostering particular tenets or demeaning beliefs. School programs, performances, and celebrations must serve educational purposes. Religious content may be included if it has an independent education purpose which contributes to the stated objectives of approved curriculum, considering intent, effect, and timing.

STUDENT EXPRESSION OF RELIGIOUS BELIEFS
Students are free to express religious or non-religious beliefs in discussions, compositions, art, music, speech, and debate. No prayer, worship, or religious expression shall be prescribed or sanctioned, though this does not restrict spontaneous discussion about religion, personal prayer, or personal meditation that is non-disruptive and respects others' privacy. The district makes reasonable efforts to accommodate religious observances regarding required schoolwork and testing, with students responsible for advance notification and arranging make-ups. Students should be excused only to the extent that their ability to complete the educational program is not jeopardized.

PROCESS FOR DECISIONMAKING — PRINCIPLES FOR DECISIONMAKING
The Three-Part Test (from U.S. Supreme Court First Amendment jurisprudence) requires affirmative answers to: Purpose — is the activity educational? Effect — does it avoid promoting religion? Excessive Entanglement — does it avoid excessive relationships between schools and religious organizations? Decision makers must also determine consistency with policy intent respecting individual dignity and beliefs.

RESPONSIBILITY FOR DECISIONMAKING
Employees must ensure activities comply with policy. When specific religious content is included in lessons or activities, employees must seek counsel from immediate supervisors. Programs, performances, celebrations, classroom activities, visual displays, assemblies, sponsoring religious groups, and facility use for special programs require principal review before inclusion of religious content. Supervisors are responsible for verifying activities have been reviewed appropriately and meet the outlined tests.

TEACHING ABOUT RELIGION AND SCHOOL PROGRAMS — STANDARDS
Religious literature, music, drama, arts, and themes in social studies must comply with these regulations when included as significant elements achieving course objectives. Religious themes are defined as concepts which are identified with any religious traditions or tenet. Materials or activities must meet two criteria: positive answers to the three-part test, and determination that content is consistent with policy intent and curriculum objectives. Teachers must monitor material appearances and request principal review when questionable.

SCHOOL PROGRAMS AND DISPLAYS
To include religious music, symbols, art, or writings in programs, displays, performances, classroom activities, and celebrations, teachers must demonstrate an independent educational purpose consistent with the stated objectives of the approved curriculum. Prior review and regulation of content is necessary and appropriate given constitutional obligations. All relevant artistic, social, and cultural aspects should be considered. School programs means school-sponsored student performances or presentations to other classes, schools, parents, or the public. Religious content means music, objectives, symbols, art, readings, or writings that are identified with any religious tradition or which refer to any matter or religious concern.

PRIOR REVIEW PROCEDURES
Teachers may either confer with the principal to establish context and cooperative communication, or submit a written instructional plan including curricular objectives, specific religious content, educational purposes for that content, and program context. The principal applies the three-part test and exercises professional judgment on compliance and policy consistency. Special attention is given to participant and audience age/maturity, proximity to religious holidays, content diversity, overall program impression, and appropriate disclaimers. Within five school days, the principal responds in writing with approval or denial identifying noncompliance areas.

APPEAL PROCESS — FIRST LEVEL, INFORMAL DISCUSSION
The appealing party meets informally with immediate supervisor; decision made within two school days. The supervisor notifies the assistant superintendent of school services.

SECOND LEVEL
A written review request goes to the director of curriculum and instruction or designee. Both parties may present positions verbally or in writing. Decision made within five school days.

THIRD LEVEL
Either party may appeal to the assistant superintendent of school services or designee. A written request must be filed within five school days after the second-level decision, setting forth all disagreement reasons and including previous submissions. A written decision is provided within five school days. During the appeal process, the portion of the activity considered questionable shall not be practiced or performed.

No provisions regarding grade point averages, class ranking, graduation requirements, program placement, participation eligibility based on test scores, automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, or machine learning appear in this policy.


---

# Section J — Students

## JBB — Harassment or Discrimination of Students

POLICY STATEMENT

The district maintains a learning environment free from harassment based on protected class status. Such conduct by employees, volunteers, students, and third parties is prohibited.

DEFINITION OF HARASSMENT/DISCRIMINATION

Harassment means "unwelcome physical or verbal conduct or any written, pictorial, or visual communication" directed at a student because of their protected class membership, if objectively offensive to a reasonable individual in that class.

The policy notes that conduct need not be severe or pervasive to violate this policy if it:
- Becomes a condition for accessing educational services
- Influences educational decisions based on acceptance/rejection
- Unreasonably interferes with educational access or creates an intimidating environment

EVALUATION FACTORS

Determination relies on the totality of circumstances, including frequency, number of individuals involved, conduct type/nature, duration, location, threatening nature, power differentials, epithets/slurs, stereotyping, physical violence, and context-specific factors (racial slurs, religious comments, ethnic language, misgendering, disability-related mimicry).

Hate speech and symbols "reasonably expected to be divisive or demeaning" constitute harassment.

TITLE IX SEXUAL HARASSMENT

"Sexual harassment pursuant to Title IX" falls under separate investigation procedures in District Policy AC-R3.

REPORTING OBLIGATIONS

Students/guardians should report incidents per Regulations AC-R1 or AC-R3. Employees witnessing harassment "must take prompt and effective action to stop" it and report to administrators.

REMEDIAL ACTIONS & SPECIAL EDUCATION

The district must determine whether harassment affected FAPE (Free Appropriate Public Education) eligibility for students with IEPs or Section 504 Plans, and convene teams to assess educational impact and revise services accordingly.

The policy emphasizes staff training and regular compliance review.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this policy.

## JC — School Attendance Areas

OVERVIEW

Student attendance areas are determined by residence according to Colorado law, with the Board of Education responsible for approving all designations.

DETERMINATION OF ATTENDANCE AREAS

"A student's designated attendance area is determined by their residence, in accordance with Colorado law." This designation establishes the student's neighborhood school assignment.

AUTHORITY AND RECOMMENDATIONS

The superintendent recommends any proposed changes to attendance areas to the Board, potentially forming a committee to review areas beforehand based on geographic and enrollment data.

REVIEW AND ADJUSTMENT CRITERIA

The District regularly examines enrollment patterns and recommends boundary modifications as needed. When establishing or adjusting boundaries, decision-makers consider:
- "the densities of students in an area in relation to the relative capacities of the schools"
- Open enrollment and choice provisions
- Efficient transportation resource use

COMMUNITY ENGAGEMENT

"The District will provide for and obtain community and employee feedback on proposed boundary changes," with the Board receiving a summary of responses alongside recommendations.

DOCUMENT HISTORY

Adopted: May 22, 1995. Most recent Board revision: June 9, 2026 (effective July 1, 2026).

REFERENCES

Cross-references JFBA (Choice/Open Enrollment) and Colorado Revised Statutes sections 22-1-102, 22-32-110, and 22-36-101.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this policy.

## JEA — Compulsory Attendance

PRIMARY REQUIREMENT

Children who turn six by August 1st and haven't reached age 17 must attend public school, with legal exceptions available. Parents bear responsibility for ensuring their child's attendance. Colorado law defines "parent" as the biological mother or father, or any individual with legal custody.

GRADE RETENTION PROVISION

Parents whose child participated in preschool or kindergarten starting at ages five or six may request that the school withhold advancement to first grade. Schools must honor such requests and keep the student at their current grade level. The district may arrange a meeting to discuss "the benefits and harms of retention."

KEY REFERENCES

Policy Code: JEA. Related Policy: JH - Student Attendance/Truancy. Legal Basis: C.R.S. 22-33-104 (compulsory school attendance ages).

REVISION HISTORY

Most recently revised June 9, 2026 (effective July 1, 2026), with prior updates in 2008, 2007, 2004, 1997, and initial review in 1995.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this policy. Truancy enforcement procedures appear addressed under related policy JH.

## JEB — Entrance Age Requirements

KINDERGARTEN ENROLLMENT

"Children may enter kindergarten if they are five years old on or before October 1" of the enrollment year. The district accepts younger students transferring from public school kindergarten programs. Additionally, younger applicants "may be accepted if they are determined by the District to be highly advanced gifted children."

FIRST GRADE ENROLLMENT

Students seeking first grade admission must be "six years old on or before October 1 of the year of enrollment." Similar to kindergarten, younger students already enrolled in first grade at another public school are accepted. The district also permits younger applicants deemed "highly advanced gifted children."

AGE VERIFICATION

"A legal birth certificate or other acceptable records shall be required for enrollment age certification."

REVISION HISTORY

The policy was adopted in April 1972 and revised multiple times, with the most recent superintendent revision in October 2019.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this policy, beyond the discretionary district determination of "highly advanced gifted children" for early entrance.

## JFABB — Admission of Non-Immigrant Foreign Students

POLICY OVERVIEW

The district acknowledges the value of international exchange and permits admission of "a limited number of non-immigrant foreign exchange students" to its schools, but only through approved programs.

APPROVED PROGRAMS

Acceptable programs are those designated by the United States Information Agency. Applications are accepted exclusively from "CSIET certified J-1 Visa agencies and Rotary branches" under the national Rotary Youth Exchange International Program.

POLICY SCOPE

This policy addresses non-immigrant foreign students temporarily residing in the district without parents or guardians for educational purposes. It specifically covers students qualifying for J-1 visas under the Immigration and Naturalization Act. The policy excludes resident aliens, political exiles, and students residing with parents/guardians from other countries.

STUDENT STATUS AND DIPLOMAS

Exchange students are ineligible for high school diplomas but may receive "a certificate of completion" instead.

TUITION REQUIREMENTS

"Foreign students on a J-1 visa are not required by law to pay tuition."

ADMISSION AUTHORITY

The district maintains discretionary authority to deny admission to any applicant in compliance with applicable law.

No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this policy.

## JFABD — Homeless Students

POLICY PRIORITY

The district prioritizes "a safe and inclusive environment where all students and families are treated with dignity and respect." Students facing housing instability must receive equal educational access without segregation or stigmatization.

KEY DEFINITIONS

McKinney-Vento: Federal law "ensuring immediate enrollment, educational stability, and support services" for homeless children and youth.

McKinney-Vento Coordinator: District employee assigned to assist eligible students, fulfilling the role of homeless liaison required by state and federal law.

School of Origin: The school previously attended while permanently housed or last enrolled.

Student Experiencing Housing Instability: Individuals lacking "a fixed, regular, and adequate nighttime residence," including those sharing housing due to economic hardship, living in motels, shelters, abandoned buildings, cars, parks, or similar inadequate settings. Also covers preschool children, migratory children, and unaccompanied youth.

Unaccompanied Youth: A student experiencing housing instability "not in the physical custody of a parent or guardian."

COORDINATOR RESPONSIBILITIES

The coordinator identifies eligible students through outreach, ensures equal educational opportunity, facilitates access to eligible services, disseminates public notice of rights, provides staff training, supports unaccompanied youth enrollment, mediates school selection disputes, and assists with transportation arrangements.

ENROLLMENT STANDARDS

Students must be "enrolled immediately, even if the student lacks records routinely required prior to enrollment." Schools request records from previous schools but cannot delay enrollment pending their receipt.

ENROLLMENT DETERMINATION FACTORS

The coordinator consults with parents/guardians, unaccompanied youth, principals, transportation directors, and liaisons when determining appropriate school placement, considering the student's best interests, educational needs, achievement impact, family wishes, and transportation requirements.

ELIGIBILITY DURATION

Students retain McKinney-Vento status and services through the academic year they become permanently housed. The following school year, they lose eligibility but may continue attending their previous school through the district's choice/open enrollment process without requiring additional paperwork.
