Vision and hearing tests occur in specified grades. Parents may object on religious or personal grounds. The district must provide advance notice for non-emergency physical examinations.

BEHAVIOR TESTING

Staff cannot recommend psychotropic drugs or conduct behavior testing without parental written notice and permission.

ADOPTION/REVISIONS

Originally adopted April 1972; most recently revised June 9, 2026 (effective July 1, 2026).

## JLIB — STUDENT DISMISSAL PRECAUTIONS

A child may receive an exemption from school attendance in accordance with applicable law. Schools bear legal responsibility for student health and safety throughout the instructional day. Therefore, each school must establish procedures to authenticate early dismissal requests, ensuring students depart only for legitimate reasons and to appropriate individuals.

TEACHER AND PRINCIPAL AUTHORITY

Teachers cannot release any student before the school day concludes or to anyone's care without prior written approval from the building principal.

The principal cannot excuse students under 18 years old before day's end without a parental request for early dismissal. Following this requirement, these practices apply: (1) no student shall be released from school early on the basis of an invalidated telephone call; and (2) children of estranged parents shall be released only upon the request of the parent whom a Colorado court holds directly responsible for the child and who is the parent or guardian registered on the school record.

ELEMENTARY STUDENTS

Elementary students must depart only with their parent or, if unavailable, with an authorized adult representative.

Principals or designated representatives shall implement supplementary protective measures as circumstances warrant.

ADOPTION AND REVISION HISTORY

Current practice codified 1995. Adopted: May 22, 1995. Revised: January 22, 1996.

## JLIE — STUDENT VEHICLE USE AND PARKING

Students may park vehicles only in designated student lots, with vehicles remaining parked during class times unless the student is excused from school. Students must not congregate or loiter in parked cars or parking lots during the school day.

PRIVILEGE AND REVOCATION

Parking constitutes a revocable privilege subject to removal for irresponsible or dangerous vehicle use. This includes speeding, reckless maneuvers, or transporting passengers on the vehicle's exterior. Such conduct may result in suspension or expulsion.

SEARCH AUTHORIZATION

By bringing a vehicle to campus, students consent to searches when reasonable suspicion the search will yield evidence of illegal or unauthorized materials exists. Refusal by a student, parent/caregiver, or vehicle owner to allow a search results in privilege revocation without hearing or appeal rights and may constitute grounds for suspension or expulsion.

SCHOOL AUTHORITY

Schools may patrol student parking lots, visually inspect student motor vehicles, and use dogs trained to alert at the scent of drugs, explosives and other illegal or unauthorized materials. Principals retain authority to establish additional regulations as needed.

ADOPTION/REVISION HISTORY

Adopted February 1974; most recently revised by Board January 27, 2026, effective July 1, 2026.

CROSS-REFERENCES

JIH, JKD/JKE, JKD/JKE-R, JKDA/JKEA.

## JQ — STUDENT FEES, FINES AND CHARGES

The district prohibits charging fees as an enrollment or attendance condition for academic coursework, though textbook rentals, consumable materials, and miscellaneous fees are permitted per state law.

PERMITTED FEES

The policy allows the district to require payment for textbook fees, fees for expendable materials, fees for items students retain or consume, and other miscellaneous fees, along with voluntary enrichment activities and parking privileges.

FEE SCHEDULE REQUIREMENTS

All student fees shall be listed or described in a fee schedule adopted by the Board of Education, and must specify each fee's purpose and derivation.

TEXTBOOK RENTAL LIMITS

Rental charges must be based solely on the purchase price and normal life expectancy of each book rented.

EXTRACURRICULAR PARTICIPATION FEES

The district may charge participation fees for extracurricular activities, with fees for non-funded students not exceeding 150% of fees for fully-funded students.

INDIGENT STUDENT WAIVERS

Certain fees may be waived for indigent students, defined as those eligible for federal free or reduced-price lunch programs.

LOSS/DAMAGE PROVISIONS

The district may require deposits on textbooks and equipment, refundable upon return in good condition. Non-payment for lost or damaged items may result in exclusion from graduation ceremonies.

ADOPTION/REVISION HISTORY

April 1972 through June 2017.

LEGAL REFERENCES

C.R.S. 22-32-109(1)(u); 22-32-110(1)(o), (jj); 22-32-116.5; 22-32-117; 22-32-118; 22-45-104.

CROSS REFERENCE

Policy EFC (Free and Reduced-Price Food Services).

## JRA-JRC — STUDENT RECORDS/RELEASE OF INFORMATION ON STUDENTS

This policy governs student education records and information release, addressing parent/guardian rights, record access procedures, amendment processes, and third-party disclosure circumstances.

KEY DEFINITIONS AND SCOPE

Student education records include identifying data; academic work completed; level of achievement (grades, standardized achievement test scores); attendance data; and scores on standardized intelligence, aptitude, and psychological tests. Records maintained by law enforcement units are excluded from this policy's protections.

ACCESS RIGHTS

Parents/guardians may inspect student records. Students age 18+ (eligible students) may access their own records, though parents of tax dependents retain access rights.

Access Procedures: records must be examined in the presence of the principal or designee. Original records remain in District/school buildings. One copy is provided within a reasonable time at a cost not to exceed 25 cents per page. Test protocols and completed test instruments cannot be copied due to copyright/integrity concerns.

RECORD AMENDMENT PROCESS

Initial Request: written amendment requests go to the building principal within 10 school days of the date that the student records were first examined.

Appeal Levels: a principal denial may be appealed to the assistant superintendent (10 days); an assistant superintendent denial may be followed by a formal hearing request to the Superintendent (10 days).

Formal Hearing Standards: the hearing is conducted within 15 school days; the parent/student may be assisted or represented by an individual of their choice at their own expense, including an attorney.

Outcome Rights: parents/students may place explanatory statements in records; these statements must be disclosed whenever the record is shared.

DISCLOSURE WITHOUT CONSENT

Permitted to District Officials: disclosure is allowed to employees with a legitimate educational interest when necessary for job duties, within an official business context, relevant to student-related tasks.

Third-Party Recipients: other schools/districts where the student enrolls; federal/state education authorities; financial aid processors; accrediting organizations; researchers and study organizations; and juvenile justice officials (with confidentiality certification).

Emergency Exception: disclosure is permitted in connection with an emergency, if knowledge of the information disclosed is necessary to protect the health or safety of the student or other individuals.

DIRECTORY INFORMATION

Disclosable Without Consent: student name, photograph, audio/video recordings, major field of study, grade level, athletic participation, weight/height of athletes, attendance dates, honors/awards, and previous institutions attended.

Protected Directory Elements: telephone numbers and addresses require express written permission and cannot be released without written consent.

Opt-Out Deadline: parents must submit written refusal no later than September 1.

SPECIAL DISCLOSURE PROVISIONS

Military Recruiting: names, addresses, and home telephone numbers of secondary students will be released to military recruiting officers within ninety (90) days unless the student objects in writing.

Medicaid: directory information (name, date of birth, gender) is released to the Colorado Health Care Policy and Financing agency; non-directory information requires annual written consent.

Alumni Directories: may include name, activities, sports participation, attendance dates, degrees, awards, and addresses of former students; current students' contact information is protected.

ANNUAL NOTIFICATIONS AND COMPLAINTS

Districts must notify families annually of their rights. Complaints regarding Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act violations may be submitted to the Family Policy Compliance Office, U.S. Department of Education.

LEGAL AUTHORITY

20 U.S.C. 1232g (FERPA); 34 C.F.R. 99.1 et seq.; Colorado Revised Statutes 19-1-303/304, 22-32-109.1(6), 22-32-109.3, and 24-72-204(3)(d)&(e).

NOTE ON SCOPE

As extracted, this policy document contains no explicit provisions addressing automated systems, algorithms, or specific records retention/destruction timelines; retention and destruction of student records are governed separately under Policy EHB, as referenced in Policy JRCB below.

## JRCB — PRIVACY AND PROTECTION OF CONFIDENTIAL STUDENT RECORD INFORMATION

The district governs student record privacy through federal FERPA, Colorado's Student Data Transparency and Security Act, and related policies. "Confidential PII" refers to personally identifiable information within student education records.

KEY DEFINITIONS

Confidential Student Education Records comprise materials in any format that: (1) contain student-related information; (2) are maintained by district officials; and (3) are not classified as directory information.

Personally Identifiable Information includes data linked or linkable to a specific student enabling community identification, encompassing names, family member identifiers, addresses, social security numbers, student IDs, biometric records, and indirect identifiers like birth dates or maiden names.

Third Party means any entity or non-district employee.

AUTHORIZED ACCESS AND SHARING

Access to Confidential PII, and the collection and sharing of Confidential PII, is only authorized in accordance with governing law and District Policies CL and JRA/JRC.

ELECTRONIC DATA SECURITY STANDARDS

District computers, devices, email, and electronically stored data require password protection with complexity standards set by the information technology executive director. E-mail between District accounts shall be encrypted in transmission and at rest. Procedures enabling encryption between district and third-party accounts must exist. The operations executive director implements physical security, including building/data center access controls and video surveillance. The technology executive director implements access logging by device/location, penetration testing, vulnerability detection tools, breach response, and notification procedures. Compliance monitoring with policies EHA, GBEE, and JS is required. Staff must report suspected unauthorized access or data breaches.

ELECTRONIC DATA SECURITY AUDITS

Annual audits assess district equipment, software, and procedures protecting Confidential PII. The technology executive director submits confidential reports to the superintendent, with board distribution as directed.

DATA RETENTION AND DESTRUCTION

Records retention follows legal requirements and Policy EHB, with subsequent destruction per law and administrative procedures.

DISTRICT STAFF TRAINING

The district conducts periodic staff education on privacy obligations involving Confidential PII, including district technology, online services, and mobile applications.

SCHOOL SERVICE CONTRACT PROVIDER ACCOUNTABILITY

Contracts with school service contract providers committing a material breach involving misuse or unauthorized disclosure of Confidential PII face termination and future disqualification. Providers may request a hearing under Board Policy GP 3.12.

PARENT/GUARDIAN COMPLAINT PROCEDURES

Parents/guardians believing the district failed Colorado Act compliance may file written complaints with the superintendent within 30 calendar days of learning relevant facts.

Required complaint contents: (1) complainant and student contact information; (2) detailed event description with dates, times, and witness names; (3) involved district employee identification; (4) harm description; and (5) supporting documentation.

The superintendent or designee renders a written determination within 30 days, investigating if necessary. Unsatisfied complainants may appeal to the Board under Policy GP 3.12.

ADOPTION AND LEGAL REFERENCES

Adopted: October 2, 2017; Revised: October 16, 2017.

Legal Citations: 20 U.S.C. 1232g; 34 C.F.R. 99.1 et seq.; C.R.S. 22-16-101 et seq.

CROSS REFERENCES

CL, EHA, EHB, GBEE, JRA/JRC, JS.

## JS — STUDENT USE OF DISTRICT INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY

CORE AUTHORIZATION AND SUSPENSION

The district permits student use of its technology exclusively for education-related purposes. The district may suspend or terminate access at any time it is in the District's best interest and retains authority to adjust usage limits and parameters through its chief technology officer.

DEFINITIONS

District information technology encompasses computers, devices, provisioned software, email, curriculum resources, and internet access. A district technology device (DTD) is a District-purchased tablet, camera, recorder, hand-held device, computer, laptop, system, network, or associated peripheral with installed software. A personal technology device (PTD) is a privately-owned portable device including cell phones, tablets, laptops, GPS devices, cameras, wearables, and recorders. Academic dishonesty means engaging in a practice in relation to schoolwork that does not meet the requirements through undisclosed material misrepresentation. Plagiarism means representing that work that is not the original creation of the student's is the student's own; it constitutes a form of academic dishonesty.

DEVICE ACCESS AND INSURANCE

Students may receive DTDs conditioned on insurance charges, with exemptions for free/reduced lunch-eligible students. Intentional or reckless damage may result in access restrictions.

PRIVACY RIGHTS

Students possess no expectation of privacy when using District information technology. The district reserves the right to monitor, inspect, copy, review, isolate, store and/or remove (at any time and without notice) all usage, including internet communications. Student-created content remains student-authored, but all material and information accessed/received/created through District information technology remains the property of the District.

SECURITY REQUIREMENTS

Students must guard passwords carefully and disclose them only to parents/caregivers; avoid sharing credentials unless authorized by technology support personnel; lock or log off unattended devices accessing confidential information; and password-protect DTDs and PTDs used for district access.

EMAIL POLICY

Deleted emails remain accessible through the "deleted items" folder. The Information Technology Department may purge student email annually unless otherwise required by law or District policy.

INTERNET ACCESS

The district implements technology protection measures that block or filter internet material that is obscene, child pornography or otherwise harmful to minors. Teachers must instruct students on internet safety before allowing access. Students encountering inappropriate material must immediately back out of the site and notify a District employee.

HARDWARE AND SOFTWARE MODIFICATIONS

Students cannot connect hardware to district devices or modify or circumvent the operating conditions set by the Information Technology Department without express authorization.

ARTIFICIAL INTELLIGENCE

The district acknowledges AI may enhance learning. Students may use AI tools only when clearly stated in the assignment or specified by the teacher. Citations of AI use are required. Unauthorized AI use may constitute plagiarism and academic dishonesty.

Students must recognize that AI tools are prone to "hallucinations," false answers/information, or outdated, misleading and/or biased information, and should verify results using reliable sources.

Critical restriction: students should not upload or input any personal, confidential, proprietary, or sensitive information into any AI tool accessed through District information technology, including passwords, personal information, images, and financial account numbers.

PROHIBITED USES

Students cannot use district technology to generate, send, receive, or store communications containing: content threatening safety; sexually-oriented or pornographic material; profanity directed at persons or classifications; violence advocacy or unlawful acts; information about weapons or controlled substances; harassment, bullying, threats, defamation, or violence against persons; plagiarism or academic dishonesty; privacy violations or confidentiality breaches; impersonation or anonymous proxy transmission; unauthorized access to district systems; unlicensed software or data downloads; violations of federal, state, or local law; policy violations; or interference with district operations or educational opportunities.

CONSEQUENCES

Violations result in potential suspension, modification, or revocation of use privileges, detention, and suspension or expulsion from school.

ADOPTION AND REVISION DATES

Adopted: April 13, 2010 (effective July 1, 2010). Revised: June 12, 2012; April 28, 2015; May 28, 2019; June 9, 2026.

CROSS-REFERENCES

AC – Nondiscrimination/Equal Opportunity; EHA - District Information Technology; EHB - Records Retention; GBEE - Employee Use of District Information Technology; JICJ – Student Possession and Use of Personal Technology Devices; JKDA/JKEA - Grounds for Suspension/Expulsion; JRA/JRC - Student Records/Release of Information.

LEGAL REFERENCES

47 U.S.C. 254(h); C.R.S. 22-87-101 et seq. (Children's Internet Protection Act).

## JT — YOUTH SUICIDE PREVENTION

The policy establishes the District's commitment to suicide prevention. The District recognizes that the physical and mental health of the entire school community are integral components of student outcomes and acknowledges suicide as a leading cause of youth death. The policy emphasizes the school's role in creating a supportive environment and recognizes employee responsibility to follow protocols.

RESOURCE AVAILABILITY

Resources that support suicide prevention and emotional wellness efforts will be maintained on the District's website and made publicly available.

EMPLOYEE OBLIGATIONS

District employees must be equipped with practical skills and remain alert to warning signs. Those aware of students exhibiting suicidal thoughts must follow current District protocols, typically coordinating with mental health special services providers.

MENTAL HEALTH PROVIDER RESPONSIBILITIES

Mental health specialists should conduct suicide risk screenings, contact parents/caregivers, and share available resources within District and community settings, including collaboration with crisis resources while complying with Policy JRA/JRC regarding student records.

ADOPTION/REVISION INFORMATION

Adopted by Board: September 27, 2022. Revised by Board: January 27, 2026, effective July 1, 2026.

CROSS-REFERENCE

JRA/JRC – Student Records/Release of Information on Students.

# Section K — School-Community-Home Relations

## KBA — Title I Parent Involvement

PURPOSE
This policy governs how the district involves parents of Title I students in the planning, review, and improvement of Title I programs, consistent with federal Title I parent-involvement requirements.

INVOLVEMENT WITH TITLE I PLANNING
The district holds an annual meeting of the Title I Community-Parent Advisory Council, bringing together parent representatives from Title I schools, community members, Title I staff, and principals to discuss program plans and the use of Title I funds.

INVOLVEMENT IN SCHOOL REVIEW AND IMPROVEMENT
In each school receiving Title I funds, an effort is made to have a Title I parent serve as a member of that school's Accountability Committee. Parents who are not committee members may still provide input into the school improvement process by contacting the principal or by attending committee meetings.

DISTRICT SUPPORT FOR PARENT INVOLVEMENT
The district commits to providing coordination, technical assistance, and other support to Title I schools, including: recruitment and training of parent volunteers; provision of materials and training to help parents work more effectively with their children (including materials addressing the state's academic content and achievement standards and state/local assessments); assistance with translation of informational materials into languages families can understand; and fiscal assistance in carrying out parent-involvement activities.

PARENTAL INVOLVEMENT ACTIVITIES / COMMUNICATION
Schools must provide multiple opportunities for two-way, meaningful communication between staff and families, which may include parent-teacher conferences, email, phone contacts, home visits, and written communication provided in a format and, to the extent practicable, a language that parents can understand.

ANNUAL EVALUATION
The district conducts, with the involvement of parents, an annual evaluation of the content and effectiveness of this policy, led by the Assistant Director of English Language Acquisition and Federal Programs. The evaluation specifically seeks to identify barriers to greater participation by parents, with particular attention to parents who are economically disadvantaged, have disabilities, have limited English proficiency, have limited literacy, or are of any racial or ethnic minority background.

SCHOOL-LEVEL POLICIES AND COMPACTS
Individual Title I schools are required to develop their own written parent-involvement policies, including school-parent compacts that outline how parents, school staff, and students will share responsibility for improved student academic achievement.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools appears anywhere in this document.

## KBE-KJA — Support Organizations

PURPOSE AND DEFINITION
The district welcomes and encourages the involvement of "support organizations" — formally or informally organized groups of individuals that are not part of the district — that support district schools or specific school programs (e.g., PTAs/PTOs, booster clubs, foundations). These groups operate independently of the district but must operate in accordance with this policy.

COMPLIANCE REQUIREMENTS
Support organizations must comply with all applicable laws, their own association bylaws, and relevant district policies, including those governing construction/maintenance work on district property (Policy EC), use of district facilities (Policy KF), standards of conduct on district property (Policy KFA), advertising and sponsorship arrangements (Policy KHB), and distribution of materials (Policy KHC), as well as policies governing volunteers (Policy KJ). Failure to comply may result in the organization being prohibited from further association with district schools or programs.

GIFTS AND DONATIONS
All gifts and donations from support organizations and their members are subject to the following rules: support organization funds and other assets shall not be held, maintained, managed, or administered by the district or any of its schools or departments — the organization must maintain its own funds separately. Gifts and donations may be offered to the district either for use as the district determines in its discretion, or for limited purposes and/or subject to terms and conditions specified by the support organization. Gifts and donations accepted by the district become the property of the district and are maintained, accounted for, and used by the district as a whole, or by the appropriate school or department, in accordance with guidelines developed by the district controller and consistent with any specifications of the support organization or its contributing members. No district program or activity shall receive any gift or donation directly from a support organization — all such gifts must be routed through and accepted by the district itself. No district employee or volunteer shall receive any pecuniary compensation, fringe benefit, or other form of remuneration directly or indirectly from a support organization.

AUTHORIZATION AS A SUPPORT ORGANIZATION
To be recognized as an authorized support organization, a group must obtain and maintain principal approval and demonstrate compliance with applicable district policies. It must file its organizational documents (e.g., bylaws or articles) or, if informally organized, a mission statement signed by its leadership. It must report its officers to the district and notify the district of any changes in leadership.

FINANCIAL RECORDKEEPING
If a support organization receives or expends money, it must maintain written accounts documenting all receipts and expenditures, and must retain sales slips, receipts, and/or invoices supporting each expenditure. The district retains the right to inspect these financial records.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools appears anywhere in this document.

## KD — Public Information and Communications

PURPOSE
The Board views the residents of the district as having an interest in their schools as an extension of their homes, existing to perform a special function in the development of their children. On that basis, the Board commits to two goals: to keep the public informed about the policies, administrative operations, objectives, and educational programs of the schools; and to provide the means for furnishing full and accurate information — both favorable and unfavorable — together with interpretation and explanation of school plans and programs.

ROLE OF TEACHERS AND DIRECT COMMUNICATION
The Board places great importance on the role of the teacher as communicator and interpreter of the school program to parents and the general public, and recognizes that direct communication between school officials and the community is necessary and should be encouraged.

SUPERINTENDENT'S RESPONSIBILITY
The superintendent is directed to develop procedures and techniques for ensuring a continuous and free-flowing line of communication between district staff and the district's residents.

CROSS-REFERENCES
Related policies AEC and BEC; statutory citations include C.R.S. 22-2-117, 22-7-104(2), 22-35-109, and 22-53-207(5).

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools appears anywhere in this document. This is a short, high-level communications policy without a detailed complaint procedure.

## KDB — Public Inspection and Copying of District Records

PURPOSE
The district permits public inspection and copying of district records consistent with the Colorado Open Records Act (CORA), while protecting records that are confidential, privileged, or otherwise exempted from disclosure by law.

REQUEST SUBMISSION PROCEDURE
Requests should be submitted electronically by completing the online submission form accessible from the district's website. All record inspection and copying requests must be sufficiently specific to allow the district to efficiently identify the desired records with reasonable certainty — requestors are expected to include identifying details such as relevant employee names, applicable date ranges, and subject matter.

RESPONSE TIMELINE
The district is allowed three working days to respond to a request made under CORA, and will make every effort to respond within that period. If the district invokes the extension permitted under CORA, it receives an additional seven working days to respond (i.e., up to ten working days total). If a request is received after 4:30 p.m., it is considered received on the next working day. In calculating the response time, the day the request is received is not counted.

FEE SCHEDULE
The district may charge a fee of $33 per hour for all time spent in excess of one hour on: research and retrieval of requested records; conducting searches for requested records; inspecting records to segregate those that are not responsive, not public records, or are confidential and/or privileged; and the production and/or copying of voluminous records. For hard copies of district records in excess of 100 pages, the district charges a fee not to exceed 25 cents per page, unless actual copying costs exceed that amount, in which case actual cost is charged. Where a requested record results from computer output other than word processing, the copy fee is based on recovery of the district's actual costs of providing the electronic service and product, together with a reasonable portion of the costs associated with building and maintaining the information system.

RECORDS EXEMPT / PROTECTED FROM DISCLOSURE
The district is prohibited by law from disclosing certain confidential records, and other records are not subject to disclosure because they are privileged. Protected categories include, but are not limited to: private, personally identifying information about students and their families; district personnel records relating to employees — except that the following personnel-related records MAY be released: applications of past or current employees, employment agreements, any compensation including expense allowances and benefits, and any amount paid or benefit provided incident to termination of employment; proprietary information; specialized details of security arrangements or investigations; and other records required by federal or state law, regulation, or judicial decision to remain confidential or non-disclosable.

NO DUTY TO CREATE RECORDS OR MANIPULATE DATA
The district has no duty to create a record that does not exist, and has no obligation to manipulate electronic data to create one or more new records in response to a public request. If the district, in its discretion, chooses to manipulate data to generate such a record anyway, it may charge a reasonable fee not to exceed the actual cost of manipulating the data and generating the record.

DENIAL OF REQUESTS
If the district denies a request for access to records and the requestor asks for a written statement of the grounds for denial, the district will provide a written statement citing the law or regulation under which access was denied. Further recourse for a requestor is through the statutory CORA judicial-review mechanism referenced in cross-citations, not an internal district appeal board.

HARASSING OR DUPLICATIVE REQUESTS
The district is not required to respond to harassing or abusive communications. Multiple or repeated submissions seeking the same or overlapping records will be consolidated as permitted by this policy.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools appears anywhere in this document.

## KDE — Crisis Management and Prevention

PURPOSE AND PLAN MANDATE
The Board requires the superintendent to develop and implement a crisis management and prevention plan that must adhere to the National Incident Management System (NIMS). The plan must include written procedures for taking action and communicating with local law enforcement agencies, community emergency services, parents, students, and the media in the event of a crisis.

INCIDENT COMMAND SYSTEM
Within NIMS, the Incident Command System (ICS) is adopted as the standard framework used by all federal, state, and local emergency responders; adoption of this standard ensures that all responders use common language and processes when responding jointly to a crisis. The policy relies on the NIMS/ICS framework itself to structure the response rather than defining separate numbered crisis levels or phases.

PUBLIC INFORMATION OFFICER ROLE
The plan designates a Public Information Officer function responsible for: coordinating overall communication responses for students, parents, and the media; identifying and anticipating communication requirements; preparing communications tailored for specific groups as required; and establishing secure areas for the dissemination of information to the media and the public (i.e., a controlled media briefing area separate from the response scene).

NOTIFICATION / COORDINATION WITH OUTSIDE AGENCIES
The crisis plan must set out written procedures for taking action and communicating with local law enforcement agencies, community emergency services, parents, students, and the media in the event of a crisis, ensuring coordinated notification across these stakeholder groups rather than ad hoc communication.

STAFF TRAINING REQUIREMENTS
Staff training under the plan must enable staff to: recognize and effectively address student behavior and other indicators that signal possible violence or other impending crisis; know when to report such behavior/indicators to parents, other persons in the school community, and law enforcement; function with awareness of applicable district policies and guidelines concerning student discipline and student rights; practice physical security methods for themselves and others; teach and model nonviolent conflict-resolution techniques; foster moral reasoning and self-control in students' behavior; teach and model tolerance of others; and effectively respond to various types of crises.

AUTOMATED EXTERNAL DEFIBRILLATOR (AED) STANDARDS
The Medtronic LIFEPAK CR+ Automated External Defibrillator is the only AED the district shall purchase or accept, standardizing equipment district-wide. The Risk Management Department coordinates AED acquisitions. A designated individual at each site is responsible for conducting a visual inspection of the AED on a monthly basis, with documented results. Identified responders must receive training in cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR) and AED use through a course meeting nationally recognized standards consistent with Colorado requirements. AEDs must be appropriately functional for both pediatric and adult use.

POST-CRISIS PSYCHOLOGICAL SUPPORT
The plan calls for involving specialists in psychology as appropriate to manage debriefing and grieving of staff and students following a traumatic loss, coordinating mental-health response after an incident.

ADOPTION HISTORY
Originally adopted September 9, 1996; revised January 8, 2008, and June 17, 2013.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
The only "automated" reference in this document is the "automated external defibrillator" (AED) hardware, which is a medical device with an automated shock-advisory function, not an algorithmic/AI/ML/predictive decision system. No other mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools appears anywhere in this document.

## KEB — PUBLIC CONCERNS/COMPLAINTS ABOUT PERSONNEL

This policy addresses how the district handles concerns or complaints from the public about district personnel.

INITIAL NOTIFICATION

When a supervisor receives a concern or complaint about a staff member, the supervisor must notify the employee involved and other appropriate personnel.

INVESTIGATION AND RESOLUTION

Following an investigation, the supervisor and the employee shall agree upon a course of action to address the concern or complaint.

FURTHER ACTION

If additional steps beyond the initial resolution are required, approved personnel procedures shall be followed.

CROSS-REFERENCE

The policy cross-references policy GBJ, Personnel Records and Files, for handling of related personnel records.

ADOPTION HISTORY

Adopted April 1972; revised September 1973, August 1976, and April 28, 1997.

SCOPE NOTE

The policy text is brief and does not itself spell out a detailed step-by-step complaint procedure, a designated review body or decision-maker, specific timelines, appeal/grievance rights, confidentiality protections, or records-management protocols beyond the cross-reference noted above.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI NOTE

No automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools are mentioned anywhere in this policy document.

## KEC — Public Concerns/Complaints about Instructional Resources

SCOPE AND WHO MAY FILE
Any concerned District resident or District employee may request reconsideration of educational/instructional materials used in the schools. The policy channels objections to books, media, or other instructional resources through a defined, staged process rather than ad hoc removal or restriction.

INFORMAL RESOLUTION
When a complaint or concern about instructional resources is raised directly with the media specialist or a classroom teacher, the policy encourages an immediate dialogue between the teacher and the complainant in an effort to resolve the concern informally at that level, without escalation. If the complaint is lodged with someone other than the staff member directly responsible for the material, it is referred to the principal, who facilitates resolution with or without personally mediating, as circumstances indicate.

FORMAL COMPLAINT / RECONSIDERATION PROCEDURE
If the concern is not resolved informally, the complainant must fill out a written reconsideration form provided by the District. Filing this form triggers a formal hearing involving the complainant, the media specialist or classroom teacher whose material/decision is being challenged, the principal or other administrators, and other appropriate parties as circumstances warrant.

REVIEW COMMITTEE
Following the hearing, a review committee is convened. The person responsible for convening it shall select and chair a committee including appropriate representation of teachers, administrators, media specialists, and parents or other citizens — a deliberately cross-constituency committee mixing school staff with community/parent representation. The committee reviews the complaint and the challenged material.

DECISION AND TIMELINE
The committee must render its decision to the complainant in writing within 10 school days following the hearing — a hard, explicit timeline running from the hearing date, measured in school days rather than calendar days.

APPEAL
If the complainant is not satisfied with the committee's written decision, any further consideration of the matter requires arrangement with the superintendent, who makes the final determination. The superintendent serves as the final appellate authority within the administrative process.

EXCEPTION FOR PREVIOUSLY BOARD-APPROVED TEXTBOOKS
Textbooks or supplementary text materials already approved by the Board of Education are carved out of this complaint/reconsideration procedure. Complaints about those materials are instead referred to the appropriate instructional improvement committee — a separate, curriculum-governance body rather than the ad hoc reconsideration committee used for other instructional resources.

CROSS-REFERENCES
This policy is closely paired with its companion complaint form, KEC-E, which operationalizes the reconsideration form referenced above, and with KEF/KEF-E, which govern complaints specifically about teaching methods, activities, or presentations (as distinct from instructional resources/materials).

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools found in the retrieved text.

## KEC-E — Public Concerns/Complaints Form

PURPOSE AND FILING WINDOW
This is the standardized complaint intake form referenced by policy KEC (and used more generally for public concerns/complaints). The form states that it must be filed within 60 days of the incident — a hard limitations period measured from the date of the incident giving rise to the complaint.

FORM FIELDS AND STRUCTURE
The form requests, in order: (1) "School or site location of incident(s)" — a blank line for the complainant to identify where the events occurred; (2) "Date(s) of incident(s)" — a blank line for the specific date or dates; (3) "Description of your concern" — a substantial block (nine blank lines) for narrative description, with an instruction that the complainant should attach information where necessary and must sign their name on all attachments, ensuring supplementary documentation is authenticated as belonging to the complainant's submission; (4) "Outcome you are requesting" — three blank lines for the complainant to state the specific remedy or resolution sought, forcing articulation of desired relief rather than leaving it to administrative interpretation; (5) contact information fields: "Name," "Telephone number," and a two-line "Address" field, so the District can follow up with the complainant.

ADMINISTRATIVE RESPONSE SECTION
Below the complainant's portion, the form contains an administrative response block reading, in substance, "(Administrator) has reviewed your concern. The following action has been taken:" followed by four blank lines for the administrator to record the resolution/action taken, and fields for "Date" and "Administrator Signature" — creating a documented, signed record of how the complaint was resolved and by whom.

SUBMISSION / ROUTING
The completed form is directed to be returned to the Office of School Services, Johannsen Support Services Center, 2407 Laporte Avenue, Ft. Collins, CO 80521 — a specific central administrative office and physical address, rather than to the building level, for intake/logging purposes.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools found in the retrieved text.

## KEF — PUBLIC CONCERNS/COMPLAINTS ABOUT TEACHING (INCLUDING METHODS, ACTIVITIES, OR PRESENTATIONS)

This policy establishes a multi-step process for members of the public to raise concerns about teaching methods, activities, or presentations.

STEP ONE — INITIAL TEACHER CONFERENCE

Parents/guardians are encouraged to meet at a mutually agreed upon time with the appropriate teachers or other staff involved, to attempt to resolve the concern informally.

STEP TWO — PRINCIPAL CONFERENCE

If the concern is not resolved at the teacher level, the school principal shall hold a conference with the complainant, and a written record of that conference is distributed to all parties involved.

STEP THREE — SUBSEQUENT MEETINGS

The involved teacher attends any follow-up meetings; written minutes of these meetings are documented and shared with the parties.

STEP FOUR — FORMAL CHALLENGE PROCESS

If the complainant remains dissatisfied, the principal provides the complainant a copy of these procedures along with the Citizen's Challenge or Objection to Teaching Methods form, to initiate formal review by committee.

REVIEW COMMITTEE AND TIMELINE

The principal forwards the completed challenge form to the review committee chairman within 10 working days. Copies of the form are sent to the superintendent, the complainant, and the teacher. The resulting report is kept in the school file, and in the employee's personnel file when appropriate. The review committee provides a written recommendation within 15 working days from receiving the completed and signed challenge form.

PROCEDURAL PROTECTIONS

Both the principal and the complainant are given the opportunity to render an opinion on the appropriateness of the material at issue, using supporting evidence.

APPEAL RIGHTS

A party dissatisfied with the committee's recommendation may appeal to the superintendent. Subsequent challenges to the same material are to reference the previous decision unless there are significant differences in the challenge or significant new evidence.

REPRESENTATION

Any party may be represented by counsel at any step of this procedure.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI NOTE

No automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools are mentioned anywhere in this policy document.

## KEF-E — Public Concerns/Complaints about Teaching (form)

CONTENT
This document, despite its "-E" (exhibit/form) designation matching the pattern of KEC-E, is a single-page referral notice rather than a fillable complaint form. Its full substantive text reads, in essence: "KEF-E - PUBLIC CONCERNS/COMPLAINTS ABOUT TEACHING (INCLUDING METHODS, ACTIVITIES, OR PRESENTATIONS)" followed by the instruction: "For details about the Citizen's Challenge or Objection to Teaching Methods, Activities, or Presentations form, contact the instructional services division in the district's central administrative offices."

This implies a gatekeeping/intake step through central administration before a formal teaching-related complaint can be lodged in writing, in contrast to the self-contained KEC-E form used for instructional-resource complaints.

## KF — Use of District Facilities

PURPOSE
This policy governs the scheduling and use of Poudre School District facilities (buildings, grounds, and athletic fields) outside of their regular District educational use. Community use of District facilities does not constitute District endorsement of the using organization or its beliefs, purposes, or activities.

ADMINISTRATION
The Customer Support Center (CSC), operating under the direction of the facility services director, is responsible for administering facility scheduling, assessing and collecting fees, maintaining facility-use calendars, and handling related communications with District staff and community applicants.

SCHEDULING PROCEDURES
District activities must be scheduled through the CSC by June 30 preceding the fiscal year in which the activity will occur, or at minimum 10 days in advance of the activity if scheduled after that date. A designated District employee is responsible for ensuring compliance with the facility-use rules and for providing on-site supervision during District-scheduled activities.

Community (non-District) activities require at least 10 days' advance notice, and scheduling begins each fiscal year on July 1. Community applicants must satisfy several conditions before a permit will be issued, including: submitting an application through CSC procedures; designating a responsible contact person; providing proof of liability insurance; paying a damage deposit where required; and obtaining a signed use permit. The individual signing the permit, as an authorized representative of the requesting organization, personally assumes legal and financial responsibility for the activity and any resulting damage or liability.

PROHIBITED USES
District facilities may not be scheduled for personal or family use, including but not limited to parties, memorials, reunions, weddings, funerals, and receptions. Facilities may not be used for activities occurring on paid holiday weekends, except for CHSAA (Colorado High School Activities Association) events and outdoor, non-building uses. Facilities may not be used for any activity that advocates or teaches the overthrow of the government by force, violence, or unlawful means, or that promotes social or political change through violence or subversive doctrine.

ATHLETIC FIELD RESTRICTIONS
Community use of District athletic fields is not permitted during the period from November 1 through March 15 each year, to protect field conditions during the off-season/winter period.

FEES
Facility-use fees are organized into a tiered structure. The lowest tier applies to curricular/co-curricular District activities and public elections, which are exempt from fees entirely. An intermediate tier (approximately 12.5% of the full rental rate) applies to uses such as licensed summer child-care programs. Higher tiers (ranging from approximately 25% up to 100% of the full rate) apply based on the type of requesting organization (e.g., youth-serving nonprofit vs. community-based religious organization vs. government/political meeting) and whether the activity is exclusive to a limited membership or open to the general public.

LIABILITY AND INDEMNIFICATION
Community users are required to indemnify and hold the District harmless for claims, damages, or injuries arising from their use of District facilities, and to carry adequate liability insurance as a condition of the permit.

APPEALS
An applicant whose facility-use request is denied may appeal the denial first to the facility services director. If still denied, the applicant may further appeal to the superintendent, whose decision is final.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools found in the retrieved text.

## KFA — Public Conduct on District Property

PURPOSE
This policy establishes standards of conduct for all persons — not just students and staff — while on District property, in order to protect the safety, order, and educational mission of the District.

PROHIBITED CONDUCT
The policy identifies approximately twelve categories of prohibited conduct on District property, including: any statement or action that disrupts or threatens to disrupt District operations, or that otherwise creates a nuisance, safety hazard, or disruption; conduct that interferes with an employee's ability to perform his or her job duties, or with students' participation in educational activities; conduct that disrupts or interferes with Board of Education meetings or other official District proceedings; obstructing or impeding passageways, including driveways, parking areas, hallways, doorways, or building entrances/exits; damaging, defacing, or destroying District property, or threatening to do so; possessing a dangerous weapon on District property, except when possessed by authorized law enforcement personnel; violating any applicable federal, state, or local law, or any District policy, rule, or regulation while on District property; and failing or refusing to leave District grounds or facilities when directed to do so by a District administrator, employee, or other official with authority to make such a request.

ENFORCEMENT
Any individual who violates this policy is subject to removal from District property and may be subject to criminal prosecution under applicable law (including trespass statutes). District officials are authorized to proactively exclude a person from entering District property if the official reasonably believes that the person will engage in conduct prohibited by this policy.

CROSS-REFERENCES
The policy cross-references Colorado Revised Statutes provisions relating to trespass, weapons possession, and controlled-substance regulation, and cross-references related District policies covering tobacco/marijuana use, employee conduct involving substances, student weapons conduct, use of District facilities (KF), and visitors to schools (KI).

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools found in the retrieved text.

## KHB — District Revenue through Advertising

PURPOSE AND SCOPE
Poudre School District permits revenue-generating advertising from non-District organizations as a means of supplementing funding for District operations and programs. The superintendent (or designee) holds final authority to interpret this policy.

DEFINITION
"Revenue advertising" is defined broadly to include printed materials, banners, signs, and audio or video communications that promote non-District businesses, products, activities, or causes, where the promotion generates revenue or an in-kind benefit for the District. This definition explicitly includes sponsorships, fundraisers, endorsements, and exclusive-provider contracts.

GOVERNING STANDARDS
All advertising accepted by the District must conform to standards of community taste and, where possible, should encourage or support student achievement. The District will not endorse a non-District entity, its products, or its services without specific Board of Education approval. Any use of the District's name, logos, or mascots by an outside party requires prior written authorization from the District. Non-District organizations are restricted from directly marketing to District employees, students, or families unless such marketing has been specifically approved. Advertising placed within classrooms or tied to curriculum is prohibited unless specifically authorized by the superintendent or an appropriate director.

APPROVAL AUTHORITY
Building principals are authorized to approve advertising at the individual school/site level. District-wide advertising is approved by the director of communications. Both site-level and District-wide advertising arrangements require additional approval from the purchasing manager. All advertising agreements must be in writing and are limited to a one-year term, or otherwise must be subject to cancellation by the District on an annual basis, unless a longer term is specifically approved by the Board.

REVENUE HANDLING
Revenue generated from school-level (site-specific) advertising is directed to the discretion of the building principal. Revenue generated from District-wide advertising arrangements and from scoreboard-related advertising is determined and allocated by the Board of Education. The policy calls for revenue and space-allocation guidelines that ensure equitable access to limited advertising space/opportunities among interested advertisers.

PROHIBITED ADVERTISING CONTENT
Advertising is prohibited if it relates to, depicts, or promotes: drugs, alcohol, or firearms; political organizations or religious organizations; ballot issues or election-related matters; unlawful conduct; content that would disrupt District operations; or situations that would create a conflict of interest for a District employee or Board member.

APPROVED VENUES/FORMATS
Advertising is permitted in specifically approved formats and locations, including: concession stands; vending machines; school publications; athletic event game programs; the District's Youth Activity Guide; fundraiser-related websites; Channel 10 (District cable channel), limited to a maximum of 30 seconds per advertisement, up to six airings per hour; cafeteria/facility signage limited to a maximum size of 2 feet by 3 feet; gymnasium banners; and scoreboard advertising — all subject to further guidelines to be developed by the District.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools found in the retrieved text.

## KHC — DISTRIBUTION/POSTING OF NON-DISTRICT COMMUNICATIONS

This policy governs how non-district communications and materials may be distributed or posted in connection with the district.

PERMITTED MATERIALS — PRINTED ADVERTISING FLIERS

Printed advertising fliers from non-district entities are limited to three times each school year, and are restricted to fliers advertising structured and supervised athletic, cultural, and academic programs for students. A nominal fee may be charged for this distribution.

PERMITTED MATERIALS — EMPLOYEE-FOCUSED POSTINGS

Two categories of postings are permitted on designated district websites, subject to guidelines set by the communications director: commercial advertising offering discounts to employees, and postings of goods and services available to, or sought by, employees.

PERMITTED MATERIALS — PHYSICAL POSTINGS

Site administrators may display advertising and other promotional notices, pamphlets, and fliers on bulletin boards and displays located in common areas, with discretion left to the site administrator regarding timing and the nature of activities advertised.

REVENUE ADVERTISING

Advertising conducted for revenue purposes is permitted under a separate policy, KHB.

REQUIRED DISCLAIMER

All non-district materials distributed or posted under this policy must include a statement that the district provides them only as a public service and is neither recommending nor endorsing the content.

PROHIBITED COMMUNICATIONS

The policy explicitly forbids materials that are inconsistent with the district's educational values; content concerning drugs, alcohol, or firearms; obscene or defamatory communications; materials promoting or opposing religion; content portraying unlawful conduct or violations of district policy; materials promoting disruptive conduct; and communications that would create a conflict between an employee's job responsibilities and private interests.

EXCEPTIONS

District-sponsored curriculum materials and communications from district support organizations are excluded from these restrictions.

ADOPTION/REVISION HISTORY

Adopted October 28, 1996; revised October 1, 2012; December 10, 2012; and May 12, 2014.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI NOTE

No automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools are mentioned anywhere in this policy document.

## KI — Visitors to Schools

PURPOSE AND DEFINITIONS
This policy establishes guidelines governing all visitors to District schools. A "visitor" is defined as any person who is not a member of the student body and who is not a member of the regular school staff, who enters onto school grounds or into a school building. Visitation by non-employees is characterized as a privilege, not a right, which may be limited, denied, or revoked based on considerations of safety, the orderly operation of the school, protection of the educational environment, or violation of District policy.

NONCOMPLIANCE CONSEQUENCES
Failure to comply with this policy may result in denial or withdrawal of a visitor's authorization to visit the school and/or referral of the matter to law enforcement.

CLASSROOM OBSERVATION RULES
Classroom or instructional-area observation is limited to specific categories of individuals: the parent(s)/guardian(s) of a student in the classroom or area being visited; relatives of a student in the classroom or area being visited; and other visitors specifically authorized by the student's parent(s)/guardian(s), where such observation is reasonably necessary for the benefit of the student.

LIMITS ON OBSERVATIONS
No more than three observers may be present in a classroom or area at one time, unless otherwise approved. Observers may not interfere with ongoing educational activities. Observation privileges are limited in aggregate to one day per week.

ENTRY AND CHECK-IN PROCEDURES
All visitors must enter the building only through designated doors and must report directly to the school office immediately upon entering. Visitors must state the purpose of their visit and may be required to provide identification to verify their identity. Once authorized, visitors may be required to sign in and out, wear a visible identification badge for the duration of their visit, and/or be accompanied by a District employee while on school premises.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, predictive tools, visitor-management software, or background-check screening technology was found anywhere in this policy's text.

## KJ — Volunteers

PURPOSE
Poudre School District R-1 invites community members to volunteer, stating that authorized volunteers enrich the District's educational programs, enhance supervision, and contribute to school safety.

DEFINITIONS
A "volunteer" is a person who provides unpaid service to the District and who may have contact with students outside the direct supervision of a District employee. An "authorized volunteer" is one who has completed registration and complies with all District policy requirements applicable to volunteers.

REGISTRATION AND APPLICATION
Individuals wishing to volunteer must complete a volunteer application and agreement form, available online through the District website or through the Partnership and Volunteer Center or the building's volunteer coordinator.

BACKGROUND CHECK / SCREENING
A background check shall be conducted by the District, at its own expense, as part of the volunteer application review process. Application information and background check results are maintained as confidential personnel records under Colorado law.

APPROVAL / DENIAL PROCESS
The District may deny a person the opportunity to volunteer if it determines that volunteer service by that person would be incompatible with the welfare or safety of students. A criminal conviction will not automatically result in denial of volunteer status — each case is given individual consideration on its own facts. An applicant denied volunteer status may appeal, with the executive director of human resources making the final determination.

IDENTIFICATION
Approved/authorized volunteers must be issued identification badges, which are required to be worn/displayed during all volunteer service.

FOLLOW-UP / PERIODIC RE-SCREENING
Registered volunteers are subject to follow-up background checks when circumstances warrant, and, at minimum, at least one random background check every three years.

DUTIES AND SUPERVISION
Building principals are responsible for assigning appropriate volunteer duties/services and for providing volunteers with necessary training. Volunteers must comply with all District policies and applicable school rules while performing service.

LEGAL PROTECTIONS
Authorized volunteers are afforded protections under Colorado's Governmental Immunity Act and the Teacher/Administrator Protection Act.

CROSS-REFERENCES
This policy is implemented through the accompanying regulation KJ-R.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this policy.

## KJ-R — Volunteers

PURPOSE / SCOPE
This regulation implements Board Policy KJ (Volunteers) and sets out detailed operational procedures for volunteer registration, screening, supervision, and site-level administration.

PARTNERSHIP AND VOLUNTEER CENTER
The District's Partnership and Volunteer Center is responsible for maintaining the online volunteer application system via the District website, through which registration is mandatory for all volunteers. The Center coordinates distribution of approved volunteers to individual school sites, maintains confidential volunteer files, provides training, issues identification badges, and conducts follow-up background checks.

BACKGROUND CHECK / SCREENING PROCEDURE
All applicants undergo a background check performed through a contractor approved by the executive director of human resources. For applicants who have resided out-of-state, the contractor is additionally required to utilize one or more national criminal databases as part of the screening.

DISQUALIFYING / ESCALATION FACTORS
The Partnership and Volunteer Center must immediately escalate for further review any case involving: a felony conviction; two or more DUI convictions; a domestic violence conviction; a conviction for child abuse or reckless endangerment; an outstanding warrant; a current criminal charge with a pending court date; a conviction for illegal sale of drugs; a conviction for unlawful sexual behavior; or any other information suggesting that the applicant's volunteer service may be incompatible with the protection of student health, welfare, safety, or morals. "Conviction" is defined broadly to include a verdict of guilty by judge or jury, forfeiture of bail, payment of a fine, a plea of nolo contendere (no contest), and a deferred or suspended sentence.

PRINCIPAL / SITE ADMINISTRATOR RESPONSIBILITIES
Building principals must require online registration of all volunteers at their site, may permit only volunteers who have a completed application and an approved/cleared background check to serve, must ensure that all volunteers wear their identification badge while on site, and must respond immediately to any staff concerns raised about a volunteer.

SITE VOLUNTEER COORDINATOR RESPONSIBILITIES
Each site's volunteer coordinator is responsible for recruiting volunteers, managing the online registration process at the site level, conducting volunteer orientations, submitting monthly reports on volunteer activity, monitoring the quality of the volunteer program, and establishing and maintaining a check-in system for all volunteers entering the site — this check-in system must include providing each volunteer with a mandatory identification badge upon entry.

FOLLOW-UP / RANDOM RE-SCREENING PROCEDURE
Volunteers who fail to update their profile by July 1 of a given year are treated as inactive and receive a final notice with a two-week window to respond before removal from active status. Active volunteers are subject to quarterly random background checks, targeting approximately 10% of the active volunteer roster each quarter, in addition to a comprehensive re-screening of all active volunteers at least once every three years.

CROSS-REFERENCES
This regulation directly implements and operationalizes Board Policy KJ.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this regulation. The background-check "contractor" and "national criminal databases" are named, but no automated scoring, AI, or algorithmic risk-assessment tool is described.

## KLB — Relations with Election Authorities

POLICY STATEMENT / PURPOSE
The Board authorizes high school principals, or their designees, to serve as deputy registrars for the limited purpose of conducting voter registration activities.

ELIGIBLE REGISTRANTS
Voter registration services under this policy may be provided to students, District employees, persons attending school functions, or any other person who is otherwise eligible to vote.

FACILITY ACCESS FOR REGISTRATION
Voter registration services may be conducted at District school buildings at any time the buildings are open for either educational activities or community/public use, consistent with applicable state election law.

ADMINISTRATIVE HISTORY
The policy was adopted May 22, 1995, codifying existing District practice, and was reviewed October 28, 1996. It is grounded in C.R.S. 1-2-401 et seq.

AI/AUTOMATED SYSTEMS
No mention of automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools was found in this policy. The policy is brief and confined to the deputy-registrar/voter-registration-access provisions described above.

## KLG — RELATIONS WITH STATE AND FEDERAL AGENCIES TO ENHANCE THE SAFETY AND SECURITY OF STUDENTS, EMPLOYEES, AND THE COMMUNITY

The policy sets out the district's approach to interacting with state and federal agencies, including immigration enforcement, in a manner intended to protect students, employees, and the community.

PRIMARY OBJECTIVES

The policy establishes four main goals: protecting civil rights and immigration status of students, families, and staff; developing crisis and safety plans; assessing security policies; and establishing protocols for contacting outside agencies.

ACCESS TO FACILITIES

Access to district schools and other buildings for all visitors, including federal immigration enforcement agents, is governed by district Policy KI, Visitors to School.

INFORMATION COLLECTION RESTRICTIONS

The district prohibits collecting immigration or citizenship status information except as necessary to verify information as required by state and/or federal law, or as necessary to determine eligibility for a government-funded program. The policy states that the district will not inquire into, or request information or documents to ascertain, a person's immigration status.

STUDENT RECORDS PROTECTION

Student education records require prior written consent from the student's parent/caregiver before disclosure, subject to limited statutory exceptions. Records are shared with immigration officials only if required by law, or with the permission of the student's parent/caregiver.

DESIGNATED AUTHORITY

The district's general counsel is the designated employee responsible for serving as the point of contact during visits by immigration officials and for responding to related information requests.

DISCIPLINARY MEASURES

Employees who violate this policy are subject to discipline, up to and including dismissal.

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI NOTE

No automated decision systems, algorithms, artificial intelligence, machine learning, scoring, or predictive tools are mentioned anywhere in this policy document.

# Section L — Education Agency Relations

## LB — Relations with Other Schools and School Systems

COOPERATION MANDATE
Poudre School District will "cooperate whenever possible with other school districts, with institutions of higher education, with boards of cooperative services, and with other local, state, and regional agencies."

COOPERATION AREAS
Cooperation areas include "joint educational services, service provider for other districts, research, exchange of data and information, coordination of curriculum, coordination of school activities and calendars, and cooperative use of school facilities."

STUDENT INTEREST PRIORITY
"In all instances, the interests of the district's students must be the priority."

Adopted May 22, 1995; revised August 11, 1997. Legal reference: C.R.S. 22-32-122.

## LBD — Charter Schools

GOVERNING FRAMEWORK
"Poudre School District charter applications and charter schools are governed by the Colorado Charter Schools Act and this policy."

CHARTER APPLICATION CONTENTS AND STANDARDS
Charter applications must satisfy requirements in Colorado Revised Statutes § 22-30.5-106(1) plus additional District requirements: (1) "Aggregate information concerning the grade levels and schools in which the proposed charter school's prospective students are currently enrolled"; (2) two budgets for each fiscal year of the requested charter term—one based on reasonably anticipated enrollment and one based on the minimum enrollment allowing continued economically viable operation; (3) facility planning details including indoor/outdoor space amounts, space utilization plans, facility readiness timelines, zoning/permitting considerations, lease/purchase status, and cost projections. Applicants should consult "the District's Charter Application Review Handbook." Substantial post-filing changes may restart the application timeline.

CHARTER APPLICATION PROCEDURES — PRE-FILING NOTIFICATION
Applicants must submit a letter to the District's charter school liaison "no later than thirty (30) days prior to filing a charter application" with a brief school description and intended filing date.

CHARTER APPLICATION PROCEDURES — FILING DEADLINE
"Except in unusual circumstances expressly approved by the Board of Education, new charter schools may open only at the beginning of a school year." The original application plus fifteen copies must be filed "on or before 4:00 p.m. on August 15 of the year preceding the school year of requested opening," or the first business day after if August 15 falls on a weekend/holiday.

CHARTER APPLICATION PROCEDURES — COMPLETENESS REVIEW
"Within fifteen (15) days after the charter application is filed with the charter school liaison, the District administration will review it to determine whether it is complete." If incomplete, the District specifies deficiencies in writing. Applicants have "fifteen (15) days after receiving the District administration's written list of deficiencies" to correct them.

CHARTER APPLICATION PROCEDURES — BOARD PRESENTATION
"The Board shall receive the charter application at its next regularly scheduled meeting after the District administration has determined that it was timely filed and is complete."

EVALUATION — APPLICATION REVIEW COMMITTEE
An "application review committee comprised of members of the District Accountability Committee, including at least: (a) one person with a demonstrated knowledge of charter schools, regardless of whether that person resides within the District; and (b) one parent or legal guardian of a child enrolled in a charter school in the District." Representatives from existing charter schools are invited to participate. The committee prepares an insight memorandum for the Board's consideration.

EVALUATION — SUBJECT MATTER EXPERT REVIEW
"The charter application shall be evaluated by District employees who are subject matter experts in the areas of: (a) budget; (b) facilities and operations; (c) risk management and insurance; (d) human resources; (e) students with special needs; and (f) curriculum, instruction and assessment." A separate insight memorandum is prepared from each expert perspective for the Board's consideration.

EVALUATION — APPLICANT RESPONSE OPPORTUNITY
Applicants receive copies of insight memoranda and may provide additional documents/information responding to them, submitted "at least fourteen (14) days prior to the date scheduled for the Board hearing" unless otherwise specified.

EVALUATION — BOARD HEARING
"The Board shall hold a hearing on the charter application prior to taking action thereon." Copies of insight memoranda and the applicant's additional materials are provided to each Board member prior to the hearing.

EVALUATION — EVALUATION STANDARDS
"In evaluating the charter application, the Board and administration shall consider the standards specified in the District's Charter Application Review Handbook."

DECISION TIMELINE
"The Board shall take action on the charter application within ninety (90) days after it is received by the District, except as may otherwise be provided by law."

ANNUAL REVIEW OF CHARTER SCHOOL PERFORMANCE
"The District shall review the performance of each charter school on an annual basis during the term of its charter. The review shall include: (a) the charter school's progress in meeting the objectives identified in its unified improvement plan; (b) the charter school's most recent annual financial audit; and (c) the charter school's compliance with the terms of its charter school contract. The District shall provide the charter school with written feedback regarding any concerns raised as a result of its review."

CHARTER RENEWAL
Governing bodies seeking renewal must submit a letter to the Board "no later than December 1 of the year in which the charter is due to expire," specifying the renewal term and conditions requested, together with a written report on progress achieving goals, objectives and pupil performance standards. The Board considers renewal information plus annual review data and Colorado student assessment results.

RENEWAL DECISION TIMELINE
"The Board of Education shall rule by resolution on the charter school's renewal request no later than February 1 of the year in which the charter is due to expire." At least fifteen days prior to the renewal/revocation determination, the superintendent must provide the Board and the charter school a written recommendation with supporting reasons.

REVOCATION GROUNDS
"The Board may revoke or decline to renew a school's charter for any one or more of the reasons specified in C.R.S. § 22-30.5-110."

CHARTER SCHOOL CLOSURE
"The District shall attempt to work with a charter school to coordinate the winding up of its operations in an orderly fashion as provided in its charter school contract in the event of the school's closing for any reason." The District works with parents of enrolled students to help ensure orderly transition to another District school per Policy JFBA (Choice/Open Enrollment). "If it is practicable, economically feasible for the District and in the best interest of the charter school students, the District shall allow the charter school to continue operating through the end of the school year following a revocation or nonrenewal of its charter."

AUTOMATED SYSTEMS / AI
No mention found in this policy document.

NONDISCRIMINATION / DISABILITY
The document does not contain explicit nondiscrimination language. Subject matter experts specifically include evaluation of "students with special needs" in charter applications, indicating disability consideration during approval processes.

ACCOUNTABILITY
Accountability mechanisms are embedded throughout: annual performance reviews against unified improvement plan objectives; financial audit review requirements; charter contract compliance monitoring; student assessment data review via the Colorado student assessment program; written feedback provision regarding review concerns; renewal contingent on goal/objective achievement and pupil performance.

Adopted April 22, 2002; revised August 9, 2004; August 23, 2011; May 28, 2013. Legal reference: C.R.S. 22-30.5-101, et seq. (Colorado Charter Schools Act).
